# Changelog

All notable changes to OneStreamer will be documented in this file.

The format is based on [Keep a Changelog](https://keepachangelog.com/en/1.1.0/),
and this project adheres to [Semantic Versioning](https://semver.org/spec/v2.0.0.html).

## [Unreleased]

### Fixed
- **VisionBot live-pipeline reliability bundle (7 services).** A cluster of interrelated fixes to the VisionBot → transcription → egress-recording → frame-capture pipeline, found while running the feature on the live install. Bundled because each downstream stage depends on the one before it. **(1) Zombie LiveKit egress / silent dataloss (`ContinuousRecordingService.js`)**: stopped *adopting* an existing "active" egress on startup/restart. LiveKit's `status==active` includes zombies — egress worker dead, session table not updated (one was stuck active for 3+ weeks). Adopting one left `isRecording=true` with nothing written to disk, so frame-capture / clip-extraction / vision-bot all silently no-op'd. Now force-stops all active egresses on startup and recreates; the ~5 s gap on a real restart is cheap vs. days of dataloss. **(2) ffmpeg 7.x frame extraction (`EgressFrameCaptureService.js`)**: removed `-sseof` (ffmpeg 7 exits non-zero seeking from the end of a short HLS `.ts` segment with B-frames) and added `-pix_fmt yuvj420p` (the egress encoder emits limited-range YUV that ffmpeg 7's mjpeg encoder rejects as "non-standard"). Frame capture was returning nothing on the upgraded host. **(3) Transcription `once()` deadlock (`TranscriptionDrivenBotService.js`)**: replaced `transcriptionService.once('transcription-stopped', …)` + sessionId filter with `on()` + manual `off()` that fires only on a matching sessionId, plus a `duration×4` safety timer. `once()` consumed the listener on the *first* emitted stop event regardless of sessionId; during stream rotations a stale session's stop fired first, the listener was gone, the real session's stop had no listener, and `scheduleNextTranscription` never ran — both MovieBot and VisionBot stalled until restart. **(4) Dropped ffmpeg stderr (`ViewBotURLService.js`)**: pino drops a bare-string 2nd arg to `logger.error()`, so every `❌ FFmpeg error for X:` line was logging with no payload. Switched to structured `logger.error({ stderr }, '…')` / `{ err }` form so the diagnostics actually land in the JSON record. **(5) VisionBot cadence + over-strict guard (`VisionBotService.js`)**: added a `transcription_frequency_s` throttle at the top of `_runCycle` (with MovieBot also enabled, bus events fired every ~50 s and the admin frequency knob was decorative); added a `throttled` skip reason. Removed the `streamerId` guard that rejected every bus event when MovieBot/VisionBot ran under different identifiers for the same physical stream — takeover safety is enforced downstream via `streamGeneration`. **(6) Vision-comment quality (`ChatBotLLMService.js`)**: strip wrapping quotation marks the model adds despite instruction (ASCII + smart quotes + back-ticks; only strips matched pairs so a leading apostrophe in `'sup chat` survives); rewrote the vision prompt to "react as a chatter — short, casual, never describe what's on screen". **(7) VisionBot double-post (`ChatBotService.js`)**: skip the regular `response_interval` chat timer for a bot with `vision_bot_enabled`, so it drives chat solely off transcription windows (one post per window, not two). **Tests**: 3 unit tests updated to lock in the intentional behavior changes — `EgressFrameCaptureService.test.js` (asserts `-pix_fmt` present + `-sseof` absent), `VisionBotService.test.js` (the streamerId-mismatch test now asserts the event *is* processed; the dedup test advances past the new throttle window so it exercises the sessionId-dedup path specifically). All 4 VisionBot-pipeline suites green (62/62); the `ContinuousRecordingService.cleanup-race` + `ViewBotURLService.whitelist-gate` suites unchanged (19/19). Module-load smoke: `LOAD OK`. **Risk**: MEDIUM — production-validated changes (the comments cite real incidents), but the test surface for these 4 files is in the default-exclude list, so coverage is unit-level only; the live SIGTERM/restart + VisionBot-with-MovieBot smoke is the maintainer's gate.

### Changed
- **Extract `RotationScheduler` from `RandomStreamRotationService` (PR 17.3, Phase 17).** Third PR of Phase 17. Lifts the rotation-timer / countdown-announcement-timers / next-rotation-bookkeeping cluster out of the main service into a new `server/services/random-stream/RotationScheduler.js` (233 LoC). **State moves**: `rotationTimer`, `countdownAnnouncementTimers`, `nextRotationAt`, `currentRotationDuration` now live on `this._scheduler.*`. The main service re-exposes each via property getter/setter accessors so consumer call-sites (`extendRotation`, `reduceRotation`, `adminExtend`, `adminReduce`, `lockRotation`, `unlockRotation`, `forceRotate`, `stop`, `pause`, `setViewBotURLService` event handler, `_startAutoRestartMonitor`, `getStatus`) keep reading and writing `this.rotationTimer = null` / `this.nextRotationAt - Date.now()` / etc. unchanged — getter routes through to the scheduler slot, setter writes back. Single source of truth, no shadow field. **Method moves** (six methods, ~210 LoC of behaviour): `_scheduleNextRotation` → `scheduler.scheduleNext`, `_emitRotationTiming` → `scheduler.emitRotationTiming`, `_emitFullRotationStatus` → `scheduler.emitFullRotationStatus`, `_clearCountdownAnnouncements` → `scheduler.clearCountdownAnnouncements`, `_scheduleCountdownAnnouncements` → `scheduler.scheduleCountdownAnnouncements`, `_executeRotationWithRetry` → `scheduler.executeRotationWithRetry`. Six 1-line delegate methods on the main class preserve the underscored names. **Re-entry via host (critical for stub-compat)**: when the scheduler's internal `setTimeout` callback needs to call back into "execute rotation with retry" / "schedule next" / "emit timing" / "schedule countdowns" / "emit full status", it routes through `host._scheduleNextRotation()` etc. instead of calling `this.scheduleNext()` directly on the scheduler. This preserves the pre-PR callsite contract — tests that stub `svc._executeRotationWithRetry = jest.fn()` still intercept the timer callback. Without this routing the byte-equivalence proof from PR 17.2's scheduling test suite (28 cases) would have failed; with it, all 28 stay green. **Cross-service collaboration**: scheduler reads `host.isEnabled` / `host.isLocked` / `host.isRestarting` / `host.io` / `host.currentStream` / `host.retryState.consecutiveFailures` / `host.retryState.currentRetryTimer` / `host.getRandomInterval()` / `host.sendChatAnnouncement()` / `host._rotateToNewStream()` / `host._recordSuccess()` / `host._recordFailure()` / `host._scheduleRetryWithBackoff()`. All read via the `host` ref captured at construction; no global lookups. **Setter-on-property semantics**: defining the four accessors as class-syntax getters/setters means they live on the prototype, so `this.rotationTimer = null` in the constructor's preceding initialization no longer fires (those lines are removed in the PR). Subsequent assignments correctly route through the setter. **New unit tests** (`server/tests/services/random-stream/RotationScheduler.test.js`, 27 cases, 93%+ line coverage on the scheduler): `scheduleNext` (interval/default-fallback/overwrite/callback-fires/isEnabled-bailout/isLocked-bailout/isRestarting-reschedule), `emitRotationTiming` + `emitFullRotationStatus` shapes + no-op gates, `clearCountdownAnnouncements` (idempotent), `scheduleCountdownAnnouncements` bounds (0/1/2/3 announcements at <30s / 45s / 90s / 4min remaining; isLocked-bailout), `executeRotationWithRetry` (disabled/locked no-ops; success → recordSuccess+scheduleNext+emitFull all routed through host; failure → recordFailure+scheduleRetryWithBackoff; defensive reschedule when retry path leaves nothing armed). **Behavior-preserving** — every existing test passes unchanged: 65/65 from PR 17.2's verb+scheduling files (after the host-route adjustment fixed two byte-equivalence regressions that the harness caught), 144/144 across the full rotation suite (10 files), plus the new scheduler unit tests → 171/171 in the targeted suite total. The harness catching the byte-equivalence regression on first run is exactly what PR 17.2 was for. **Reviewer subagent verdict**: CLEAN, no blocker. Punch list checked: timer ownership across all 9 manual-control verbs + 3 lifecycle methods; setTimeout-callback re-entry via `host._*`; recovery-branch defensive reschedule; `this` binding in arrow callback; ordering of `_recordSuccess → _scheduleNextRotation → _emitFullRotationStatus`; `clearCountdownAnnouncements` runs first inside `scheduleCountdownAnnouncements`; nextRotationAt read/write coherence (no shadow field); zero stray `setTimeout` in the main file (only the unrelated cleanup-delay sleeps + the auto-restart `setInterval` survive); PR 17.1 shims (`retryConfig`, `retryState`, `usedAnimalNames`) intact; `setViewBotURLService`'s 60-LoC inline handler still reads `this.rotationTimer` + `this.retryState.currentRetryTimer` correctly through the new accessors. **Diff**: `server/services/random-stream/RotationScheduler.js` +233 (new), `server/services/RandomStreamRotationService.js` -177 / +43 (state init removed; 23 lines of getter/setter accessors + 6 lines of method delegates added; 6 method bodies deleted), `server/tests/services/random-stream/RotationScheduler.test.js` +260 (new, 27 cases), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`RandomStreamRotationService.js` now 1650 LoC**, down from 1815 (−165, −9%; cumulative from Phase 17 start: 2032 → 1650, −382, −19%). **Risk**: MEDIUM — timer ownership transfer is the trickiest part of Phase 17, but the PR 17.2 harness + the new unit tests + the reviewer subagent's punch list together prove the byte-equivalence. **Phase 17 status**: 3/5 sub-PRs landed; PR 17.4 (RotationTimerController — compress the 9 manual-control verbs into a sibling class with thin delegates) is next; it's MED-HIGH risk because it changes 470 LoC of repetitive verb code at once and is the only PR-17 change directly tied to the chat-service `/api/random-stream/*` response shapes.

### Added
- **Test-harness investment for `RandomStreamRotationService` (PR 17.2, Phase 17).** No code moves — pure test add ahead of the higher-risk extractions in PRs 17.3-17.5. Pre-PR test surface was intentionally thin (only `RandomStreamRotationService.test.js` for `updateSettings` persistence regression + `whitelist-fanout.test.js` for the WhitelistService setter; constructor wiring covered indirectly via `bootstrap/start-streaming-backend.test.js`; the one private-method touch in `ModerationActionArbiter.test.js`). The manual-control verb math, scheduling internals, lock-time preservation, retry-execution recovery, and countdown-announcement scheduling had **zero** direct test coverage, which is exactly the surface the next three PRs will move into helpers — so the safety net lands first. **65 new unit tests** across two files. **`RandomStreamRotationService.manualControl.test.js` (37 cases)** — covers every branch of the 9 manual-control verbs: `extendRotation` (happy/no-arg-random-default/event-shape/cooldown-record/cooldown-block/cooldown-expiry/not-enabled/no-rotation/in-progress/clears-old-timer), `adminExtend` (happy/locked/all-error-paths/event-shape/no-cooldown-side-effect), `reduceRotation` (happy/30s-floor/shared-cooldown/random-default/all-error-paths), `adminReduce` (happy/locked/event-shape/30s-floor), `lockRotation` (happy/clears-retry-timer-and-countdowns/emits/all-error-paths), `unlockRotation` (happy/scheduleNextRotation-called-with-stored-remaining/all-error-paths), `getLockStatus` + `getExtendCooldownStatus` (4 cases incl. fresh / mid-window / past-window), `forceRotate` (not-enabled-short-circuit/clears-existing-timer/platform-override-forwarded/emits-random-rotation-force/unlock-on-rotate-success/no-reschedule-on-failure). The verb response shapes the chat-service vote handlers depend on (`extendedByMinutes`, `reducedByMinutes`, `newNextRotationAt`, `remainingMs`, `nextRotationAt`, `cooldownRemaining`, `currentRotationDuration`, `currentStream`, `isAdminExtend`, `isAdminReduce`) are explicitly pinned via `toMatchObject` — that's the byte-equivalence proof the chat-service contract (referenced by `chat-service/votes/{extend,reduce,lock,unlock,skip}Vote.js`) is still load-bearing after PR 17.4 moves these methods into `RotationTimerController`. **`RandomStreamRotationService.scheduling.test.js` (28 cases)** — covers the scheduling internals slated for PR 17.3 extraction: `_scheduleNextRotation` (interval setting, getRandomInterval default, overwrite-existing-timer, callback fires after interval, callback respects `isEnabled === false`, callback respects `isLocked === true`, schedules countdown announcements, emits rotation-timing), `_clearCountdownAnnouncements` (clears all timers/idempotent), `_scheduleCountdownAnnouncements` (0/0/1/2/3-announcement bounds at <30s / 45s / 90s / 4min remaining, isLocked-bailout, isEnabled-bailout, message-string-shape), `_emitRotationTiming` (happy/disabled-no-op/null-io-no-throw), `_emitFullRotationStatus` (happy/null-currentStream-no-op), `_executeRotationWithRetry` (disabled-no-op/locked-no-op/success-resets-failures+reschedules+emits-full/failure-records-and-calls-backoff). **Test harness convention**: both files use a `makeRunningService` (manual-control) or `makeEnabledService` (scheduling) helper that constructs the real service then stubs `_scheduleNextRotation`/`_scheduleCountdownAnnouncements`/`_clearCountdownAnnouncements`/`_emitRotationTiming`/`_emitFullRotationStatus` to stateful no-ops, so verbs that internally call these methods don't leak real multi-minute `setTimeout` instances into jest's event loop. The scheduling file flips the switch and uses `jest.useFakeTimers()` to advance simulated time through the real `_scheduleNextRotation` and `_scheduleCountdownAnnouncements` paths. Persistence file (`server/data/random-rotation-state.json`) is backed up + cleared per-test (matching the pre-existing `RandomStreamRotationService.test.js` pattern). Both files run with `--forceExit` to clean up any incidental dummy timers the tests create themselves. **What this PR does NOT cover**: `start`/`stop`/`pause` lifecycle (touches 4 different `global.*` services with entangled cleanup ordering — the locked Phase 17 decision is to leave these inline, so they get integration-style coverage from the existing `bootstrap/start-streaming-backend.test.js`); `_rotateToNewStream` orchestrator (Twitch/Kick service interactions need full doubles — out of scope for PR 17.2, covered indirectly by `ModerationActionArbiter.test.js`'s `_rotateToNewStream` mock call); auto-restart polling loop (will be extracted in PR 17.5 and gets its own tests there); `_loadState`/`_saveState` persistence (covered by `RandomStreamRotationService.test.js`'s existing two-test suite and again by PR 17.5's `RotationStatePersistence` extraction tests). **Diff**: `server/tests/services/RandomStreamRotationService.manualControl.test.js` +328 (new, 37 cases), `server/tests/services/RandomStreamRotationService.scheduling.test.js` +259 (new, 28 cases), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Service code: 0 LoC changed.** **Tests**: 65/65 new + all 33 pre-existing rotation/bootstrap/arbiter tests pass unchanged. **Risk**: ZERO — pure test add; no production code touched. **Phase 17 status**: 2/5 sub-PRs landed; PR 17.3 (RotationScheduler extraction — timer ownership transfer for `rotationTimer`/`countdownAnnouncementTimers`/`nextRotationAt`/`currentRotationDuration` + the 6 scheduling methods) is now unblocked; the harness above will catch any byte-equivalence regression.

### Changed
- **Extract four pure helpers out of `RandomStreamRotationService` (PR 17.1, Phase 17 kickoff).** First PR of Phase 17 — single-file decomposition of `server/services/RandomStreamRotationService.js` (2032 LoC, EventEmitter subclass with 50+ methods spanning ~12 logical clusters). New `server/services/random-stream/` subdirectory mirrors the `server/services/game/` pattern; the main service file remains the canonical class (still extends `EventEmitter`, still owns `start`/`stop`/`pause`/`_rotateToNewStream`/the manual-control verb family), and the new helpers are internal collaborators that the main class wires up in the constructor. **Four helpers extracted (~220 LoC of behaviour moves out)**: (1) `RotationRetryState.js` — exponential-backoff math (`calculateRetryDelay`/`recordSuccess`/`recordFailure`/`shouldRetry`/`clearTimer`/`reset`/`scheduleRetryWithBackoff`). The helper owns its own `config` + `state` objects; the main service exposes `this.retryConfig` and `this.retryState` as references to those exact objects so existing in-file read sites (auto-restart monitor, lifecycle methods, `getStatus`, the lock/unlock verbs) remain unchanged. The async `scheduleRetryWithBackoff` takes a `{ isLocked, logger }` options bag so the main service can pass `() => this.isLocked` and its bound child logger. (2) `AnimalNameGenerator.js` — the 160-entry `ANIMALS` + 40-entry `ADJECTIVES` arrays plus `generate()` and `reset()` methods. The "100-attempts-then-clear-cache" fallback is preserved verbatim. The helper exposes its internal `usedNames` Set; the main service aliases `this.usedAnimalNames` to that Set so the `clearStats() { this.usedAnimalNames.clear(); }` call site continues to work unchanged. (3) `RotationAnnouncer.js` — the 15-template `ROTATION_MESSAGES` array + `generate(streamer)` for `{STREAMER}/{PLATFORM}/{URL}/{GAME}` substitution. (4) `PlatformSelector.js` — `isReady(settings, viewBotURLService)` + `selectRandom(settings)` + `getRandomInterval(settings)`. Helper holds refs to `twitchService` + `kickService`; settings are passed per call so the main service stays the source of truth for `this.settings`. **Public method signatures preserved as thin delegates** — `generateAnimalName()` (called from `server/routes/random-stream.js:460,490,510`), `generateRotationAnnouncement()`, `getRandomInterval()`, `isReady()`, `selectRandomPlatform()`, and the five `_calculate*/_record*/_shouldRetry/_scheduleRetryWithBackoff` private methods all stay on the main class, each as a 1-line delegate to the relevant helper. External consumers (`server/sockets/StreamHandler.js`, `ViewBotRotationService`, `SimpleViewBotRotation`, `ModerationActionArbiter`, `server/bootstrap/start-streaming-backend.js`, every route in `server/routes/random-stream.js`) see no API change. **Drive-by dead-code removal**: the unused `retryConfig.resetAfterSuccessMs: 60000` field (declared but never read anywhere — confirmed by grep across the whole repo) is dropped. **New unit tests** (`server/tests/services/random-stream/{RotationRetryState,AnimalNameGenerator,RotationAnnouncer,PlatformSelector}.test.js`, 46 cases total, 95%+ line coverage on each helper): retry-state covers exponential growth, the `maxDelayMs` cap, success-clears-timer behaviour, the max-retries-reached path that waits `maxDelayMs` once and resets, the `isLocked()` bailout inside the scheduled callback; animal-name covers shape, uniqueness across many calls, the maxAttempts-clear fallback, `reset()`; announcer covers placeholder substitution (Twitch vs Kick label, displayName/username fallback, game `Unknown` fallback) and template-pool defaulting; platform-selector covers the full `isReady` decision matrix (twitch-configured + viewBotURLService combinations), single-platform shortcut, weighted random behaviour (via stubbed `Math.random` for determinism), and interval bounds. **Behavior-preserving** — every existing test (`server/tests/services/RandomStreamRotationService.test.js`, `RandomStreamRotationService.whitelist-fanout.test.js`, `bootstrap/start-streaming-backend.test.js`, `services/ModerationActionArbiter.test.js`) passes 33/33 unchanged. Service smoke (`new RandomStreamRotationService(); svc.generateAnimalName(); svc.isReady(); svc._calculateRetryDelay(); svc._shouldRetry()`) returns expected shapes. Module-load: `LOAD OK` (the server reaches the listener-bind step, which fails only because port 8443 is held by the live pm2 process — unrelated to this PR). **Diff**: `server/services/random-stream/RotationRetryState.js` +114 (new), `server/services/random-stream/AnimalNameGenerator.js` +92 (new), `server/services/random-stream/RotationAnnouncer.js` +50 (new), `server/services/random-stream/PlatformSelector.js` +93 (new), `server/tests/services/random-stream/RotationRetryState.test.js` +180 (new), `server/tests/services/random-stream/AnimalNameGenerator.test.js` +75 (new), `server/tests/services/random-stream/RotationAnnouncer.test.js` +68 (new), `server/tests/services/random-stream/PlatformSelector.test.js` +138 (new), `server/services/RandomStreamRotationService.js` -250 / +33 (constants block + 7 method bodies replaced by helper imports + 6 thin delegates + 3 constructor wiring lines; `resetAfterSuccessMs` field dropped), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`RandomStreamRotationService.js` now 1815 LoC**, down from 2032 (−217, −11%). **Risk**: LOW — pure helpers with no global state, no I/O surface, no timer side-effects outside the retry-helper's owned timer; the four extractions are mechanical moves with thin-delegate compatibility shims. **Phase 17 status**: 1/5 sub-PRs landed; PR 17.2 (test-harness investment — ~30-50 unit tests targeting the manual-control-verb math + scheduling bounds + animal-name uniqueness fallback + platform-weight distribution) is next; PR 17.3 (RotationScheduler extraction) cannot start until 17.2 lands.

- **Extract `/admin/award-points` + `/admin/take-points` to `AccountService` admin-ledger methods (PR 16.4, Phase 16 close).** Final PR of Phase 16. The 75-LoC `/admin/award-points` and 85-LoC `/admin/take-points` inline handlers in `server/routes/internal.js` move into two new methods on `AccountService`: `adminGrantPoints(adminUserId, targetUsername, amount)` and `adminRevokePoints(adminUserId, targetUsername, amount)`. **Behavior-preserving HTTP layer** — same response shapes (`{ success, newBalance, targetUserId, targetUsername }` on 200), same status codes (400 missing params / insufficient balance on revoke, 401 unauth / mismatched-token, 403 is_admin guard, 404 target-not-found, 500 unexpected), same audit-row arguments to `AccountService.addPoints` / `subtractPoints` (`type='admin_award'` / `'admin_deduction'`, `description='Admin award by <name>'` / `'Admin deduction by <name>'`, `metadata={ adminId }`) so the points ledger is unchanged. The integration test at `routes.internal.points.integration.test.js` covers `/admin/award-points` end-to-end and keeps passing 60/60 unchanged — that's the byte-equivalence proof at the HTTP layer. **Service shape**: each method funnels through the existing `addPoints` / `subtractPoints` (so the production audit invariants — atomic SQL, race-safe balance arithmetic — are preserved unchanged). Validation failures throw `AccountServiceError` (new `Error` subclass with `{ statusCode, clientMessage }`); routes catch and map to the byte-equivalent JSON body. Same typed-error pattern PRs 16.2 (`GameMechanicsError`) and 16.3 (`InventoryError`) established. **Ordering preserved verbatim**: admin row lookup → is_admin guard → target lookup → (revoke only) balance precheck → ledger write. A non-admin caller hitting either endpoint short-circuits at the is_admin gate BEFORE the target lookup, so the 403 fires even when `targetUsername` doesn't exist — same as pre-PR. **Auth check stays in the handler** per the Phase 16 locked decision: routes verify Bearer + `decoded.id === adminUserId` and only then dispatch to the service; the service trusts the caller's claim that they're `adminUserId` and adds the row-level is_admin check. **New unit tests** (`server/tests/services/AccountService.adminPoints.test.js`, 12 cases): both methods' happy paths (asserting `addPoints` / `subtractPoints` args incl. type + description + adminId metadata); 403 when admin row missing or `is_admin=0`; 404 when target doesn't resolve; ordering pin (admin lookup fires before target lookup); revoke 400 with `User only has X points (cannot deduct Y)` message; revoke boundary at `balance === amount`; `AccountServiceError` shape. **Diff**: `server/services/AccountService.js` +110 / -1 (two methods + `AccountServiceError` + module exports), `server/routes/internal.js` +30 / -135 (two handlers collapse from 75 + 85 LoC to ~25 + ~25 LoC; net -105 LoC), `server/tests/services/AccountService.adminPoints.test.js` +175 (new), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`routes/internal.js` now 818 LoC**, down from 901 at PR 16.4 start. **Cumulative Phase 16 reduction: 1168 → 818 (-350 LoC, -30%)**. The original Phase 16 target was ≤500 LoC, but landing at 818 reflects (a) the dispatch + auth boilerplate per remaining route (each thin handler is ~25–35 LoC of auth + body-validate + dispatch + error-map even with the typed-error helper) and (b) the deliberately-inline read-only routes the plan said to LEAVE ALONE (leaderboard, stream-uptime). The 18 routes are now all thin — no inline business logic survives. **Tests**: new unit suite 12/12; integration `routes.internal.points` 60/60 unchanged; gift integration 28/28 unchanged; full server jest 1191/1191 (the previously-flaky `database/transaction.test.js` ↔ `database/database-better.test.js` race passed clean this run). Module-load: `LOAD OK`. **Risk**: LOW — same dispatch pattern as PR 16.2/16.3, with the integration test for `/admin/award-points` providing end-to-end byte-equivalence proof. **Phase 16 status**: 4/4 sub-PRs landed; Phase 16 CLOSES.

- **Extract `/gift-item` + `/giftable-items` to `InventoryService` (PR 16.3, Phase 16).** Third PR of Phase 16. The 120-LoC `/gift-item` and 57-LoC `/giftable-items/:userId` inline handlers in `server/routes/internal.js` move into two new methods on `InventoryService`: `giftItem(fromUserId, toUserId, itemId, quantity = 1)` and `getGiftableItems(userId)`. **Behavior-preserving HTTP layer** — same response shapes (`{ success, item: { id, name, emoji }, quantity, from, to }` on the gift; `{ success, items: [...] }` on the list), same status codes (400 self-gift / not-tradeable / insufficient, 404 user / item / item-no-longer-resolves, 401 auth, 500 unexpected), same audit-row write to `gift_transactions` with `(from_user_id, to_user_id, item_id, quantity, timestamp = datetime('now'))` so the gift ledger is unchanged. **Split of concerns**: the route owns HTTP-string-to-domain-id translation (username → recipientId via `accountService.getUserByUsername`, itemName → item via `itemService.getAllItems()` + case-insensitive find — both keeping their pre-PR 404 messages); the service owns the eligibility chain (self-gift, `is_tradeable`, sufficient-quantity) and the swap + audit write. Self-gift 400 fires before the item lookup in the new service body so the ordering observable at the HTTP layer matches the pre-PR sequence (1: username 404 → 2: self-gift 400 → 3: item 404 → 4: not-tradeable 400 → 5: insufficient 400). **Service shape**: `giftItem` returns `{ item: { id, name (display_name), emoji }, quantity }` for the route to fold into the 200 response (the route still owns `from` / `to` username fields); `getGiftableItems` returns the array shape directly. Client-facing failures throw `InventoryError` (new `Error` subclass with `{ statusCode, clientMessage }`); the route catches and maps to `res.status(...).json({ success: false, error })`. **`inventoryService` resolution**: the route reads it from `req.app.locals.services.inventoryService` (the canonical, factory-wired instance) with a fallback to `new InventoryService(new ItemService())` for test harnesses that don't supply the services bag. This is the same dispatch pattern PR 16.2 introduced for `gameMechanicsService`. **Audit-row mechanics**: the `INSERT INTO gift_transactions` write is now inside `InventoryService.giftItem` (late-`require`d so unit tests can `jest.mock` the database module without dragging it into the require graph at service module-load time) — same SQL, same bindings as pre-PR. **NOT transactional today** — the three writes (remove from sender, add to recipient, insert audit) remain unwrapped, matching pre-PR behaviour; wrapping in `withTransaction` is called out as a follow-up but is out of scope for Phase 16 (which is byte-equivalent extraction, not bug-fixing). **New unit tests** (`server/tests/services/InventoryService.giftItem.test.js`, 11 cases): `giftItem` happy path (asserts `updateQuantity`/`insertItem`/`runAsync` SQL + bindings); self-gift short-circuit verifies item lookup + writes never fire; itemId no-longer-resolves 404; soulbound 400 with `display_name` in the message; insufficient-inventory 400 with `(have: N, need: M)` detail; have:0 path when sender owns no row; `quantity` defaults to 1 when omitted; `getGiftableItems` filters to `is_tradeable && quantity > 0` and drops rows whose `item_id` no longer resolves; `InventoryError` shape. **`bonus-status` / `giftable-items` `parseInt` boundary** — same pattern PR 16.2 introduced: the route calls `parseInt(req.params.userId)` once at the boundary, passes the int to the service. **Integration test setup unchanged in PR 16.3** — the `routes.internal.points.integration.test.js` covers `/transfer-points` and `/award-points`, not gift; the gift route's fallback to `new InventoryService(...)` when `app.locals.services` is unset keeps the test mounting story trivial. **Diff**: `server/services/InventoryService.js` +97 / -0 (two methods + `InventoryError` + module exports), `server/routes/internal.js` +29 / -92 (two handlers collapse from 120 + 57 LoC to ~70 + ~25 LoC; net -63 LoC), `server/tests/services/InventoryService.giftItem.test.js` +209 (new), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`routes/internal.js` now 885 LoC**, down from 948 at PR 16.3 start; cumulative Phase 16 reduction 1168 → 885 (-283). **Tests**: new unit suite 11/11; integration `routes.internal.points` 60/60 unchanged; full server jest 1178/1179 (same pre-existing parallel-SQLite flake). Module-load: `LOAD OK`. **Risk**: MEDIUM — gift handling has user-facing edge cases (gifting to self, soulbound items, insufficient quantity) that the new unit tests pin and that the reviewer subagent on this PR is verifying. **Phase 16 status**: 3/4 sub-PRs landed; PR 16.4 (admin/award-points + admin/take-points → AccountService) is next and closes Phase 16.

- **Extract `/gamble` + `/slots` + `/claim-chat-bonus` + `/transfer-points` + `/bonus-status` to `GameMechanicsService` (PR 16.2, Phase 16).** Second PR of Phase 16. Five inline route handlers in `server/routes/internal.js` previously carried 60–110 LoC each of game-mechanic logic (RNG rolls, slot payout table, 2-minute chat-bonus cooldown window, balance math, peer-transfer ordering); now they dispatch to `GameMechanicsService` methods seeded by PR 16.1, and the handlers are thin auth + dispatch + error mapping (~10–15 LoC each). **Behavior-preserving HTTP layer** — same response shapes, same status codes (`400` insufficient/missing/self-transfer, `401` unauth/bad-credentials, `404` sender/recipient not found, `429` bonus cooldown, `500` unexpected), same audit-row arguments to `AccountService.addPoints` / `subtractPoints` so the points ledger is unchanged. **Service shape**: each method returns a payload object on success; client-facing failures throw `GameMechanicsError` (an `Error` subclass with `{ statusCode, clientMessage, extra }`) which the new `respondGameMechanicsError(err, res)` helper in the route module maps to the byte-equivalent JSON body. The `extra` slot carries the `remainingSeconds` + `nextAvailable` fields the cooldown 429 response needs. **`bonus-status` `parseInt` boundary**: the previous inline handler did `userBonusCooldowns.get(parseInt(userId))` because `req.params` always returns strings while the writer (`claim-chat-bonus`) uses the JSON body's numeric `userId`. The PR moves the `parseInt` to the route boundary (handler does `parseInt(req.params.userId)` once, passes to the service); the service deals only in numeric ids. **Frozen slot payout table** — `SLOT_SYMBOLS = Object.freeze(['🍒','🍋','🍊','🍇','💎','7️⃣'])` exported alongside `CHAT_BONUS_COOLDOWN_MS` (`2 * 60 * 1000`) and `CHAT_BONUS_AMOUNT` (`100`) so future tweaks happen in one place and a careless in-place mutation TypeErrors instead of silently shifting odds. **Integration test setup updated** (`server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js`): `buildApp()` now constructs an `AccountService` + `GameMechanicsService` + cooldown Map per test and stuffs them on `app.locals.services` — the assertions (which is the byte-equivalence proof) are unchanged. **New unit tests** (`server/tests/services/GameMechanicsService.test.js`, 27 cases): constructor contract (rejects missing deps, identity-pins the cooldown Map by reference), `gamble` win/lose/insufficient with `Math.random` stub, `slots` jackpot/diamond/3-of-kind/2-of-kind-break-even/lose/insufficient with rigged spin index math, `claimChatBonus` happy + 429 cooldown + past-cooldown, `getBonusStatus` available/expired/inside-cooldown + map-readonly, `transferPoints` happy/sender-404/recipient-404/self-400/insufficient-400 + DB-username fallback, `GameMechanicsError` shape. **Diff**: `server/services/GameMechanicsService.js` +283 / -54 (stub bodies → real implementations, plus `GameMechanicsError` + exported constants), `server/routes/internal.js` +37 / -263 (five handlers collapse from 60–110 LoC each to ~12 LoC each; net -226 LoC), `server/tests/services/GameMechanicsService.test.js` +377 (new), `server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js` +18 / -4 (wire `services` bag in `buildApp`; assertions unchanged), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`routes/internal.js` now 942 LoC**, down from 1168 at Phase 16 start (-226). **Tests**: new unit suite 27/27; integration `routes.internal.points` 60/60 unchanged; full server jest 1167/1168 (one pre-existing flaky parallel-SQLite failure between `database/transaction.test.js` ↔ `database/database-better.test.js` — same failure pattern present on `main` HEAD). Module-load: `LOAD OK`. **Risk**: MEDIUM — slot payout math and gamble win-condition arithmetic are precisely the off-by-one targets the reviewer subagent on this PR is tasked with verifying; integration test for `transfer-points` (the one PR-16.2 endpoint with end-to-end coverage) passing unchanged is the byte-equivalence proof. **Phase 16 status**: 2/4 sub-PRs landed; PR 16.3 (gift extraction to `InventoryService`) is next.

### Added
- **`GameMechanicsService` scaffold + bootstrap wiring (PR 16.1, Phase 16 kickoff).** New `server/services/GameMechanicsService.js` (~75 LoC) carries five stub methods — `gamble`, `slots`, `claimChatBonus`, `transferPoints`, `getBonusStatus` — that all `throw new Error('… not implemented (PR 16.2)')`. The bodies land in PR 16.2; this PR lands the seam so the factory + tests can name the service. Constructor takes `{ accountService, userBonusCooldowns }` — `accountService` for the audited points ledger (every balance change in PR 16.2 will flow through `AccountService.addPoints` / `subtractPoints`, so the audit trail is preserved), and `userBonusCooldowns` is the shared `Map<userId, lastClaimEpochMs>` previously declared just above the `/api/internal/*` mount in `server/index.js`. **Map ownership stays in `server/index.js`** per the Phase 16 locked decision — the Map is created before `createServices()` and passed in as a factory dep, then `app.locals.userBonusCooldowns = userBonusCooldowns` continues to expose the same reference to the routes module. Same shared-by-reference pattern PR 15B.2.a used for `lastEmittedStreamReady`. Wiring in `server/bootstrap/services.js`: factory accepts `userBonusCooldowns` in its deps object, constructs `gameMechanicsService` immediately after the item/inventory/shop chain, exposes it in the returned services bag. Test surface in `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js`: new mock + require + key-list entry + instance-of check + dep-graph test that identity-pins the cooldown Map (catches a future refactor that accidentally clones it); expected key count bumps 42 → 43. **Behavior-preserving** — no route handler in `routes/internal.js` calls into the new service yet, so HTTP behavior is unchanged. `routes/internal.js` LoC unchanged (1168). **Diff**: `server/services/GameMechanicsService.js` +75 (new), `server/bootstrap/services.js` +18 / -2, `server/index.js` +9 / -3 (Map construction hoisted + factory call updated + alias comment), `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js` +27 / -2 (mock + require + key + instance-of + dep-graph test), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js` 44/44 (up from 43/43); `server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js` 60/60 (unchanged from baseline). Module-load: `LOAD OK`. **Risk**: LOW (read-only addition; the route file is untouched). **Phase 16 status**: 1/4 sub-PRs landed; `routes/internal.js` decomposition begins in PR 16.2.

- **URL-relay English-language filter (ADR-0023, Phase 1).** Extends the ADR-0010 whitelist with a new `preferred_languages` JSON column on `url_relay_filter_config` (default `["en"]` per the seed; empty array disables the gate per-platform). New language gate inside `WhitelistService.checkAllowed()` runs after the always-on CCL / mature checks and after the `mode === 'off'` short-circuit — so off mode still bypasses all policy, but blacklist and whitelist modes now reject candidates whose ISO-639-1 broadcaster language isn't in the preferred set. **Strict-vs-lenient on null language** matches each mode's existing posture: whitelist mode rejects unknown (`language_unknown_strict`), blacklist mode lets it through (the precision/recall split mirrors the streamer/category list semantics). Plumbed into `TwitchRandomService.findRandomStreamer()` via the existing `stream.language` field from `/helix/streams` (no extra API calls — the field was already in the response, just never re-checked), and into `KickRandomService.findRandomStreamer()` via a new normalization in `server/services/kick-api-helper.py` that probes the known carriers (`stream.language`, `stream.channel.language`, `stream.broadcaster_language`, the `livestream` / `user` nested shapes) and falls back to the URL-path language filter as the last-resort signal. **Live-test discovery on 2026-05-27**: Kick's scrape endpoint returns full lowercase English language NAMES (`"english"`, `"spanish"`, `"turkish"`, ...) rather than ISO-639-1 codes, so the helper now includes a `LANGUAGE_NAME_TO_ISO` mapping (40+ entries covering the languages Kick's broadcaster picker offers). Without this mapping, the gate would reject 100% of Kick streams under `preferred_languages: ["en"]`. Additionally, the `/livestreams/<lang>` URL filter is empirically a hint — only 11 of 30 streams from `/livestreams/en` were actually English on the test pull. End-to-end smoke verified: under blacklist mode + preferred `["en"]`, the gate correctly allows 8 streams, rejects 13 by language (correct ISO codes for `es` / `tr` / `pl` / `ar` / `pt` / `ru`), and 9 by the always-on mature/CCL gates (precedence: mature/CCL fires before language as designed). `getCurrentStreamSnapshot()` on both services now returns `language`, so the existing `WhitelistEnforcer` drift check picks up a streamer who switches their declared language mid-broadcast. New admin endpoint `POST /api/whitelist/language { platform, preferred_languages: [...] }` calls `WhitelistService.setLanguagePreference(platform, langs, actor)` which normalizes (trim → lowercase → dedupe), persists, writes a `language_preference_change` audit row, refreshes cache, and emits `change` event. The read path is already covered by `GET /api/whitelist/config` (the cache returns the parsed array). Schema migration `server/migrations/202605270010-url-relay-add-preferred-languages.js` ADDs the column on existing DBs and is a no-op on fresh installs — `url_relay_filter_config` is owned by `WhitelistService._applySchema()` which runs **after** the migration runner on a fresh boot, and the updated `server/database/url-relay-whitelist-schema.sql` now declares the column at CREATE TABLE time, so the migration silently skips when its target table isn't there yet. **Deferred to follow-up phases (per ADR-0023):** (1) **Kick OAuth migration** to the authenticated `api.kick.com/public/v1/*` Public API — free to register (`dev.kick.com`, no fees, no KYC), but deferred for blast-radius because the existing curl_cffi scrape path is what provides authenticated JWT playback URLs and replacing it needs its own PR. (2) **Twitch Helix multi-language query** — `TwitchRandomService.getLiveStreams()` still passes the hardcoded `language=en` URL parameter, which correctly serves the default but doesn't honour a non-English `preferred_languages` setting at the server-side prefilter step; the WhitelistService post-filter is the authoritative check. (3) **Title-text language detection** with `lingua-language-detector` (~7ms per check, Rust-backed, designed for short noisy text) for streams where the API field is missing or returns `"other"` — covers most of the documented ~10–20% Twitch mislabel rate at trivial cost. (4) **Whisper audio sampling** with `faster-whisper` tiny on 15–30s HLS pulls as a last-resort fallback. (5) **EventSub / Kick webhook integration** for push-invalidation on `channel.update` and `livestream.metadata.updated`. (6) **Admin UI surface** — Phase 1 ships DB + API + seed only. **Tests**: `npx jest server/tests/WhitelistService.test.js` passes 49/49 including 16 new language-gate and `setLanguagePreference` cases; `npx jest server/tests/services/{TwitchRandomService,KickRandomService}.whitelist.test.js` passes 18/18 including 7 new shape-plumbing and drift-snapshot cases; `npx jest server/tests/database/migrations.runner.test.js` passes 8/8 (the new migration's table-existence guard keeps both fresh-DB-idempotency and legacy-DB-backfill scenarios at zero logged errors). **Risk**: LOW — changes layer onto the existing ADR-0010 gate as an additional check; the seed-default mirror of the previous implicit behaviour (Twitch was already calling Helix with `language=en`) means production rotation behavior is unchanged for the default operator. **Files**: `server/database/url-relay-whitelist-schema.sql` (+2 / -0, column declaration), `server/data/seeds/url-relay-whitelist.seed.json` (+2 / -0, `preferred_languages: ["en"]` on both platforms), `server/migrations/202605270010-url-relay-add-preferred-languages.js` (new, 55 lines), `server/services/WhitelistService.js` (+96 / -10, helper, gate, mutator), `server/services/TwitchRandomService.js` (+2 / -0, two shape additions), `server/services/KickRandomService.js` (+10 / -1, shape addition + snapshot extraction), `server/services/kick-api-helper.py` (+48 / -8, `_extract_language` helper + normalization in `get_live_streams`), `server/routes/whitelist.js` (+14 / -0, new POST `/language` endpoint), `server/tests/WhitelistService.test.js` (+162 / -5, two new `describe` blocks plus `language: 'en'` added to existing whitelist-mode tests so they continue to test their original gates rather than failing the new strict-on-null check), `server/tests/services/TwitchRandomService.whitelist.test.js` (+62 / -0, two new tests covering shape plumbing and snapshot output), `server/tests/services/KickRandomService.whitelist.test.js` (+86 / -0, four new tests), `docs/architecture/adr/0023-url-relay-language-filter.md` (new), `CHANGELOG.md` (+1 entry).

the `useVisualFxProcessor` hook itself and its callers in `WebRTCStreamer.tsx` / `WebRTCViewer.tsx`; the standalone test pages `client/public/{test-potato-client.html, visual-effects-test.html}` (they exercise the live `ClientVisualFxProcessor.js`, separate from the deleted debug-panel surface). **Inventory comment updated**: the "visualfx debug static assets" residual row in `server/index.js` rewrites to `[deleted]` with archaeology — Phase 15B residual count drops from ~5 to ~3 (user chat-color + admin dashboard render only). **Diff**: `server/index.js` -30 / +7 (inventory rewrite), `client/public/index.html` -13, `client/src/setupProxy.js` -10, three orphan files removed (704 + 704 + 1100 LoC + 1 build artifact), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`index.js` now 2421 LoC** (down from 2446 at start of this PR). **Tests**: 80/80 pass. - **Extract custom emoji CRUD to `routes/emojis.js` + cleanup duplicate chat-mod routes (PR 15B.3.b, Phase 15B follow-up).** Eighth route-cluster extraction. **(1) Emoji CRUD**: 6 routes / 317 LoC moves out of `server/index.js` — `GET /api/emojis` (public list), `GET /api/admin/emojis` (admin list), `POST /api/admin/emojis` (upload, multipart), `PUT /api/admin/emojis/:id`, `DELETE /api/admin/emojis/:id`, `POST /api/emojis/:code/use` (public usage tracker). Same pattern PR 15B.3.h used — factory accepts `serverDir` as absolute path; callsites become `path.join(serverDir, '..', basePath)` and `path.join(serverDir, 'uploads', 'emojis')`. **(2) Honesty cleanup — duplicate chat-mod routes deleted from `index.js`**: PR 15B.3.c (admin-moderation extraction) mounted the router with all 16 routes BUT only deleted one of the two non-contiguous source blocks; the first block (chat-mod proxy POSTs — moderation/ban/unban/timeout/remove-timeout) remained inline as duplicates of the mounted router's first 5 routes. Express was processing the mounted router's handlers first (registered earlier in the middleware chain), so behaviour was preserved — but the duplicates were a real cleanliness bug. This PR deletes the inline duplicates (92 LoC) at the same time as the emoji extract. Body byte-equivalent except for the standard `app.X(...)` → `router.X(...)` transform plus the two `__dirname` → `serverDir` substitutions. **Worktree workflow**: developed in `.claude/worktrees/emoji-routes-extract/`. **Module-load verified**: `LOAD OK`. **Diff**: `server/routes/emojis.js` +355 (new), `server/index.js` -411 / +6 (delete emoji cluster + delete duplicate chat-mod block + insert emoji mount call + update inventory rows), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **`index.js` now 2444 LoC** (down from 2847 — 92 from chat-mod cleanup + 311 from emoji extract). **Cumulative since Phase 15 start: 5279 → 2444, ~54% reduction. From Phase-5 baseline: 5708 → 2444, ~57%**. **Tests**: 80/80 pass. **Risk**: MEDIUM (chat-mod cleanup means any client hitting `/api/admin/{ban,unban,timeout,...}` now exercises the extracted router exclusively — same handler since 15B.3.c, but worth a smoke). **Phase 15B.3 status**: 8/10 sub-PRs landed; residual inline-route count drops from ~11 to ~5.

- **Extract admin-ops bundle (stream control + cooldowns + debug + system metrics + uploaded videos) to `routes/admin-ops.js` (PR 15B.3.f+g, Phase 15B follow-up).** Seventh route-cluster extraction; combined 15B.3.f and 15B.3.g (and 15B.3.g's adjacent uploaded-videos surface) per the "admin-ops bundle" maintainer call — these clusters share auth (`authenticateAdmin` / `adminKeyAuth`) and most deps, so bundling amortizes the per-cluster factory boilerplate. **15 routes / 399 LoC** moves out of `server/index.js`: stream control (`POST /admin/{force-disconnect,send-message,clear-stream}`, `GET /admin/connections`), cooldowns (`POST /admin/{remove-cooldown,reset-cooldowns}`, `GET /admin/cooldowns`), debug + system (`GET /debug/server-state` — unauth'd by design; `GET /admin/{system-metrics,system-health,performance-stats}`, `POST /admin/clear-alerts`), uploaded videos (`POST /admin/upload-video`, `GET /admin/uploaded-videos`, `DELETE /admin/uploaded-videos/:filename` — all `adminKeyAuth`). Factory: `createAdminOpsRouter(deps)` accepts both middleware refs plus the union of all service deps used by the 15 handlers (`sessionService`, `streamService`, `takeoverService`, `accountService`, `itemService`, `timeTrackingService`, `mediasoupService`, `resourceMonitor`, `streamNotifier`, `viewerCountNotifier`, `database`, `io`, `fs`, `path`, `upload`, `uploadsDir`, `logger`). - **Extract shutdown sequence + signal handlers + `cleanupMediaProcesses` to `bootstrap/shutdown.js` (PR 15B.4, Phase 15B).** Moves the 277-LoC graceful-shutdown block from `server/index.js:5253–5557` into a new module. The pre-PR block contained `async function shutdown(signal)` (the orderly drain — stoppables registry iteration, socket disconnect, ViewBot/Recording/VisualFx service cleanup, MediaSoup teardown, session clear, Redis quit, server close), the four `process.on(...)` handlers (SIGINT, SIGTERM, uncaughtException, unhandledRejection), and the `cleanupMediaProcesses()` emergency-pkill helper. Post-PR shape is a single factory `registerShutdownHandlers(deps)` that wires all four handlers and contains byte-equivalent bodies. **Lazy-service handling** mirrors PR 15B.5: services that may be undefined at module-load time (`viewbotService`, `viewBotClientService`, `recordingService`, `visualFxService`, `streamInterceptorService`, `timeTrackingService`, `resourceMonitor`, `sessionService`, `mediasoupService`, and the optional `viewBotGStreamerService` / `simpleMediaStreamService`) are passed via getter functions — lookups happen at signal-arrival time. Eager deps (`stoppables`, `io`, `server`) are passed by value. **Two `// console-allowed: uncaughtException fallback` markers** preserved inline in the extracted module (PR 15A.2 originals); the docstring rewords its mention of the markers to avoid the literal token that would fail the expanded `no-console.test.js` (same archaeology-comment pattern PR 12.3 used). **Shutdown ordering invariants documented** in the module docstring (six numbered rules; do not reorder without re-running the SIGTERM smoke). The `typeof X !== 'undefined'` guards for `viewBotGStreamerService` / `simpleMediaStreamService` are preserved verbatim (pre-existing pattern — those services may or may not exist depending on env / feature flags). **Diff**: `server/bootstrap/shutdown.js` +291 (new), `server/index.js` -279 / +22 (delete inline shutdown block + handlers + cleanup helper; insert single `require('./bootstrap/shutdown')({ ... })` call with full deps bag; update inventory comment), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: 80/80 pass across sockets, observability, bootstrap. **Risk**: MEDIUM per Phase 15 plan (shutdown ordering matters). - **Extract per-connection socket-handler registration to `bootstrap/register-socket-handlers.js` (PR 15B.5, Phase 15B).** The `io.on('connection', async (socket) => { ... })` block — 264 LoC at `server/index.js:4565–4828` — moves into a new `bootstrap/register-socket-handlers.js` factory: `registerSocketHandlers(io, deps)` registers the connection listener once and forwards the deps bag to each per-namespace `register*Handler(io, socket, …)` call. Same pattern `bootstrap/start-listeners.js` established in PR 4.3. **Lazy-service handling**: four services are assigned inside `startServer()` after the socket listener is registered (`viewbotService`, `viewBotClientService`, `recordingService`, `transcriptionService`). The pre-PR inline body resolved them through closure-at-callback-time; the post-PR extracted module accepts getter functions (`getViewbotService`, `getViewBotClientService`, `getRecordingService`, `getTranscriptionService`) so the lookup happens at connection-callback time, after `startServer()` has wired them. The deps bag passed from `index.js` to `registerSocketHandlers(io, deps)` is the union of every dep referenced inside the connection block: ~40 entries spanning eager services (StreamService, TakeoverService, MediasoupService, BuffDebuffService, etc.), shared module-scope state (`notifiedStreamers`, `viewbotSocketIds`, `lastEmittedStreamReady`), orchestration helpers (the 15B.2.a trio), the cache helpers (15B.2.b), chokepoint notifiers, utility imports (axios, https, runAsync, database), and the four lazy-service getters. **Body byte-equivalent**: every per-handler `register*Handler(io, socket, ...)` call inside the new module has the same dep keys as the pre-PR inline version. IP-ban check, JWT auth, session register, `socket.onAny` debug logger, and the `canvasFxService.handleClientConnection(socket)` / `visualFxService.handleClientConnection(socket)` per-socket setups all preserved. **Diff**: `server/bootstrap/register-socket-handlers.js` +228 (new — factory, deps destructure, full byte-equivalent connection body), `server/index.js` -250 / +75 (delete the inline io.on block; insert the `require('./bootstrap/register-socket-handlers')(io, { ... })` call with the full deps bag; one inventory comment update), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: 80/80 pass across sockets, observability, bootstrap (`npx jest server/tests/sockets/ server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js server/tests/bootstrap/`). **Risk**: LOW–MEDIUM per Phase 15 plan (mechanical move; lazy-service handling preserved via getters). **No reviewer subagent pass** — plan flags 15B.5 as low risk; the lazy-service handling matches the proven pattern from PR 15B.2.a. **Phase 15 status**: 10/11 PRs done.

- **Middleware / route-mount / server-init section headers in `server/index.js` (PR 15B.6, Phase 15B).** Per Phase 15 plan's locked decision #7: middleware extraction is downgraded to a section-header pass. Pure `app.use(...)` wiring is wiring; middleware order is load-bearing; extracting into `bootstrap/middleware.js` would force `index.js` to import a module to call `applyMiddleware(app, ...)` instead of seeing the chain in plain Express idiom. The cognitive win comes from navigability, not module count. Three section headers added: **MIDDLEWARE SETUP** (compression → cors → trace-context → security headers → body parsing → static → session → passport), **ROUTE MOUNTS** (top-of-tree fanout), **SERVER INIT** (express app + HTTP/HTTPS server objects, with a one-line note that the HTTPS cert load lives in `startServer()` and shutdown closes the server objects). Each header carries a brief "order matters; see ADR-0020 for trace-context placement" note so a future reader doesn't reorder without reading the relevant ADR. **Diff**: `server/index.js` -2 / +25 (the three header blocks + one inventory comment update); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. Zero runtime impact (pure JS comments). **Tests**: 1/1 no-console.test.js passes (the comments contain no `console.*` tokens). **Risk**: LOW.

- **Extract `initializeRedis` to `bootstrap/redis.js` + viewbot username cache to `services/viewbot/UsernameCache.js` (PR 15B.2.b, Phase 15B).** Second of three 15B.2 sub-PRs. Similarly, `getStreamerDisplayName` (the lazy-service-closure helper from PR 15B.1's audit) stays inline pending maintainer call on the destination — `UserService` vs. inline-with-section-header — recorded as a Phase 15B residual. **(1) `initializeRedis` → `bootstrap/redis.js`.** Pre-PR shape mutated a module-scope `let redisClient` in `index.js`; post-PR shape returns the connected client (or `null` when the env var is absent / connection fails) so the caller does the assignment. Small signature change with only one caller (`startServer()` at `index.js:4915` — now reads `redisClient = await bootInitializeRedis()`). The `let redisClient` declaration stays at `index.js:504` because (a) `shutdown()` calls `redisClient.quit()` on it, and (b) the in-flight `createServices({ ..., redisClient, ... })` call at `index.js:548` is intentional — services receive `undefined` at module-load and consult the module-scope binding lazily after `startServer()` runs the assignment. **(2) Viewbot username cache → `services/viewbot/UsernameCache.js`.** Pre-PR shape had three module-scope state holders (`VIEWBOT_ANIMALS` array, `viewbotUsernameCache` Map, `viewbotSocketIds` Set) and two helpers (`cleanupViewbotUsername`, `generateViewbotUsername`) sharing the state via closure. Post-PR shape is a factory `createUsernameCache()` that returns `{ cache, socketIds, cleanup, generate }`. The `cache` and `socketIds` are still accessible as module-scope bindings in `index.js` (destructured from the factory result) because they are still referenced from `getStreamerDisplayName` (inline; deferred to 15B.2.c or beyond), from `enrichStreamStatus` (now in `services/StreamOrchestration.js` via `getStreamerDisplayName`), from socket-handler deps bags, and exposed on `app.locals` for `server/routes/internal.js`. **Diff**: `server/bootstrap/redis.js` +42 (new — `initializeRedis()` factory + null-fallback + JSDoc covering the behaviour-preservation invariants), `server/services/viewbot/UsernameCache.js` +75 (new — `createUsernameCache()` factory + the animals list + `cleanup` / `generate` methods + docstring covering the cross-module-consumer ownership), `server/index.js` -73 / +15 (delete two helper definitions + three state-holder declarations; replace with two factory invocations and destructure-back-to-original-names; update three inventory-comment rows to `[extracted]`), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: 80/80 pass across sockets, observability, and bootstrap (`npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/sockets/ server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js server/tests/bootstrap/`). **Risk**: LOW–MEDIUM per plan; no lazy-service closures involved in either extraction (both helpers' closures are eager — the redis path mutates a `let` declared just above, the username cache's state is module-private and exposed via destructure). **No reviewer subagent pass** (plan only requires reviewer for 15B.2.a + 15B.2.c, not 15B.2.b; the changes here are mechanical file moves with the destructure-back-to-original-names trick that PR 15B.2.a established). **Phase 15 status**: 6/9 PRs done. Next: PR 15B.2.c — VisualFx-sync helpers + verification pass + maintainer call on `getStreamerDisplayName`.

- **Extract three orchestration helpers to `services/StreamOrchestration.js` (PR 15B.2.a, Phase 15B).** First of the three 15B.2 sub-PRs. Moves the cross-service glue helpers `broadcastGlobalCooldown`, `enrichStreamStatus`, and `verifyAndEmitStreamReady` out of `server/index.js` and into a new module behind a factory: `createStreamOrchestration({ io, takeoverService, mediasoupService, getStreamerDisplayName, lastEmittedStreamReady })`. Construction lands in `index.js` right after `getStreamerDisplayName` is declared (the inline helper, still in place — its extraction is 15B.2.b's call) and the three methods are destructured back to module-scope so the existing route handlers (`index.js:1769,1803`) and socket-handler `deps` bags (StreamHandler/`:4740,4744`, MediaSoupHandler/`:4770,4773`) continue to reference the same names. **Why a dedicated module, not a domain service**: the three helpers coordinate across ≥2 services each — `broadcastGlobalCooldown` reads `takeoverService.globalCooldownSeconds` and emits via `io`; `enrichStreamStatus` is the cross-service display-name resolver; `verifyAndEmitStreamReady` coordinates MediasoupService verification (LiveKit path) with display-name resolution and the shared dedup state — and forcing them into a single domain service would create cross-imports between domain services that today don't know about each other (per Phase 15 plan's locked decision #5). **Closure audit predictions held empirically**: the PR-15B.1 audit flagged `enrichStreamStatus` + `verifyAndEmitStreamReady` as transitively reading lazy-init services (via `getStreamerDisplayName` → `global.randomStreamRotationService` / `global.viewBotURLService` / `viewbotService`) and predicted the safe extraction path is "pass `getStreamerDisplayName` as a function reference so the lazy reads happen at call time". The factory below does exactly that — `getStreamerDisplayName` is invoked from inside the orchestration methods, never at construction time — so `createStreamOrchestration` can be invoked at module-load time (before `startServer()` and before the lazy services exist) without ReferenceError. Verified by `node --check server/index.js` (clean) and the full sockets+observability+bootstrap test surface (80/80 pass under `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/sockets/ server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js server/tests/bootstrap/`). **Shared module-scope state**: `lastEmittedStreamReady` (the 2-second dedup window state for `verifyAndEmitStreamReady`) stays declared in `index.js` and is passed by reference into the factory AND into `StreamHandler`'s deps bag — so both emit paths (the orchestration helper and the socket handler's stream-ready emit at `StreamHandler.js`) see the same object. Moving ownership of `lastEmittedStreamReady` into the orchestration module would force the socket handlers to read it through a second indirection (`streamOrchestration.lastEmittedStreamReady`), which the plan's minimum-touch rule discourages. **Verb mapping preserved**: every `logger.X(...)` call inside the extracted helpers keeps its level and message (PR 15A.2's mapping is the only style touch on this surface). **Diff**: `server/services/StreamOrchestration.js` +180 (new — factory, three methods, constructor-arg null-checks, file-level docstring explaining the closure audit and the lazy-vs-eager call), `server/index.js` -111 / +20 (delete three inline helpers; keep `lastEmittedStreamReady` declaration in place; insert factory invocation; destructure three names back to module-scope; update three rows of the PR-15B.1 inventory comment block to mark them `[extracted]`), `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Inventory comment maintained**: the three lines that previously read `841–860 broadcastGlobalCooldown → services/StreamOrchestration.js (15B.2.a)` now read `[extracted] broadcastGlobalCooldown → services/StreamOrchestration.js (15B.2.a — landed)`. By the end of Phase 15B, every line either reads `[extracted]` or has been deleted; PR 15B.2.c is the cleanup pass that removes the marker lines once every helper in the block has been moved. **Tests**: 80/80 across sockets, observability, and bootstrap. No new unit test for `StreamOrchestration` yet — 15B.2.c will add empirical verification (deliberate-attempt + boot-time success check) and any focused unit tests if the maintainer's reviewer flags coverage gaps. **Risk**: MEDIUM per Phase 15 plan (closure-over-lazy-service was the audit's headline hazard). Reviewer subagent pass required per plan; harsh prompt focuses on (1) the lazy-service closure correctness and (2) whether the `lastEmittedStreamReady` shared-by-reference shape holds end-to-end. **ADR call deferred**: the plan's "maintainer choice point" for whether `StreamOrchestration` warrants ADR-0023 ("cross-service orchestration belongs in a dedicated module") sits at this PR's review time. The CHANGELOG records the *fact* of extraction; the maintainer's call on whether to ship an ADR alongside lands at merge time. **Phase 15 status**: 5/9 PRs done. Next: PR 15B.2.b — domain helpers extraction (`initializeRedis` → `bootstrap/redis.js`, `getActiveVisualEffects` + `startVisualEffectSync` → `services/VisualFxService.js`, `cleanupViewbotUsername` + `generateViewbotUsername` → `services/viewbot/UsernameCache.js`, and the maintainer-choice call on `getStreamerDisplayName`).

- **Phase 15B opens: `server/index.js` decomposition inventory + closure audit (PR 15B.1, Phase 15B, read-only triage).** First PR of Phase 15B. Read-only — adds a 77-line comment block at the top of [`server/index.js`](server/index.js) mapping every remaining inline surface (helpers, routes, lifecycle, socket-handler registration, middleware) to its destination file in the planned 15B.2/15B.3/15B.4/15B.5/15B.6 sub-PRs. The block is the load-bearing input for every subsequent 15B PR: each sub-PR removes its row as it lands, so a reader can always see what's already moved and what's still inline. **Closure audit** (recorded in the PR description, per the plan's "no separate .md" rule) catalogues the ten helpers at lines 432–1121 by what module-scope state each closes over, whether that state is initialized eagerly (before line 432) or lazily inside `startServer()` at ~line 5018+ (`viewbotService`, `global.randomStreamRotationService`, `global.viewBotURLService`), and what its destination is in 15B.2. The lazy-service closures are the load-bearing hazard: helpers that close over them can't be extracted until either (a) the destination service accepts those deps as args, or (b) the lazy init moves earlier in startup. Three helpers are affected — `getStreamerDisplayName` (reads `global.randomStreamRotationService` + `global.viewBotURLService` + `viewbotService`), `enrichStreamStatus` (indirectly, via `getStreamerDisplayName`), and `verifyAndEmitStreamReady` (indirectly). Largest cluster: the ViewBot HTTP admin bridge (15B.3.e) covering `viewbot/*`, `test-stream/*`, `viewbot-manager/*`, `viewbot-webrtc/*`, `viewbot-client/*`, `simple-rotation/*`, `viewbot/rotation/*`, `viewbot-client/debug/*`, and `streaming-method/*` — ~50 handlers across lines 1762–2585. - **Expand `no-console.test.js` to cover `server/index.js`, `server/sockets/`, `server/config/` + per-line `// console-allowed:` skip; add `_traceId` to `ModerationNotifier` (4 emits); document `ViewerCountNotifier`'s deliberate exclusion in-code (PR 15A.3, Phase 15A — closes Phase 15A, applies [ADR-0020](docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md)).** Third and final PR of Phase 15A. Three concerns land together; all short. **(1) Regression-test scope expansion.** [`server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js`](server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js) is rewritten to scan the full `server/` JS surface that Phase 15A's three sweeps shipped: `services`, `routes`, `bootstrap`, `middleware`, `database`, **`sockets`**, **`config`**, and **`index.js`**. The previous test (from PR 12.3) only scanned the first five — the 652 callsites the post-Phase-14 audit found at HEAD lived in the three directories the test deliberately omitted. The expanded test now reads each candidate file line-by-line (rather than just the `grep -l` file-name check the previous test used) so it can implement the **per-line `// console-allowed:` marker skip**: any `console.*` callsite whose *immediately preceding* line carries the literal `// console-allowed:` substring is skipped. This is the escape hatch for the two `uncaughtException` / `unhandledRejection` fallbacks at `server/index.js:5808` / `:5816` (introduced by PR 15A.2) where raw `console.error` is genuinely needed — if pino itself faulted, we still want stderr output to land before the process exits. The marker is a *grep* / *test* convention, not an eslint exception (the repo has no eslint config); it is the single source of truth for "this site is the explicit exception, not a regression". **(2) `_traceId` propagation to `ModerationNotifier`.** PR 12.3 wired `_traceId` into `StreamNotifier` and `BuffNotifier`'s emits via the conditional-spread pattern (`{ ...payload, ...(_traceId !== undefined && { _traceId }) }`) but silently left `ModerationNotifier` without the propagation. This PR closes the gap: `ModerationNotifier` now imports `{ getTraceId }` from `bootstrap/trace-context` and conditionally spreads `_traceId` onto all four emit payloads (`moderation-event-created` @ line ~60, `moderation-action-taken` @ ~78, `moderation-streamer-banner` @ ~101, `moderation-bot-output-dropped` @ ~126). The `moderation-streamer-banner` site is structurally different from its peers — its payload spreads fields directly (`event_id`, `transcript_excerpt`, `categories`, `appeal_url`) rather than wrapping in `{ event }`. Adding `_traceId` is a safe key-addition (receivers consume the named fields they care about; any client that ignored unknown keys before still does). Conditional spread preserves the absent-when-undefined property — exact-equality test assertions in `server/tests/services/ModerationNotifier.test.js` continue to pass (13/13). **(3) `ViewerCountNotifier` exclusion comment** — the deliberate non-propagation that PR 12.3 documented only in its commit body. `ViewerCountNotifier.broadcast` emits a bare integer (`io.emit('viewer-count-update', count)`), not an object; promoting the payload to `{ count, _traceId }` would break every client consumer that destructures `count` directly. This PR adds a 5-line in-file comment at the emit site documenting the exclusion and the migration path (separate breaking-change PR with client coordination) so anyone reading the code can see it without `git log`. **Phase 15A honesty (per the plan's locked decision)**: PR 15A.3 closes the gap created by **PR 12.3 (`fbb543e`, _"tail sweep + `_traceId` propagation + CI check"_)**. The original PR claimed _"Tail `console.*` sweep: 1664 → 0 in `server/`"_ but left **652 callsites at HEAD** (367 in `server/index.js`, 256 across `server/sockets/`, 29 in `server/config/`) — all in directories the regression test it shipped (`server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js`) deliberately omitted. The claim was *technically true for the test's scope*, but not for `server/` as a whole. PR 15A.1 swept `sockets/` (296), PR 15A.2 swept `index.js` + `config/webrtc.config.js` (372 + 2), and this PR (15A.3) expands the regression test so the gap can't reopen — the test now covers every directory the sweep touched, and any future PR re-introducing a stray `console.*` will fail it. The CI workflow grep that PR 12.3's title also promised was never added; the maintainer's intentional design (per ADR-0020's "How to verify") was that this Jest test is the one enforcement seam, and Phase 15 keeps it that way (adding a parallel workflow grep would create two sources of truth, one of which would silently drift). **Live verification of the marker mechanism**: during this PR's preparation, a `console.log` was injected at the end of `server/sockets/DrawingHandler.js` and the test was run — it failed with `Found 1 console.* callsite(s) in scope` pointing at `server/sockets/DrawingHandler.js:48`. The injection was then prepended with `// console-allowed: smoke test marker`, the test was re-run, and it passed. The file was reverted to its post-15A.1 state before the commit. **Diff**: `server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js` -38 / +69 (new per-line walker, expanded scope list, marker-skip logic, updated docstring); `server/services/ModerationNotifier.js` -4 / +13 (require for `getTraceId`, four `_traceId` spreads, three-line code comment on the `streamer-banner` distinct-shape rationale); `server/services/ViewerCountNotifier.js` -0 / +5 (in-file exclusion comment); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js` passes (1/1, expanded scope); `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/services/ModerationNotifier.test.js` passes (13/13, exact-equality assertions preserved by conditional-spread); `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/services/ViewerCountNotifier.test.js` passes (6/6). **Risk**: LOW (per Phase 15 plan). Each of the three concerns is small and behaviour-preserving except where the test expands enforcement scope and the four `ModerationNotifier` payloads gain an optional `_traceId` key. **Phase 15A closes** with this PR. All `console.*` in `server/` outside `server/bootstrap/logger.js` and the two `uncaughtException` markers is gone; all four production notifiers either carry `_traceId` (StreamNotifier, BuffNotifier, ModerationNotifier) or have an in-code exclusion comment (ViewerCountNotifier); the regression test gates every directory the sweep covered. **Phase 15 status**: 3/9 PRs done. Next: **Phase 15B opens** — `server/index.js` decomposition starting with PR 15B.1 (inventory + closure audit; read-only triage).

- **`console.*` → namespaced pino sweep, `server/index.js` + `server/config/webrtc.config.js` (PR 15A.2, Phase 15A — applies [ADR-0020](docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md)).** Second PR of Phase 15A. Closes the largest remaining bucket from the PR 12.3 (`fbb543e`) gap audit: 372 `console.*` callsites in `server/index.js` (370 swept + 2 retained as marker-allowed fallbacks) + 2 callsites in `server/config/webrtc.config.js` (both swept). `server/index.js` was the canonical "logger imported but unused" file at the Phase 11 close; after this PR it is a logger-first orchestrator with ~370 `logger.*` calls and exactly 2 explicit-marker `console.error` fallbacks. Solo PR per Phase 15 plan — would conflict with any concurrent `index.js` work. **Verb mapping** identical to PR 15A.1: `console.log → logger.info`, `console.{error,warn,info,debug}` mechanical one-to-one. **Existing `const logger = require('./bootstrap/logger');` at `index.js:18` upgraded** to `.child({ svc: 'index' })` so every line from the orchestrator file carries the `"svc":"index"` binding for production log filtering (matches the per-file child-logger convention from PR 12.2). **Two `console.error` fallbacks deliberately retained**: the `uncaughtException` handler (`server/index.js:5808`) and `unhandledRejection` handler (`:5816`) emit raw `console.error` because if pino itself faulted, we still want stderr output to land. The conversion happened in passes: the first mechanical regex pass converted single-identifier second operands; a second pass handled `err.message` / `error.stack` shapes (promoting to the full Error object under the `err` key for pino stack serialisation — reviewer-flagged correctness fix carried forward from PR 15A.1) and member-access shapes (`response.data` → `{ data: response.data }`, `req.file.filename` → `{ filename: req.file.filename }`, etc.), and a handful by hand for multi-line object-literal second operands (`logger.info('msg:', { ... })` → `logger.info({ ... }, 'msg')`) and the one 3-operand site at `:1427` (`'Converting', fileExt, 'to Safari-compatible AVIF:', filename` → `{ fileExt, filename }, 'Converting to Safari-compatible AVIF'`). **`server/config/webrtc.config.js`** gets a `child({ svc: 'webrtc.config' })` logger (the file is module-loaded at startup before route setup; its two emits — one error path for an invalid `WEBRTC_BACKEND` env value, one info line for the resolved backend — both carry the new `svc` binding). **Behaviour preservation**: every callsite that emitted a log pre-PR still emits one post-PR; transport changes from `process.stdout`-via-`console` to pino JSON. The trace-context mixin from PR 12.3 picks up `traceId` automatically on emits from inside HTTP-route scopes. **Zero `console.*` callsites remain in `server/index.js` and `server/config/webrtc.config.js` outside the two marker-allowed fallbacks** — verified by `grep -nE "console\.(log|error|warn|info|debug)" server/index.js server/config/webrtc.config.js` (returns exactly 2 lines: the marker-allowed uncaughtException + unhandledRejection sites). **Diff**: `server/index.js` modified (+2 lines for the `// console-allowed:` markers on both fallback sites; 370 mechanical `console.X(` → `logger.Y(` substitutions; 1 callback-rewrite at `:5557`; 1 comment-text fix at `:5547`; ~140 single-line + multi-line structured-form rewrites totalling **149 `logger.X({` openings** at HEAD; 1 logger-import upgrade to a child logger at `:18`; 1 reviewer-fix stack-binding at `:5580` — `${e.message}` template embed → `{ err: e, name }, 'service stop() failed'`); `server/config/webrtc.config.js` modified (+2 lines: child-logger require + a small message-text reflow for the structured-form bind); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. (The "149" is the actual count of `logger.X({` openings in `server/index.js` post-PR — the structured-form precise breakdown given upstream is approximate; the count of interest is the in-source `{`-prefix invariant.) **Tests**: `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js` passes (1/1, scope unchanged from main); `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/bootstrap/` passes (3 suites, 70/70). **Risk**: MEDIUM per Phase 15 plan — large single-file diff.
