- **`console.*` → namespaced pino sweep, `server/sockets/` (PR 15A.1, Phase 15A — applies [ADR-0020](docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md)).** First PR of Phase 15A (observability sweep, honestly — recovery from the PR 12.3 (`fbb543e`) gap audited post-Phase-14). PR 12.3 claimed "Tail `console.*` sweep: 1664 → 0 in `server/`"; the claim was true for the directories its companion test (`server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js`) checks (`services / routes / bootstrap / middleware / database`) but **652 callsites remained** at HEAD across `server/sockets/`, `server/index.js`, and `server/config/`, all in directories the test deliberately omitted. PR 15A.1 sweeps the `server/sockets/` subset (296 callsites across 9 files); PR 15A.2 will sweep `server/index.js` + `server/config/`; PR 15A.3 will expand the test's directory list so the gap can't reopen. **Files swept** (9, count = `console.*` at HEAD): `StreamHandler.js` (103), `ViewBotHandler.js` (83), `MediaSoupHandler.js` (52), `DisconnectHandler.js` (19), `GameHandler.js` (16), `BuffHandler.js` (9), `EffectHandler.js` (8), `AdminHandler.js` (5), `DrawingHandler.js` (1). **Audit-vs-HEAD drift, named**: the Phase 15 plan's audit (`phase-15.md:61`) estimated `MediaSoupHandler.js` at 41 and listed 8 files (omitting `DrawingHandler.js`). At HEAD, MediaSoup was 52 and DrawingHandler had 1 callsite — accounted for as 9 files / 296 callsites in this PR. Each file now imports a module-scoped child logger via `const logger = require('../bootstrap/logger').child({ svc: '<HandlerName>' });` placed above `module.exports`. **Verb mapping** (per Phase 15 plan's explicit instruction): `console.error(` → `logger.error(`, `console.warn(` → `logger.warn(`, `console.info(` → `logger.info(`, `console.debug(` → `logger.debug(`, **`console.log(` → `logger.info(`**. This last mapping is a **deliberate divergence from PR 12.2/12.3's `console.log → logger.debug` choice**: PR 12.2's conservative-to-debug choice would have silenced socket-handler operational logs in production (prod default `LOG_LEVEL=info` per [`server/bootstrap/logger.js`](server/bootstrap/logger.js) gates `.debug` out), and the socket-handler logs are the spine of "what just happened on this stream" diagnostics. The Phase 15 plan chose `→ logger.info` to preserve pre-sweep production visibility byte-for-byte. The result is a mixed-level convention across the swept tree (services on `.debug`, sockets on `.info`) — an operational-tuning artefact, not a future correctness issue; the services-side `.debug` calls can be promoted to `.info` case-by-case in later operational tuning if their visibility is missed. **Pino structured form** mandated by Phase 15 plan for multi-operand callsites (the "queryable logs" point of the sweep): `console.log('msg:', value)` → `logger.info({ value }, 'msg')`, with the trailing colon stripped from the message (it lives in the binding now). 69 sites were converted to structured form during the sweep — 56 by mechanical regex (single-identifier second-operand, optionally an Error-shaped name like `err`/`error`/`*Error` which gets bound under the `err` key for pino's stack-serialisation), 13 by hand (typed-expression second operands like `typeof callback`, `JSON.stringify(data)`, `Array.from(socket.rooms)`, `error.message`, `streamService.getCurrentStreamer()`, `!!streamService.getCurrentStreamer()`, member accesses like `data.streamConfig`, and one 3-operand site at `ViewBotHandler.js:295` — `producer trace` events emit `{ traceType, traceInfo }`). Single-argument callsites (template literals with interpolated state) stay as-is — the interpolated identifiers are already inline-traceable. **Behaviour preservation**: every callsite that emitted a log pre-PR still emits one post-PR; transport changes from `process.stdout`-via-`console` to pino JSON via the shared logger module. The `svc:'<HandlerName>'` binding lands on every line for production log-aggregator filtering (e.g. `"svc":"StreamHandler"` for join-as-viewer / request-to-stream events; `"svc":"MediaSoupHandler"` for WebRTC signalling; etc.). The trace-context mixin from PR 12.3 picks up the request `traceId` automatically on lines emitted inside an HTTP-route scope — sockets that fire in response to an authenticated HTTP-originated event will now carry both `svc` and `traceId` in their JSON output for free. **Zero `console.*` callsites remain in `server/sockets/`** — verified by `grep -rcE "console\.(log|error|warn|info|debug)" server/sockets/` (each file reports `0`). The regression test (`server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js`) still passes — it currently doesn't check `server/sockets/`, but it also reports zero violations elsewhere; PR 15A.3 will expand its directory list to include `server/sockets/`, `server/index.js`, and `server/config/` so the gate forecloses re-introduction. **Test impact**: `server/tests/sockets/AdminHandler.test.js` continues to pass (its `jest.spyOn(console, 'log' / 'error')` calls become noise-suppression scaffolding with zero spied calls — same pattern as the 16 other test files PR 12.2 left untouched). No test file required migration. **Diff**: 9 socket-handler files modified (+9 lines for the logger-require headers; 290 mechanical `console.X(` → `logger.Y(` substitutions; 69 single-line structured-form rewrites for multi-operand sites (the 3-operand site at `ViewBotHandler.js:295` collapses to one structured-form call with `traceType` + `traceInfo` bindings); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry). Net change per file: roughly +1 line (the require header). **Tests**: `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js` passes (1/1); `npx jest --config config/jest/jest.config.js server/tests/sockets/` passes (9/9). **Risk**: LOW (per Phase 15 plan). The sweep is mechanical; the structured-form pass is single-line-deterministic with the script's manual-fix list reviewed by hand; the level divergence from PR 12.2 is documented above and is in the direction of preserving prod visibility, not suppressing it. **Reviewer subagent pass**: Phase 15 plan flags this PR as eligible for a reviewer pass but lists 15A.2 (large `index.js` diff) as the **required** one; PR 15A.1's mechanical shape and unit-test coverage are sufficient signals here. **Phase 15 status**: 1/9 PRs done. Next: PR 15A.2 sweeps `server/index.js` + `server/config/webrtc.config.js` (~376 callsites, solo PR — conflicts with any concurrent `index.js` work).

### Fixed
- **OpenAI key DB-fallback for Stage 3 (text + image moderation) — `openai_config` table + boot resolver + admin endpoints (PR-M8, follow-up to [ADR-0021](docs/architecture/adr/0021-omni-image-moderation.md)).** Symmetric with the Groq Stage 2 DB-fallback hotfix that landed in `36cfa17`. Discovered while smoke-testing OmniImageMod on the live install: the operator's pattern is to keep API keys in DB (admin-managed via `/admin/groq/config`) rather than env, but `ModerationStage3` only read `OPENAI_API_KEY` from `process.env`. Net effect: **the existing text-moderation Stage 3 had been silently degraded since PR-M3 shipped** — every Stage 2 risk-level=3 verdict routed to `admin_review` instead of triggering the 2-of-2 HIGH agreement auto-ban gate, because Stage 3 reported `degraded: 'no_api_key'` on every call. OmniImageMod's image-moderation path (which uses a second Stage 3 instance per ADR-0021) would have inherited the same silent failure the moment `image_moderation_enabled=1` was flipped. **Schema**: new `openai_config` table in `ai-moderation-schema.sql` mirroring `groq_config`'s shape (singleton id=1, `enabled`, `api_key`, `updated_at`, `updated_by`). Seed row inserted by `_applySchema` on boot. **Resolver in `server/index.js`** (around the ModerationStage3 construction): `OPENAI_API_KEY` env → `openai_config.api_key WHERE enabled=1` DB → null. Same priority chain as the PR-M7 Groq fix. Returns the same key to BOTH `moderationStage3` (text) and `moderationStage3Image` (image, ADR-0021) so the two pipelines share configuration but keep their independent circuit-breaker state. **Boot logs**: `✅ ModerationStage3: OpenAI key loaded from openai_config table (env unset)` when the DB path fires; `⚠️ ModerationStage3: no OpenAI key in env OR openai_config — Stage 3 (text + image) will be skipped` when both are empty. **Admin endpoints**: `GET /admin/openai/status` (returns `enabled`, `hasKey`, `keyLength`, `keyPrefix`, `updated_at`, `updated_by`, `envKeyPresent` — never echoes the full key value) and `POST /admin/openai/config` (accepts `enabled` and/or `apiKey` independently; dynamic UPDATE so the caller can flip enabled without re-sending the key and vice versa; the response includes a `note` reminding the operator that the boot-time resolver reads the row ONCE on startup so a server restart is required for a new key to take effect). Both behind `adminKeyAuth` (X-Admin-Key), matching the `/admin/groq/*` precedent. **Tests**: no new unit tests, matching the PR-M7 Groq DB-fallback fix's precedent ("validated by production verification rather than a unit test — the change is a straight inline DB read into the env-fallback chain"). The four existing Moderation suites continue to pass unchanged. **Risk**: LOW — purely additive, no schema-incompatible changes (the existing CREATE-IF-NOT-EXISTS + INSERT-OR-IGNORE patterns are idempotent), no behavior change for installs that already have `OPENAI_API_KEY` in env (the env path still wins). **Operator path**: either (a) keep using env (already-working installs need no migration), or (b) POST to `/admin/openai/config` with the key + `enabled: true` and restart the server. The restart is intentional — the resolver runs once at boot to keep the Stage 3 instances stateless. **Honesty**: this PR was scoped after the OmniImageMod PR series merged because the OmniImageMod smoke test discovered the silently-degraded text Stage 3. The CHANGELOG entry for OmniImageMod (below, under Added) and ADR-0021 both correctly described the BEHAVIORAL design but didn't flag this configuration gap because Stage 3 *appeared* wired correctly when read from the code (it reads `process.env.OPENAI_API_KEY`); the gap was a runtime/operations issue, not a code issue.

### Added
- **Schema migrations layout — inline ALTER TABLE block extracted to numbered migration files ([ADR-0022](docs/architecture/adr/0022-schema-migrations-layout.md), PR 14.1, Phase 14 — closes Phase 14).** Single PR of Phase 14 (schema cleanup). The 21 inline `ALTER TABLE ... ADD COLUMN` (and one `DROP COLUMN`) calls in `server/database/database.js` — interleaved across ~600 lines of `initializeDatabase()`, half guarded by `PRAGMA table_info(...)` lookups and half by raw catch-duplicate-column, depending on which week the column was added — move out into nine numbered files under `server/migrations/2026MMDDHHMM-<description>.js`. The bootstrap shrinks ~200 lines (`database.js` was 959, now 759). A small runner ([`server/migrations/_runner.js`](server/migrations/_runner.js)) enumerates files matching `^\d{12}-[a-z0-9-]+\.js$` in lexicographic filename order and invokes each module's exported `run(db, logger)` from **inside the bootstrap's `db.serialize()` block**, immediately after every `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` queues — so migration ALTERs execute on the same handle in the same serialized order they did pre-PR. The runner exposes two helpers — `addColumn(db, table, column, definition, logger)` (ALTER + catch "duplicate column") and `dropColumn(db, table, column, logger)` (ALTER + catch "no such column") — that consolidate the idiom each migration would otherwise re-implement. **Filename convention**: `2026MMDDHHMM-<short-kebab-desc>.js`; the 12-digit prefix is what makes lexicographic = chronological. **Legacy ad-hoc scripts ignored**: 20 pre-Phase-14 files (`add-avatar-description.js`, `setup-viewbot-tables.js`, `migrate-points-system.js`, etc.) keep sitting in `server/migrations/` and continue to be invoked by their existing ad-hoc paths (`setup-viewbot-tables` is still required via `setTimeout(1500)` from `database.js`); the runner regex deliberately excludes them — their effects are already baked into deployed DBs, retroactively converting them risks side effects we cannot enumerate. **No `schema_migrations` tracking table**: per ADR-0022 we accept paying one no-op `ALTER` per migration per cold boot in exchange for zero bug surface around tracking-table drift. At single-host single-tenant scale (~30 tables) the per-boot cost is well under one millisecond. **The nine migrations**: `202605270001-users-add-admin-flags.js` (is_admin/is_banned/is_moderator on users), `202605270002-user-stats-drop-legacy-points.js` (DROP COLUMN points — `user_stats.points_balance` is the authoritative balance source since the `migrate-points-system` migration), `202605270003-user-stats-add-chat-color.js`, `202605270004-items-add-buff-properties.js` (duration_seconds, effect_data, stack_behavior), `202605270005-chatbot-message-history-add-moviebot-columns.js` (exact_prompt, message_type, content, metadata — the MovieBot logging extension), `202605270006-chatbot-config-add-llm-model.js`, `202605270007-chatbots-add-bot-flags.js` (use_assigned_name, llm_model, moviebot_enabled, vision_bot_enabled), `202605270008-users-add-vision-audit-optout.js`, `202605270009-recordings-add-session-and-user.js` (recordings.session_id, recordings.user_id, recording_events.user_id). **Bit-identical schema guarantee**: PR-14.1's MEDIUM-risk rating is earned by a committed fixture (`server/tests/fixtures/schema-snapshot-pre-pr-14-1.json`) that is `PRAGMA table_info` for every user table the **pre-PR** bootstrap produced — captured against `:memory:` by booting the unmodified pre-PR `database.js` through a sqlite3 monkey-patch BEFORE making any changes, so the fixture is a true pre-state record, not a fabrication. The new test suite [`server/tests/database/migrations.runner.test.js`](server/tests/database/migrations.runner.test.js) (8 tests) boots the post-PR `database.js` against `:memory:` from inside Jest, waits 2.5 s for the bootstrap's two `setTimeout`-deferred bits to settle (recording-index creation @1000ms which depends on the `recordings.session_id` and `recordings.user_id` columns the migration runner backfills; ViewBot tables @1500ms via the existing legacy `setup-viewbot-tables.js`), snapshots the resulting schema, and asserts `expect(snapshot).toEqual(fixture)`. The snapshot must be empty — any drift fails the test. **Test breakdown**: (i) **filename-discovery** (2 tests) — pins that `listMigrationFiles()` returns only the 9 new files in lexicographic order, and explicitly does NOT pick up the 20 legacy `add-X.js` / `setup-X-tables.js` / `migrate-X.js` files; (ii) **legacy-DB backfill** (3 tests) — constructs a pre-Phase-14 minimal schema (tables exist but WITHOUT the columns the migrations add), runs the runner, asserts all 21 columns appear with correct types/defaults (`is_admin` is `BOOLEAN DEFAULT '0'`, `stack_behavior` is `TEXT DEFAULT 'replace'`, `message_type` is `TEXT DEFAULT 'chat'`, `llm_model` on `chatbot_config` is `TEXT DEFAULT 'mistral'`); also asserts the legacy `user_stats.points` column gets dropped; zero error-log calls; (iii) **fresh-DB idempotency** (2 tests) — constructs a fresh-bootstrap schema (CREATE TABLE statements that ALREADY include all the columns the migrations would add) and asserts the runner logs zero errors (every ALTER hits the duplicate-column catch path) and is safe to run twice (the snapshot of the schema after one run equals the snapshot after two runs); (iv) **bit-identical bootstrap** (1 test) — the load-bearing guarantee described above. **Diff**: `server/database/database.js` -209 / +9 (21 ALTER blocks + the four `PRAGMA table_info` wrappers removed; one `require('../migrations/_runner')` + one `migrationRunner.runAll(db, logger)` call added inside `db.serialize()`); `server/migrations/_runner.js` +97 (new); 9 × `server/migrations/202605270XXX-*.js` ~10–20 LoC each (new); `server/tests/database/migrations.runner.test.js` +280 (new, 8 tests); `server/tests/fixtures/schema-snapshot-pre-pr-14-1.json` +2606 (new fixture, 39 tables); [`docs/architecture/adr/0022-schema-migrations-layout.md`](docs/architecture/adr/0022-schema-migrations-layout.md) (new); `docs/architecture/adr/README.md` +2 (backfills missing 0021 OmniImageMod row that PR #157 didn't add to the index, AND adds new 0022 row — same scope-creep pattern PR 12.1 used to add 0019); `docs/architecture/plans/phases-6-plus.md` -4 / +5 (Phase 14 section corrected: Risk LOW → MEDIUM matching the actual assessment; ADR-0020 → ADR-0022 — the original plan text and the Phase 13 handoff both got the ADR slot wrong because OmniImageMod's PR #157 took 0021 in parallel; "~30 inline ALTERs" → "21" the actual count). **Tests**: unit suite — **1117/1117 in parallel** (was 1109; +8 from the new test file), wall-clock ~18 s — under the Phase 13 budget. Under `--runInBand` the suite reports 1116/1117 with one teardown-race failure that **oscillates between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js`** depending on Jest worker order — this is the well-documented pre-existing flake (database-better.test.js passes 18/18 in isolation; transaction.test.js passes in isolation; the failure only fires when the two are in the same worker on the same run), unchanged from main. Integration suite (`npm run test:integration`) — **124/124, 3 s** (the 62 tests double-count because `jest.integration.config.js` does not exclude `.claude/worktrees/` — pre-existing config gap, NOT introduced by this PR; out of scope). **Risk**: MEDIUM as briefed — the schema bootstrap is load-bearing; this PR earns the rating with the bit-identical fixture test. **Live smoke** (maintainer-gated, this autonomous agent cannot run `npm run dev`): (a) **fresh DB** — delete or move `server/data/onestreamer.db`, run `npm start`, expect a working schema in one boot with no manual `npm run migrate` step (this PR preserves the single-command fresh-clone story); (b) **existing DB** — `npm start` against the live `server/data/onestreamer.db`, expect zero log lines starting with `Migration ALTER TABLE ... failed` or `Migration ALTER TABLE DROP COLUMN failed` (every migration converges to no-op on a DB that already has the columns); (c) **PRAGMA spot-check** — `sqlite3 server/data/onestreamer.db "PRAGMA table_info(users)"` and compare against pre-PR shape, then likewise for `chatbots`, `chatbot_message_history`, `items`, `user_stats`, `recordings`, `recording_events` — column lists must be identical. **Phase 14 closure**: success criterion met — new schema changes are written as numbered migration files, not as inline ALTERs in `database.js`; `database.js` shrunk ~200 lines; `npm start` against an empty DB produces a working schema with no manual steps; a bit-identical-schema regression test pins `PRAGMA table_info` for every user table. **Things deliberately deferred** (per ADR-0022): converting the 20 legacy ad-hoc migration scripts to the new convention (their effects are baked into deployed DBs; re-running data-shape `migrate-*.js` files under the new runner risks side effects); a `schema_migrations` tracking table (not warranted at this scale; idempotency-per-boot is cheaper and has zero bug surface); migrating the bootstrap to an async-await shape that returns a promise after migrations complete (every consumer that `require('./database')` and uses the db handle immediately depends on the current callback-queued-serialize shape — a bigger refactor than Phase 14's scope). **Phase 14 is the last numbered phase in the original Phases 6+ roadmap.** The Phase 13 discovery's long-tail untested-services list (DrawingService, ThrowingService, cooldown subsystem) remains as a potential Phase 15+ if the maintainer wants to spend more test-coverage effort; none rated high-risk, deferrable indefinitely.
- **Recording pipeline integration tests — RecordingUploadScheduler retry contract + cleanup-vs-upload race end-to-end (PR 13.3, Phase 13 — closes Phase 13).** Third and final PR of Phase 13 (test-coverage hardening). Stacked on PR 13.2 (which is stacked on PR 13.1); once both merge, GitHub auto-rebases this to `main`. Adds **30 integration tests across 2 new files** under `server/tests/integration/`, both running under the `USE_BETTER_SQLITE3=true|false` matrix via PR 13.1's `forEachBackend` helper. The fixture helper at `server/tests/integration/_helpers/db-fixture.js` is extended with `bootstrapRecordingSchema` + `seedRecordingSession` so the recording-pipeline tables (`recording_sessions`, `session_chat_messages`, `admin_review_settings`) get the same one-shot construction the money-flow tables got in PR 13.1. **(a) `recording-upload.scheduler.integration.test.js` (new, 16 tests across both backends)** — end-to-end exercise of the B2-upload pipeline at the `RecordingUploadScheduler` boundary. Real scheduler over real in-memory SQLite over a real `tmpdir` for local segment files, with `B2StorageService.processAndUploadSession` mocked at the module level (slot pattern + `mockB2Slot.*` naming so jest.mock's factory-scope rules accept the reference). Six scenario buckets per backend: **(i) happy path** — scheduled session becomes due, uploadSession runs, B2 mock reports success, the recording_sessions row is updated (b2_file_id, b2_file_name, file_size_bytes, status='uploaded'), local files are removed, queue entry cleared. **(ii) failure + retry — the brief's B2-retry contract** — B2 returns error, scheduler reverts status to 'completed', **leaves local files in place** (load-bearing invariant that the retry contract is built on — without it the retry has nothing to upload from), session re-queued for retry 30 minutes later (queue scheduledTime asserted within ±2s of `now + 30*60*1000`); a second processPendingUploads cycle with B2 back online drives the row to terminal 'uploaded' state — proves the retry path *actually retries*, not just logs. **(iii) idempotency** — session with `b2_file_id` already set returns success without invoking B2. **(iv) missing local files** — uploadSession returns the expected failure when the directory was deleted before the upload could run; row stays in 'completed' (no spurious 'processing' update). **(v) forceUpload** — bypasses queue scheduling, runs immediately, returns the same shape. **(vi) processPendingUploads partial batch** — two queued sessions, only the past-scheduledTime one is processed; the future-scheduledTime one is untouched. **(b) `recording-cleanup.upload-race.integration.test.js` (new, 14 tests across both backends)** — integration-level proof of PR 8.4 (#138)'s race fix. The existing `server/tests/services/RecordingCleanupScheduler.upload-race.test.js` (9 tests) pins the SQL filter shape at the DB-mock seam; this file complements (does NOT duplicate) by running real `RecordingCleanupScheduler` + real `RecordingUploadScheduler` against the same in-memory connection. If either scheduler's SQL drifts in a way the unit-test regex didn't anticipate (column rename, table rename, different bind shape), the real DB catches it here. Six scenario buckets per backend pinning the PR 8.4 contract: **(i) un-uploaded session past retention BUT within retry window survives cleanup** — the headline contract; pre-PR-8.4 this row would have been deleted; **(ii) past-retry-window un-uploaded session IS reaped by the safety valve** — without an upper bound a permanently-broken B2 would leak rows forever; **(iii) uploaded session past retention is deleted (baseline path unchanged + asserts B2.deleteFile is called with the right `b2_file_name`)**; **(iv) fresh sub-retention sessions never touched**; **(v) mixed batch — four sessions covering all four corners**, asserts only the safety-valve + uploaded sessions are deleted; **(vi) getStatus / runCleanup count parity** — pins that the `(b2_file_id IS NOT NULL OR start_time < extendedCutoff)` guard mirrored in `getStatus`'s `expiredCount` SELECT stays in lockstep with the actual `runCleanup` deletion count (PR 8.4 introduced both; a future drift could cause the admin status panel to lie). **End-to-end recovery story**: a final test composes both schedulers — a session past retention but within retry window with B2 down survives the first cleanup tick, then `upload.forceUpload(sessionId)` succeeds (B2 mock comes back), and the row reaches terminal 'uploaded' state with `b2_file_id` stamped. Proves the combined PR 8.4 (DB guard) + PR 2.6 (FS guard) protection actually delivers the no-loss recovery the runbook promises. **Diff**: `server/tests/integration/_helpers/db-fixture.js` +100 (adds `bootstrapRecordingSchema` + `seedRecordingSession`); `server/tests/integration/recording-upload.scheduler.integration.test.js` +280 (new); `server/tests/integration/recording-cleanup.upload-race.integration.test.js` +260 (new); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: unit suite under `--runInBand` — **1081/1082** (unchanged from PR 13.2's tip; the same 1 pre-existing teardown-race flake). Integration suite (`npm run test:integration`) — **62/62**, wall-clock 2.2 s (was 32 from PR 13.1 + 30 added here). No production code modified. **Risk**: LOW per Phase 13 brief. The new tests are additive; the `mockB2Slot` slot-pattern naming is the same trick PR 13.1 used to satisfy Jest's factory-scope variable allowlist (only `mock*`-prefixed module-scope vars are allowed inside `jest.mock(...)` factories — the existing PR 13.1 code uses `dbSlot` because it's read-only in the factory body, not assigned). **Live smoke**: N/A (tests-only PR). **Phase 13 closure**. Success criterion met — suite splits into unit (`npm test` — under 20 s budget) + integration (`npm run test:integration` — 2.2 s). Money flow (PR 13.1), ViewBot lifecycle (PR 13.2), and recording pipeline (PR 13.3) surfaces all have integration coverage. **Final combined suite count**: 1081 unit + 62 integration = **1143 tests** (vs the brief's "~1300+" target — short by ~150; the brief allowed Phase 13 to ship without exhausting every untested surface, and the load-bearing surfaces are covered. Three more wins remain for a future phase: cooldown / DrawingService / ThrowingService — none rated high-risk by the original Phase 13 discovery). **Phase 14 next** (schema cleanup — extracts the ~30 inline ALTER TABLE calls in `server/database/database.js` into numbered migration scripts; single PR, MEDIUM risk; ADR-0021 per the corrected ADR-slot numbering at Phase 12 close).
- **ViewBot lifecycle tests — watchdog extensions + ViewBotClientService PR-11.2 regression gate + post-extraction ViewBotInstance contract (PR 13.2, Phase 13).** Second PR of Phase 13 (test-coverage hardening). Stacked on PR 13.1 (needs the worktrees exclusion that PR 13.1 baked into `jest.config.js` for clean local runs). Three test files land in this PR, all unit-scoped (no integration directory churn): **(a) `UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog.test.js` extended +6 tests** — the existing 10 tests from PR 8.2 cover the load-bearing watchdog behaviors (fires on stalled, doesn't fire when fresh/null/stopped, cleared on stop/shutdown, doesn't restart the rotation). The 6 added tests close discovered gaps: **(1)** fires on EVERY consecutive watchdog check while stalled (not one-shot) — alerting pipelines deduplicate by event identity, not by single-fire, and the runbook says "rate of `viewbot-rotation-stalled` events tells you the loop is wedged vs intermittently slow"; single-firing would mask that; **(2 + 3)** log context `realStreamerActive` toggles cleanly between false/true based on `plainRtpRotation.isRealStreamerActive()` — this is the "blocked by design" hint the operator uses to separate "code bug" from "real streamer is on, loop correctly idle"; **(4)** tolerates `plainRtpRotation.isRealStreamerActive` throwing — the `_isAnyRealStreamerActive` helper's defensive try/catch is exercised so the watchdog itself stays alive when the sub-helper fails (without the try/catch the watchdog stops logging — strictly worse); **(5)** doesn't fire when `activeRotation` is null mid-flight — the `!this.activeRotation` guard catches a raced reassignment (e.g., mode toggle in progress) that would otherwise NPE on `this.activeRotation.lastTickAt`; **(6)** uses default `maxRotationInterval=180000` when `activeRotation.settings` is absent — pins the fallback shape in the `?? 180000` coalesce. **(b) `ViewBotClientService.updateRotationSettings.test.js` (new, 12 tests)** — closes the PR 11.2 documented-history regression. PR 11.2 (#151) fixed three coupled latent bugs in the same 12-line block: `this.viewBots` → `this.activeBots` (typo TypeError'd the path), `this.startRotationCheckTimer(bot.botId)` → `bot.startRotationCheckTimer()` (wrong receiver + wrong arity), and `.filter(bot => bot.isStreaming)` → `(bot) => (typeof bot.isStreaming === 'function' ? bot.isStreaming() : bot.streaming)` (function-reference is always truthy, original filter was a no-op). PR 11.2 closed those via full-suite-green; PR 13.2 pins each contract so a future "tidy" can't re-introduce them. Coverage: `getRotationSettings` defaults, `updateRotationSettings` field propagation (all three / partial / persist via `saveRotationConfig` to the rotation-config.json path), and the **PR 11.2 bug-fix block** — empty-activeBots no-throw, streaming-ViewBotInstance restart path (isStreaming() method form — pins fixes #2 and #3), placeholder-shape support (no `isStreaming` method, just `.streaming` property — pins the `typeof === 'function'` guard from fix #3), no-orphan-call when `rotationCheckTimer` is null. Also covers `getBotIdBySocketId` — Map lookup with the placeholder/instance/no-socket cases. Construction strategy: `ViewBotClientService`'s constructor fires `initialize()` which calls `detectFFmpegPath` which `spawn`s real ffmpeg with a 3-second kill `setTimeout`; under fake timers the kill never fires, the spawned child kept the process alive, Jest hung waiting for handles. **Fix**: a one-line static-method override (`ViewBotClientService.checkFFmpegAvailability = jest.fn(async () => ({available: true, path: '/usr/bin/ffmpeg'}))`) before any test runs. The constructor also schedules un-stored-handle long-lived timers (`startCooldownCleanup` at ~30 min, `startAutoValidation`); `jest.clearAllTimers()` + explicit `stopAutoValidation()` in `afterEach` reaps them so the suite doesn't need `--forceExit`. **(c) `ViewBotInstance.contract.test.js` (new, 9 tests)** — first targeted coverage of the post-PR-11.1-extraction class (PR 11.1 split this out of `ViewBotClientService.js`, no prior tests existed for the extracted class). Coverage: **constructor state shape** (all documented fields default to null/false as the orchestrator and downstream code expect — `botId`, `config`, `serverUrl`, `mediasoupService`, `parentService`, socket/browser/page/mediaStream nulls, connection-state booleans, rotation-system fields the orchestrator's filter reads, FFmpeg/RTP transport fields, DB session fields), **rotation defaults** (hard-coded 0.31 / 5000 / 10000 fallback when `parentService` is null — same numbers `ViewBotClientService`'s constructor uses, so a standalone test/dev `ViewBotInstance` and an orchestrator-with-defaults parent see identical numbers — important so the dev scaffolding behaves like production), **parent-inherited rotation settings** (`parentService.rotationProbability` etc. thread through). Pure-function regression gates on the FFmpeg argv builders: `createAudioFFmpegArgs` throws when audioRtpPort is unallocated; produces a silent `anullsrc` input when `contentType !== 'videoFile'` with spot-checked load-bearing flags (`-re`, `lavfi`, `anullsrc=...`, `libopus`, `-b:a 128k`, `-ar 48000`, `-ac 2`, `-application voip`, `-payload_type 111`, fixed audio SSRC=22222222); embeds the allocated `audioRtpPort` into the `rtp://...` URL; honours `SERVER_HOST` env var with 127.0.0.1 fallback. `createVideoFFmpegArgs` throws when videoRtpPort is unallocated, throws when `contentType=videoFile` and the file doesn't exist. **What this PR does NOT add** (covered elsewhere or operationally smoke-tested): puppeteer/socket.io browser-tab orchestration in `startStreaming` (requires headful Chromium, lives in maintainer smoke); the FFmpeg spawn pipeline itself (real-process integration); the GStreamer pipeline path (requires `gst-launch-1.0`); the MediaSoup transport setup (requires a live SFU); the per-bot reaper integration (covered by `ProcessManager.reaper.test.js` — 16 tests since PR 8.3). **Diff**: `server/tests/services/UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog.test.js` +130 / -1 (6 new tests appended); `server/tests/services/ViewBotClientService.updateRotationSettings.test.js` +250 (new); `server/tests/services/ViewBotInstance.contract.test.js` +180 (new); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: full unit suite under `--runInBand` — **1081/1082** (+27 tests vs baseline, same 1 known pre-existing teardown-race flake). Wall-clock unchanged (still under the Phase 13 budget). Integration suite (from PR 13.1) — 32/32, 1.9 s, unchanged. **No production code modified**. **Risk**: LOW per Phase 13 brief. The new tests are additive; one cross-cutting test scaffold (the static `checkFFmpegAvailability` stub in the ViewBotClientService test) is scoped to that file via `jest.fn()` assignment after the require, so it doesn't bleed into other suites. **Live smoke**: N/A (tests-only PR). **Phase 13 status**: 2/3 PRs done. Next: PR 13.3 (recording pipeline tests — `ContinuousRecordingService` lifecycle, `RecordingCleanupScheduler` vs upload race, B2 retry).
- **Money-flow integration tests through the route layer + Jest suite split (PR 13.1, Phase 13 starts).** First PR of Phase 13 (test-coverage hardening). Two concerns land together — the suite split that the rest of Phase 13 needs as scaffolding, and the first batch of integration tests (money flow through `POST /api/shop/purchase` and `POST /api/internal/{award-points, transfer-points, admin/award-points}`). **(a) Suite split.** Phase 13's brief calls for the test suite to bifurcate so that `npm test` (unit) stays inside the **<20 s wall-clock budget** while a new `npm run test:integration` carries the heavier integration suite with no time target — integration tests are typically 10–100× slower than units, so without the split a few dozen of them would blow past the budget. Split is implemented via two Jest configs: existing [`config/jest/jest.config.js`](config/jest/jest.config.js) (unit) now `testPathIgnorePatterns`-excludes the new `server/tests/integration/` tree, and the previously-CLI-flag exclusion set (`worktrees|EgressFrameCaptureService|TranscriptionDrivenBotService|ChatBotLLMService.vision|VisionBotService`) is baked into the config so plain `npm test` works without extra flags; new sibling [`config/jest/jest.integration.config.js`](config/jest/jest.integration.config.js) matches only `**/tests/integration/**/*.test.js`, skips coverage collection (integration tests verify end-to-end behavior, not line coverage), and shares the same `setupFilesAfterEnv` as the unit config. `package.json` gains `"test:integration": "jest --config config/jest/jest.integration.config.js"` and `test:all` is updated to run unit → integration → client. **(b) Money-flow integration tests** — 32 new tests across two files, both running under the **`USE_BETTER_SQLITE3=true|false` matrix** (per Phase 13 brief's test-env-flag requirement) via a `forEachBackend(describe)` wrapper in the shared helper. **[`server/tests/integration/_helpers/db-fixture.js`](server/tests/integration/_helpers/db-fixture.js)** (new, ~180 LoC) — extracts the `makeSqlite3Primitives` / `makeBetterPrimitives` / `bootstrapMoneyFlowSchema` / `seedUserAndItem` / `forEachBackend` plumbing that was copy-pasted across `ShopService.purchaseItem.atomic.test.js` and `.realAccount.test.js` so the new integration files (and any future ones touching the same schema) stay focused on the actual HTTP round-trips. The schema is the subset of the production tables that money-flow code touches (`users`, `user_stats`, `points_transactions`, `items`, `shop_items`, `user_inventory`, `item_transactions`) with the columns the live SQL references — the single source of truth for the production schema remains `server/database/database.js`; this fixture is an integration-test approximation. **[`server/tests/integration/routes.shop.purchase.integration.test.js`](server/tests/integration/routes.shop.purchase.integration.test.js)** (new, ~250 LoC, 12 tests across both backends) covers `POST /api/shop/purchase` end-to-end: real `ShopService.purchaseItem` over real `withTransaction` over in-memory sqlite3/better-sqlite3, with `AccountService` mocked at the **database module level** (slot-pattern jest.mock — same shape as `ShopService.purchaseItem.realAccount.test.js`) so `AccountService`'s module-level `runAsync`/`getAsync` (captured at require time) route through the same in-memory connection as `ShopRepository` and the helper. Six scenarios per backend: happy-path 200 (asserts balance debit, inventory credit, two audit rows in `item_transactions` + `points_transactions`, stock decrement, single `buffNotifier.inventoryUpdated` emit with the expected payload), default-quantity behavior, 400 missing-`itemId`, 402 Insufficient-points with all side-effects suppressed, 500 max-stack-exceeded pre-tx guard with rollback, 500 + complete rollback when the audit-write step throws mid-tx (the critical regression gate — proves the route-layer 500 mapping doesn't accidentally suppress the rollback that the service-layer test from PR 7.4 proved). Auth middleware is `jest.mock`ed to a pass-through stamping `req.user = { id: 42, userId: 42, username: 'tester' }` so the route handler's auth contract is satisfied; the real middleware behavior is covered by other test files. **[`server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js`](server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js)** (new, ~270 LoC, 20 tests across both backends) covers the AccountService end-to-end paths exposed by `server/routes/internal.js`: `POST /award-points` (addPoints — 4 scenarios: happy path, 400 missing params, 401 no auth, 401 token-mismatch), `POST /transfer-points` (subtractPoints + addPoints pair — 4 scenarios: happy path with both audit rows, 400 insufficient-points pre-check, 400 send-to-self, 404 unknown recipient), `POST /admin/award-points` (is_admin DB-guard — 2 scenarios: 200 for admin, 403 for non-admin). The `internal.js` routes verify Bearer tokens via `authService.verifyToken` *inside* each handler (no middleware), so `AuthService` is jest-mocked to recognize tokens of shape `Bearer user:<id>` — keeps each test's auth context explicit at the call site. Three users seeded per test: sender (id 42, 1000 pts), recipient (id 99, 0 pts), admin (id 1, is_admin=1, 0 pts). **What this PR does NOT add (covered elsewhere or deferred to PR 13.2/13.3)**: concurrent-call atomicity tests (already covered by `AccountService.points-race.test.js`); the service-boundary atomic SQL contract (covered by `ShopService.purchaseItem.atomic.test.js` / `.realAccount.test.js` — this PR proves those guarantees survive the *route* boundary, complementing rather than duplicating); items / inventory / drawing / throw routes (separate scope, not money-flow); the `/gamble` and `/slots` routes (random-outcome paths — the underlying addPoints/subtractPoints are covered by `/award-points` and `/transfer-points`; gamble/slots add coin-flip logic on top that's not a money-flow concern); ViewBot lifecycle and recording-pipeline integration coverage (PR 13.2 and PR 13.3 respectively). **Diff**: `config/jest/jest.config.js` -1 / +18 (adds `testPathIgnorePatterns` block with the seven exclusions documented inline); `config/jest/jest.integration.config.js` +14 (new); `package.json` -1 / +2 (one new script + update `test:all`); `server/tests/integration/_helpers/db-fixture.js` +180 (new); `server/tests/integration/routes.shop.purchase.integration.test.js` +250 (new); `server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js` +270 (new); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: full unit suite under `--runInBand` with the (now config-baked) exclusion list — **1054/1055** (exact baseline match; single failure is the pre-existing teardown-race flake between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js`, unchanged). Without `--runInBand` (default parallel) — **1055/1055** (the teardown race only fires under serial execution). Wall-clock: **17.98 s** — under the 20 s budget. Integration suite (`npm run test:integration`) — **32/32**, wall-clock 2.1 s. **Risk**: LOW per Phase 13 brief. The new tests are additive; the suite split touches Jest config only (no production code); the dependency on the slot-pattern `jest.mock('../../database/database', …)` is the same pattern already proven by `ShopService.purchaseItem.realAccount.test.js` since PR 7.4. **No production code modified** — this PR ships tests and Jest scaffolding only. **Live smoke (maintainer-gated)**: N/A (tests-only PR; no behaviour change). Verify the split locally by running `npm test` (unit, should finish in ~18 s) and `npm run test:integration` (integration, should finish in ~2 s); both should pass cleanly. **Phase 13 status**: 1/3 PRs done. Next: PR 13.2 (ViewBot lifecycle tests — `UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog`, post-PR-11.1 `ViewBotInstance` + `ViewBotClientService` integration), PR 13.3 (recording pipeline tests — `ContinuousRecordingService` lifecycle, `RecordingCleanupScheduler` vs upload race, B2 retry).
- **ViewBot lifecycle tests — watchdog extensions + ViewBotClientService PR-11.2 regression gate + post-extraction ViewBotInstance contract (PR 13.2, Phase 13).** Second PR of Phase 13 (test-coverage hardening). Stacked on PR 13.1 (needs the worktrees exclusion that PR 13.1 baked into `jest.config.js` for clean local runs). Three test files land in this PR, all unit-scoped (no integration directory churn): **(a) `UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog.test.js` extended +6 tests** — the existing 10 tests from PR 8.2 cover the load-bearing watchdog behaviors (fires on stalled, doesn't fire when fresh/null/stopped, cleared on stop/shutdown, doesn't restart the rotation). The 6 added tests close discovered gaps: **(1)** fires on EVERY consecutive watchdog check while stalled (not one-shot) — alerting pipelines deduplicate by event identity, not by single-fire, and the runbook says "rate of `viewbot-rotation-stalled` events tells you the loop is wedged vs intermittently slow"; single-firing would mask that; **(2 + 3)** log context `realStreamerActive` toggles cleanly between false/true based on `plainRtpRotation.isRealStreamerActive()` — this is the "blocked by design" hint the operator uses to separate "code bug" from "real streamer is on, loop correctly idle"; **(4)** tolerates `plainRtpRotation.isRealStreamerActive` throwing — the `_isAnyRealStreamerActive` helper's defensive try/catch is exercised so the watchdog itself stays alive when the sub-helper fails (without the try/catch the watchdog stops logging — strictly worse); **(5)** doesn't fire when `activeRotation` is null mid-flight — the `!this.activeRotation` guard catches a raced reassignment (e.g., mode toggle in progress) that would otherwise NPE on `this.activeRotation.lastTickAt`; **(6)** uses default `maxRotationInterval=180000` when `activeRotation.settings` is absent — pins the fallback shape in the `?? 180000` coalesce. **(b) `ViewBotClientService.updateRotationSettings.test.js` (new, 12 tests)** — closes the PR 11.2 documented-history regression. PR 11.2 (#151) fixed three coupled latent bugs in the same 12-line block: `this.viewBots` → `this.activeBots` (typo TypeError'd the path), `this.startRotationCheckTimer(bot.botId)` → `bot.startRotationCheckTimer()` (wrong receiver + wrong arity), and `.filter(bot => bot.isStreaming)` → `(bot) => (typeof bot.isStreaming === 'function' ? bot.isStreaming() : bot.streaming)` (function-reference is always truthy, original filter was a no-op). PR 11.2 closed those via full-suite-green; PR 13.2 pins each contract so a future "tidy" can't re-introduce them. Coverage: `getRotationSettings` defaults, `updateRotationSettings` field propagation (all three / partial / persist via `saveRotationConfig` to the rotation-config.json path), and the **PR 11.2 bug-fix block** — empty-activeBots no-throw, streaming-ViewBotInstance restart path (isStreaming() method form — pins fixes #2 and #3), placeholder-shape support (no `isStreaming` method, just `.streaming` property — pins the `typeof === 'function'` guard from fix #3), no-orphan-call when `rotationCheckTimer` is null. Also covers `getBotIdBySocketId` — Map lookup with the placeholder/instance/no-socket cases. Construction strategy: `ViewBotClientService`'s constructor fires `initialize()` which calls `detectFFmpegPath` which `spawn`s real ffmpeg with a 3-second kill `setTimeout`; under fake timers the kill never fires, the spawned child kept the process alive, Jest hung waiting for handles. **Fix**: a one-line static-method override (`ViewBotClientService.checkFFmpegAvailability = jest.fn(async () => ({available: true, path: '/usr/bin/ffmpeg'}))`) before any test runs. The constructor also schedules un-stored-handle long-lived timers (`startCooldownCleanup` at ~30 min, `startAutoValidation`); `jest.clearAllTimers()` + explicit `stopAutoValidation()` in `afterEach` reaps them so the suite doesn't need `--forceExit`. **(c) `ViewBotInstance.contract.test.js` (new, 9 tests)** — first targeted coverage of the post-PR-11.1-extraction class (PR 11.1 split this out of `ViewBotClientService.js`, no prior tests existed for the extracted class). Coverage: **constructor state shape** (all documented fields default to null/false as the orchestrator and downstream code expect — `botId`, `config`, `serverUrl`, `mediasoupService`, `parentService`, socket/browser/page/mediaStream nulls, connection-state booleans, rotation-system fields the orchestrator's filter reads, FFmpeg/RTP transport fields, DB session fields), **rotation defaults** (hard-coded 0.31 / 5000 / 10000 fallback when `parentService` is null — same numbers `ViewBotClientService`'s constructor uses, so a standalone test/dev `ViewBotInstance` and an orchestrator-with-defaults parent see identical numbers — important so the dev scaffolding behaves like production), **parent-inherited rotation settings** (`parentService.rotationProbability` etc. thread through). Pure-function regression gates on the FFmpeg argv builders: `createAudioFFmpegArgs` throws when audioRtpPort is unallocated; produces a silent `anullsrc` input when `contentType !== 'videoFile'` with spot-checked load-bearing flags (`-re`, `lavfi`, `anullsrc=...`, `libopus`, `-b:a 128k`, `-ar 48000`, `-ac 2`, `-application voip`, `-payload_type 111`, fixed audio SSRC=22222222); embeds the allocated `audioRtpPort` into the `rtp://...` URL; honours `SERVER_HOST` env var with 127.0.0.1 fallback. `createVideoFFmpegArgs` throws when videoRtpPort is unallocated, throws when `contentType=videoFile` and the file doesn't exist. **What this PR does NOT add** (covered elsewhere or operationally smoke-tested): puppeteer/socket.io browser-tab orchestration in `startStreaming` (requires headful Chromium, lives in maintainer smoke); the FFmpeg spawn pipeline itself (real-process integration); the GStreamer pipeline path (requires `gst-launch-1.0`); the MediaSoup transport setup (requires a live SFU); the per-bot reaper integration (covered by `ProcessManager.reaper.test.js` — 16 tests since PR 8.3). **Diff**: `server/tests/services/UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog.test.js` +130 / -1 (6 new tests appended); `server/tests/services/ViewBotClientService.updateRotationSettings.test.js` +250 (new); `server/tests/services/ViewBotInstance.contract.test.js` +180 (new); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: full unit suite under `--runInBand` — **1081/1082** (+27 tests vs baseline, same 1 known pre-existing teardown-race flake). Wall-clock unchanged (still under the Phase 13 budget). Integration suite (from PR 13.1) — 32/32, 1.9 s, unchanged. **No production code modified**. **Risk**: LOW per Phase 13 brief. The new tests are additive; one cross-cutting test scaffold (the static `checkFFmpegAvailability` stub in the ViewBotClientService test) is scoped to that file via `jest.fn()` assignment after the require, so it doesn't bleed into other suites. **Live smoke**: N/A (tests-only PR). **Phase 13 status**: 2/3 PRs done. Next: PR 13.3 (recording pipeline tests — `ContinuousRecordingService` lifecycle, `RecordingCleanupScheduler` vs upload race, B2 retry).
