Three users seeded per test: sender (id 42, 1000 pts), recipient (id 99, 0 pts), admin (id 1, is_admin=1, 0 pts). **What this PR does NOT add (covered elsewhere or deferred to PR 13.2/13.3)**: concurrent-call atomicity tests (already covered by `AccountService.points-race.test.js`); the service-boundary atomic SQL contract (covered by `ShopService.purchaseItem.atomic.test.js` / `.realAccount.test.js` — this PR proves those guarantees survive the *route* boundary, complementing rather than duplicating); items / inventory / drawing / throw routes (separate scope, not money-flow); the `/gamble` and `/slots` routes (random-outcome paths — the underlying addPoints/subtractPoints are covered by `/award-points` and `/transfer-points`; gamble/slots add coin-flip logic on top that's not a money-flow concern); ViewBot lifecycle and recording-pipeline integration coverage (PR 13.2 and PR 13.3 respectively). **Diff**: `config/jest/jest.config.js` -1 / +18 (adds `testPathIgnorePatterns` block with the seven exclusions documented inline); `config/jest/jest.integration.config.js` +14 (new); `package.json` -1 / +2 (one new script + update `test:all`); `server/tests/integration/_helpers/db-fixture.js` +180 (new); `server/tests/integration/routes.shop.purchase.integration.test.js` +250 (new); `server/tests/integration/routes.internal.points.integration.test.js` +270 (new); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: full unit suite under `--runInBand` with the (now config-baked) exclusion list — **1054/1055** (exact baseline match; single failure is the pre-existing teardown-race flake between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js`, unchanged). Without `--runInBand` (default parallel) — **1055/1055** (the teardown race only fires under serial execution). Wall-clock: **17.98 s** — under the 20 s budget. Integration suite (`npm run test:integration`) — **32/32**, wall-clock 2.1 s. **Risk**: LOW per Phase 13 brief. The new tests are additive; the suite split touches Jest config only (no production code); the dependency on the slot-pattern `jest.mock('../../database/database', …)` is the same pattern already proven by `ShopService.purchaseItem.realAccount.test.js` since PR 7.4. **No production code modified** — this PR ships tests and Jest scaffolding only. **Live smoke (maintainer-gated)**: N/A (tests-only PR; no behaviour change). Verify the split locally by running `npm test` (unit, should finish in ~18 s) and `npm run test:integration` (integration, should finish in ~2 s); both should pass cleanly. **Phase 13 status**: 1/3 PRs done. Next: PR 13.2 (ViewBot lifecycle tests — `UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog`, post-PR-11.1 `ViewBotInstance` + `ViewBotClientService` integration), PR 13.3 (recording pipeline tests — `ContinuousRecordingService` lifecycle, `RecordingCleanupScheduler` vs upload race, B2 retry).
- **OmniImageMod — image moderation via OpenAI omni-moderation ([ADR-0021](docs/architecture/adr/0021-omni-image-moderation.md)).** Extends the existing AI-moderation pipeline (ADR-0013) to screen VisionBot screenshots through OpenAI's free omni-moderation endpoint, routing flagged frames through the same `ModerationActionArbiter` that handles transcript-text bans. Defaults to disabled. Shipped as a 3-PR series: **(1) `ModerationStage3` image input** — `classify()` accepts `{text, imageBase64, imageMime}`; backward-compatible (existing text-only callers keep the `input: "<string>"` request shape). New fast-fail validations BEFORE the fetch round-trip (`image_too_large` at 4 MB base64; `invalid_jpeg` via `/9j/` prefix check) don't burn breaker counts. Response shape adds `applied_input_types` mirroring omni's `category_applied_input_types` so the caller can distinguish text-triggered from image-triggered flags. Renamed error code `empty_text → empty_input`. **(2) `ModerationService.handleVisionFrame` + schema + evidence preservation** — three new columns on `moderation_events` (`source TEXT`, `image_path TEXT`, `applied_input_types_json TEXT`) and three on `moderation_global_config` (`image_moderation_enabled INTEGER DEFAULT 0`, `image_categories_enabled_json TEXT`, `image_frame_retention_days INTEGER DEFAULT 30`). `_applySchema` swallows "duplicate column" errors so the ALTERs in `ai-moderation-schema.sql` are idempotent across reboots. New `handleVisionFrame({streamerId, frame, sessionId, endTime, transcription})` method classifies image+optional-text via a SECOND `stage3Image` instance (distinct circuit-breaker state from text — closes red-team F3 where image timeouts would otherwise blind text moderation), evaluates triggered categories (only counts if omni's `applied_input_types[cat]` includes `'image'` — suppresses text-only `sexual/minors` flags), persists a `moderation_events` row with `source='image'`, **promotes the audit JPEG to `logs/visionbot/frames/banned/<event_id>.jpg`** so it survives the rolling-hour purge (separate `bannedRetentionDays` retention, default 30, configurable to 365 — closes red-team F2 where ban appeals filed >1h after auto_ban had no frame evidence), then routes the event through the existing `ModerationActionArbiter` (stale-session check + enforce gate). `setImageModerationConfig({enabled, categories, frame_retention_days})` server-side validation drops text-only omni categories from the input (silently filters `sexual/minors`, `hate`, `hate/threatening`, `harassment`, `harassment/threatening`, `illicit`, `illicit/violent` — image input can't trigger them per OpenAI's docs) and clamps retention to [1, 365]. `EgressFrameCaptureService` gains `promoteFrameForEvent({originalPath, eventId})` + `setBannedRetentionDays` + per-subdir cutoff in `purgeOldFrames` (the `banned/` subdir uses days-scale retention, all other subdirs keep the hourly rolling purge). **(3) VisionBotService integration + admin endpoints + ADR + runbook** — `VisionBotService._runCycle` **awaits** `moderationService.handleVisionFrame()` BEFORE scheduling the bot-dispatch `setTimeout` chain (closes red-team F4 / bot-dispatch race). On `auto_ban` / `auto_skip`: halt cycle (`cycles_dropped.moderated++`, no chat post). On `clean` / `admin_review`: continue with dispatch. Bot reaction latency grows by ~0.5–2 s per cycle; acceptable. Fail-open: a moderation-gate throw is caught and dispatch continues (a moderation bug must not silence the bot). New `setModerationService(svc)` late-injection setter on VisionBotService (called from `server/index.js` after `moderationService.initialize()` resolves — the factory can't await async init). Three new `/api/moderation-ai/*` endpoints behind `authenticateAdmin`: `GET /image-config`, `POST /image-config` (validation: enabled is boolean, categories is array, frame_retention_days is number; service-side clamping enforces the [1, 365] retention and image-supported-only category subset), `GET /events/:id/frame` (streams audit JPEG; 404 if event source !== 'image' or image_path purged past retention). **CRITICAL caveat documented in ADR-0021 + runbook**: omni-moderation's `sexual/minors` (CSAM) category is **TEXT-ONLY** per OpenAI's docs — image inputs cannot trigger CSAM detection. Image moderation covers only 6 of 13 categories: `sexual`, `violence`, `violence/graphic`, `self-harm`, `self-harm/intent`, `self-harm/instructions`. Existing Stage 3 text path still catches CSAM in transcribed audio. Image-CSAM detection (PhotoDNA / Thorn Safer hash matching) is deliberately deferred. New runbook `docs/operations/runbooks/csam-incident.md` documents the manual NCMEC CyberTipline reporting workflow per 18 U.S.C. § 2258A (90-day preservation override of the 30-day banned-frame retention; legal-counsel signoff submission chain). New tests: **12 in `ModerationStage3.image.test.js`** (request-shape backward-compat, validation guards don't consume breaker count, applied_input_types response field, error propagation); **15 in `ModerationService.image.test.js`** (enable-flag short-circuit, stage3Image-not-ready short-circuit, multi-modal call shape, clean-frame writes no row, image-source flag writes `source='image'` row, applied_input_types-only-text trigger suppressed, audit-JPEG promotion + image_path UPDATE, enforce=true → arbiter promotes to auto_ban, enforce=false → admin_review retained, notifier.eventCreated fires after flag, degraded/error paths, setImageModerationConfig category filtering + retention clamping); **7 new in `VisionBotService.test.js` `image-moderation gate` describe block** (auto_ban halts dispatch, auto_skip halts dispatch, clean/admin_review continue, gate-throws fail-open, args passed correctly into the gate, no moderationService → no-op). Suite: 117/117 across the affected suites. **Risk**: MEDIUM — OpenAI dependency is already a v1 dep of text moderation (no new vendor onboarding); new auto-ban path is gated by the existing global `enforce` toggle and defaults to off; evidence preservation closes the appeal-broken-by-design hazard; separate Stage 3 instance closes the cross-pipeline breaker hazard. **Deferred** (ADR-0021): PhotoDNA / Thorn Safer for image-CSAM hash matching; automated NCMEC CyberTipline reporting (manual runbook only); per-category score-threshold admin UI (default uses OpenAI's `flagged` boolean); N-of-M consecutive-frame requirement before auto-ban; separate `image_enforce` toggle; admin UI tile in `AIModerationManagement.tsx` (server + endpoints work via curl in this PR; client RTL tests need their own PR); TOS / privacy policy update reflecting OpenAI image-data flow. **Top-3 ship-blockers from the red-team pass, all addressed**: (a) CSAM-coverage misadvertisement — runbook + ADR explicit scope statement; admin endpoint validation drops CSAM-related categories from the image-enabled set. (b) Evidence-purged-before-appeal — banned/ promotion + days-scale retention. (c) Bot-dispatch race — `_runCycle` awaits moderation BEFORE scheduling dispatch setTimeouts.

- **Tail `console.*` sweep + `_traceId` propagation + CI regression check (PR 12.3, Phase 12 — closes Phase 12, applies [ADR-0020](docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md)).** Third and final PR of Phase 12. Three concerns land together: (a) sweep the remaining ~108 tail files to the namespaced pino logger, (b) wire `_traceId` request-scoped propagation through the logger mixin and the chokepoint notifiers, (c) add a CI regression check that fails any future PR re-introducing a stray `console.*` to the server tree. **(a) Tail sweep — 1664 → 0 `console.*` in `server/`.** PR 12.2 dropped the top 20 services from 3750 → 1664; PR 12.3 sweeps the remaining 107 files (skipping `server/bootstrap/logger.js` itself per the ADR's explicit exception). Same mechanical mapping as PR 12.2 (`console.error(` → `logger.error(`, …, `console.log(` → `logger.debug(` as the conservative default). Same per-file pattern: add `const logger = require('<rel>/bootstrap/logger').child({ svc: '<basename>' });` near the top, then sed the call sites. The sweep script now handles three directory depths: `server/bootstrap/*.js` uses `./logger` (same-dir), `server/services/<sub>/*.js` and `server/database/<sub>/*.js` use `../../bootstrap/logger`, all other 1-deep server dirs use `../bootstrap/logger`. **Pre-existing pino consumers** (`server/database/database.js`, `server/routes/bug-reports.js`) already had `const logger = require('../bootstrap/logger');` — the sweep added a second declaration which is a duplicate-identifier syntax error. Fix: the bare-import lines are dropped; the new child-logger lines (with `svc` binding) take their place. Three other files that imported `../bootstrap/logger` cleanly (`database-better.js`, `applyPragmas.js`, `transaction.js`) were not in the sweep target (zero `console.*` to migrate) and stay on the plain logger — migrating those to child loggers is operational polish, not load-bearing. **Three in-comment `console.*` literals** (one each in `server/bootstrap/logger.js`'s outdated docstring, `server/bootstrap/start-listeners.js`'s archaeology comment, and `server/database/repository/UserSessionRepository.js`'s logDeletionAction comment) were rewritten so the success-criterion grep finds zero in-source occurrences. The `logger.js` docstring's "the bulk of the codebase still uses `console.*`" paragraph is replaced with the convention statement and a pointer to ADR-0020. **(b) `_traceId` propagation** — new file [`server/bootstrap/trace-context.js`](server/bootstrap/trace-context.js) (~60 LoC + JSDoc, under the ADR's ~80 LoC estimate). Surface: `getTraceId()`, `runWithTraceId(traceId, fn)`, `makeTraceId()` (8-char alphanumeric from `crypto.randomUUID()`), `expressMiddleware(req, res, next)`. The middleware honours an inbound `X-Trace-Id` header (after `^[a-zA-Z0-9-]{1,64}$` validation — rejects newline-injection / overlong values), echoes the ID back on the response header, and runs `next()` inside the `AsyncLocalStorage` scope so every downstream `logger.X(...)` call picks up `traceId` as a binding automatically via the **logger mixin** added to `server/bootstrap/logger.js`: `mixin() { const traceId = getTraceId(); return traceId ? { traceId } : {}; }`. The middleware is wired into [`server/index.js`](server/index.js) immediately after `app.use(cors())` — runs before any route handler. **Chokepoint-notifier integration**: `server/services/StreamNotifier.js` and `server/services/BuffNotifier.js` now include `_traceId` on their socket-emit payloads via conditional spread (`{ reason, ...extras, ...(_traceId !== undefined && { _traceId }) }`). Conditional spread keeps the key absent (not present-as-undefined) when emitted from a non-request scope — preserves exact-equality test assertions and avoids cluttering payloads. **`ViewerCountNotifier` deliberately excluded**: its event signature emits a bare integer (`io.emit('viewer-count-update', count)`), not an object — adding `_traceId` would force the payload from `Number` to `{ count, _traceId }` and break every client consumer. Migrating that notifier's signature is a separate breaking-change PR; for Phase 12 it's documented and skipped. The two object-payload notifiers (StreamNotifier, BuffNotifier) carry the `_traceId` per the ADR; tests pin the new shape via the conditional-spread guard. **(c) CI regression check** — new test file [`server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js`](server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js). Greps `server/{services,routes,bootstrap,middleware,database}` for `console.(log|info|warn|error|debug)` and fails if any match exists outside the ALLOWED set (currently just `server/bootstrap/logger.js`). On failure prints the offending file:line list so the next-PR author can fix in-place. This is the closing invariant from ADR-0020 §"How to verify". **`AsyncLocalStorage` semantics**: the trace context propagates across `await`, `Promise.then`, `setTimeout`, `setImmediate`, and event-emitter callbacks scheduled within the request scope. Verified by 15 new tests in [`server/tests/bootstrap/trace-context.test.js`](server/tests/bootstrap/trace-context.test.js): nested-scope inner-ID precedence, scope-revert on return, async-boundary propagation (Promise.then and setImmediate), malicious-header rejection, length-limit rejection, response-header echo, `makeTraceId()` collision-free over 100 iterations. **Test migration**: five test files asserted on `console.*` spies and broke when the swept services started calling `logger.X(...)` instead — fixed in this PR by adding `jest.mock('../../bootstrap/logger', () => …)` blocks at the top of each affected file (mock returns `{ debug, info, warn, error, fatal, trace, child }` where each level is a `jest.fn()` and `child()` returns the same mock so `.child({svc:'X'}).warn` resolves to the same `jest.fn`). Affected: `ModerationService.test.js`, `LifecycleManager.test.js`, `BuffNotifier.test.js`, `StreamNotifier.test.js`, `ModerationNotifier.test.js`. Each test file aliases its prior `warnSpy` / `logSpy` / `errorSpy` to the mocked logger's level method so the existing 35-ish assertion bodies don't need to change. The other 14 test files that `spyOn(console, ...)` only spy as noise-suppression (no assertions) so they continue to work unchanged. **Diff**: 107 tail-file sweeps (each +~3 lines for the require header; ~1664 console-call edits via sed); `server/bootstrap/logger.js` -3 / +13 (docstring rewrite + mixin + trace-context import); `server/bootstrap/trace-context.js` +60 (new); `server/services/StreamNotifier.js` +9 (require + comment + conditional spread); `server/services/BuffNotifier.js` +6 (same); `server/index.js` +6 (middleware wire); `server/tests/bootstrap/trace-context.test.js` +145 (new, 15 tests); `server/tests/observability/no-console.test.js` +50 (new, 1 test); 5 test-file migrations (`ModerationService`/`LifecycleManager`/`BuffNotifier`/`StreamNotifier`/`ModerationNotifier` — average +10 / -3 per file for the jest.mock block + alias swaps); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. **Tests**: full suite under `--runInBand` with the standard exclusion list. **Baseline (post-merge-of-#153)**: 1039/1040. **Post-PR-12.3**: 1054/1055 (+15 from trace-context.test.js + 1 from no-console.test.js, -1 lost during the test-file migrations). Single failure is the pre-existing teardown-race flake (oscillates between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js`). **Risk**: LOW per Phase 12 brief. The sweep is mechanical; the trace-context layer is additive (only logs gain a binding when a request is in flight; otherwise unchanged); the notifier payload changes preserve exact-equality semantics via conditional spread. **Operational impact**: production debug becomes a single `grep '"traceId":"abc123"'` against the pino JSON output to get every line from the originating HTTP route through every service call through the chokepoint socket emit. For events emitted from background schedulers / scheduled tasks (no inbound request), the `traceId` and `_traceId` fields are simply absent — same as today. **Phase 12 closure**: success criterion met — zero `console.*` outside the allow-list; every chokepoint notifier with an object payload carries `_traceId`; the CI regression check prevents future re-introduction. **Things deliberately deferred**: (a) `ViewerCountNotifier._traceId` (requires breaking the bare-integer payload — separate PR with client coordination); (b) migrating the three clean-adopter database files (`database-better.js`, `applyPragmas.js`, `transaction.js`) to child loggers with `svc` bindings — operational polish, no behavioural impact; (c) per-line promotion of `logger.debug` calls to `logger.info` — operational tuning when production-debug output is needed and operators identify the noise/signal threshold; (d) per-route timing middleware — a separate observability scope (Phase 12.5 or Phase 13 candidate), touches every route mounting and is its own design conversation. **Live smoke (maintainer-gated)**: tail `journalctl -u onestreamer` after deploy; (a) confirm `"svc":"<ServiceName>"` and `"traceId":"<id>"` appear on log lines from request scopes; (b) hit any route with `-H "X-Trace-Id: smoke-test-123"` and verify the `X-Trace-Id: smoke-test-123` response header AND that downstream log lines from that request carry `"traceId":"smoke-test-123"`; (c) trigger a stream-ended emit (admin clear works) and tail the client websocket — the `stream-ended` payload should include `_traceId`. **Next phase**: Phase 13 (test coverage hardening) per the roadmap. Phase 12's logging foundation is the prerequisite for any meaningful production-traffic observability work that comes after.

### Changed
- **`console.*` → namespaced pino sweep, top 20 services (PR 12.2, Phase 12 — applies [ADR-0020](docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md)).** Second PR of Phase 12. Applies the convention codified in PR 12.1 (#152 / ADR-0020) to the 20 highest-density service files identified in the inventory. **Quantitative**: in-scope `console.*` count drops from **3750 → 1664** (-2086, -56 %). Each of the 20 files now imports a module-scoped child logger via `const logger = require('../bootstrap/logger').child({ svc: '<ServiceName>' });` (or `../../bootstrap/logger` for files under `viewbot/`) and calls `logger.X(...)` instead of `console.X(...)`. The `svc` binding is the class name so production log queries can filter by `"svc":"ChatBotService"` etc., natively against pino's JSON output. **Mechanical mapping** (preserved one-to-one): `console.error(` → `logger.error(`, `console.warn(` → `logger.warn(`, `console.info(` → `logger.info(`, `console.debug(` → `logger.debug(`, **`console.log(` → `logger.debug(`** (the conservative choice — most existing `console.log` callsites were per-event detail noise that belongs at `debug` per ADR-0020's info-↔-debug boundary; promoting specific lines to `info` is deferred to operational tuning). **Files swept** (top 20 by inventory density; covers ~57 % of all in-scope callsites): `viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js` (369), `ViewBotClientService.js` (197), `VisualFxService.js` (163), `ViewBotURLService.js` (134), `RandomStreamRotationService.js` (108), `ChatBotService.js` (108), `TranscriptionService.js` (107), `MediasoupService.js` (107), `CanvasFxService.js` (89), `ContinuousRecordingService.js` (82), `ViewBotLiveKitService.js` (81), `TakeoverService.js` (74), `RecordingService.js` (72), `ViewBotSocketClient.js` (64), `ItemUseService.js` (62), `TranscriptionAudioAdapter.js` (61), `BuffDebuffService.js` (58), `ViewbotService.js` (54), `ViewBotRotationService.js` (49), `AudioBufferService.js` (47). **Two files had no top-of-file `require()` block** (`TakeoverService.js`, `ItemUseService.js` start directly with `class XYZ {` or a comment block) — the bulk-awk script that inserts the logger require after the last existing require silently skipped them, producing files that called `logger.X(...)` with no `logger` symbol in scope and would `ReferenceError` at construction time. Fix: the logger require is prepended at the very top of the file, before any other code. Both files now construct cleanly and the previously-failing test (`server/tests/TakeoverService.test.js`) passes. **Four edge-case callsites needed surgical edits** beyond the mechanical `console.X(` sweep (where `console.X` appears without an immediate-call `(`): (1) `ViewBotLiveKitService.js:16` — `const log = DEBUG ? console.log.bind(console) : () => {};` → `console.log.bind(console)` → `logger.debug.bind(logger)`; (2) `TakeoverService.js:21` — `.catch(console.error)` callback-reference → `.catch((err) => logger.error({ err }, 'loadLastStreamStartTime failed'))` (pino-idiomatic `{ err }` for stack serialization); (3) `ItemUseService.js:20` — a *comment* containing the literal `console.log` was rewritten to remove the bare token so the ADR-0020 success-criterion grep stays clean; (4) `TranscriptionAudioAdapter.js:600` — `.catch(console.error)` → `.catch((err) => logger.error({ err }, 'connect failed'))`. **Test migration** — one test file needed to follow the migration: `server/tests/services/ContinuousRecordingService.cleanup-race.test.js` was asserting on a `jest.spyOn(console, 'error')` to verify the cleanup-aborted error path logs the failure. After the sweep the service calls `logger.error(...)` and the console spy gets zero calls. Fix: add a top-of-file `jest.mock('../../bootstrap/logger', ...)` that returns a `{ debug, info, warn, error, fatal, trace, child }` shape (each method a `jest.fn()`, `child()` returning the same mock so `.child({ svc: 'X' }).error` resolves to the same mock fn), import the mocked logger, and change the assertion to `expect(logger.error).toHaveBeenCalledWith(...)`. The two existing `consoleErrorSpy` / `consoleLogSpy` declarations stay as noise-suppression scaffolding (they're harmless when nothing calls `console.*`) — minimum-touch test change to preserve the rest of the file's structure. The other 16 test files that `spyOn(console, ...)` only spy as noise suppression (no assertions on the spy) so they continue to work unchanged. **Diff**: 20 service files modified (+~50 lines for the logger require headers; ~2086 console-call edits in-place via sed; ~5 surgical edits for the edge cases); `server/tests/services/ContinuousRecordingService.cleanup-race.test.js` -1 / +14 (jest.mock block + import + one-line assertion change); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. Net per-file: roughly +3 lines (require header) per file = +60 across the 20; the sed substitutions are byte-for-byte single-token swaps so the line count is unchanged. **Tests**: full suite under `--runInBand` with the standard exclusion list (`worktrees|EgressFrameCaptureService|TranscriptionDrivenBotService|ChatBotLLMService.vision|VisionBotService`). **Baseline at Phase 11 close (now on `main`)**: 1039/1040 (+181 vs the 858/859 reported at Phase 10 close — Phase 7's PR #134 added ~9 tests, Phase 10's three PRs added +54 / +45 / +50 = +149, Phase 11's two PRs added 0 net). **Post-PR-12.2**: 1039/1040 — exact baseline match. The single failure is the same pre-existing teardown-race flake from the Phase 6 handoff (oscillates between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js` between runs depending on Jest worker ordering; reproducible on `main` without this PR). **Risk**: LOW (per Phase 12 brief). The sweep is mechanical (single-token substitution + a header line + four surgical edits); the test surface that broke (1 file, 1 assertion) was fixed in the same PR; the conservative `console.log` → `logger.debug` choice keeps production-info volume unchanged from the operator's perspective (info messages are still info; debug-level is gated by `LOG_LEVEL` which defaults to `info` in production per [`server/bootstrap/logger.js`](server/bootstrap/logger.js)). **Things deliberately deferred to PR 12.3**: (a) the **1664 remaining `console.*` callsites** in the ~108 tail files (the long tail averages ~15 calls/file; PR 12.3 sweeps them); (b) the `_traceId` propagation helper (`server/bootstrap/trace-context.js`, ~80 LoC); (c) the chokepoint-notifier integration so every socket emit carries `_traceId`; (d) the CI regression-check (the `console.*`-grep invariant from ADR-0020 §"How to verify") — lands once the global count is at zero so the check is meaningful. **Things deferred indefinitely**: per-line promotion of `logger.debug` calls to `logger.info` is operational tuning, not a refactor; do it when production-debug output is needed and operators identify the noise/signal threshold. **Live smoke (maintainer-gated)**: tail the dev server's log and confirm pino's JSON output now carries `"svc":"<ServiceName>"` on lines from the swept services (e.g. trigger a chat bot, watch for `"svc":"ChatBotService"`; trigger a stream takeover, watch for `"svc":"TakeoverService"`). At `LOG_LEVEL=debug` (dev default), the volume of swept-file output should match pre-PR — most lines that were `console.log` are now `logger.debug` and stay visible. At `LOG_LEVEL=info` (prod default), the volume from swept files should drop sharply because all the former-`console.log` callsites stop emitting. **Phase 12 status**: 2/3 PRs done. Next: PR 12.3 sweeps the ~108 tail files + adds the `_traceId` propagation helper + adds the CI regression check.

### Added
- **Namespaced-logging convention codified + `console.*` callsite inventory (PR 12.1, Phase 12 — [ADR-0020](docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md)).** First PR of Phase 12 (observability sweep). Docs-only — zero code changes. Codifies the convention the sweep PRs (12.2, 12.3) will land against and inventories the surface so the sweep has a concrete target list. **Why now**: at Phase 11 close the codebase has **3750 `console.*` callsites across 128 server-side files** (verified by `grep -rE "console\.(log|info|warn|error|debug)" server/{services,routes,bootstrap,middleware,database} --include="*.js"`), against a [`server/bootstrap/logger.js`](server/bootstrap/logger.js) module that exposes a single shared pino logger but is imported by only **six** server files — three of which use it cleanly (`database-better.js`, `applyPragmas.js`, `transaction.js`) and three of which are hybrid (`server/index.js` is the canonical "logger imported but unused" pattern at 1 logger call vs 368 console calls). Two operational consequences: (a) no filterable log structure — `process.stdout.write(util.format(...) + '\n')` mixes 96 services' output with no level / service-tag / structured timestamps to index against; (b) no correlation across layers — when a socket emit goes wrong, the originating HTTP route and the chokepoint notifier (Phase 3 — `StreamNotifier`, `ViewerCountNotifier`, `BuffNotifier`) have no shared identifier and "what happened to this user's request?" requires reading timestamps and guessing. Phase 12 closes both. PR 12.1 codifies; PR 12.2 sweeps the top 20 services; PR 12.3 sweeps the tail and adds `_traceId` propagation via `AsyncLocalStorage`. **ADR-0020 decisions**: (1) one pino child logger per service / route file, namespaced by a `svc` binding (`require('../bootstrap/logger').child({ svc: 'ChatBotService' })`) — so every log line carries `"svc":"ChatBotService"` in the JSON payload and Loki / ELK / Datadog can filter natively. Child loggers are cheap (pino caches bindings); construct one at module scope per file. (2) Level conventions pinned: `fatal` (process about to die), `error` (handled error — request failed, service continues; always include `err` so pino serializes the stack), `warn` (suspicious state, degraded operation, retries), `info` (noteworthy lifecycle — service started, scheduled task ran, user-visible state transition), `debug` (per-request / per-event detail for production troubleshooting; default-on in dev, default-off in prod), `trace` (very-noisy interior loops; production-off). The boundary that matters most operationally is **info ↔ debug** — info lines should read as a story of what the system did at a high level. (3) What stays on `console.*`: migration scripts under `scripts/migrations/` (CLI tools, no shared logger context, 526 callsites — explicitly out-of-scope per Phase 12 brief's success criterion), other `scripts/` (ops, deploy, setup), and `server/bootstrap/logger.js` itself (circular if it logs through itself). Everything else migrates. (4) `_traceId` propagation (target shape; lands in PR 12.3): every chokepoint notifier emit carries `_traceId`; trace ID generated at HTTP-route entry via express middleware and propagated through the service call chain via `AsyncLocalStorage` so every `logger.X(...)` call inside the request scope picks up `traceId` as a binding automatically. A production debugging session collapses to `journalctl -u onestreamer --since '15 min ago' | grep '"traceId":"abc123"'` and gets every line from the HTTP route through the service through the socket emit. The propagation helper lands in PR 12.3 as `server/bootstrap/trace-context.js` (~80 LoC); PR 12.2 prepares the way by sweeping services to use the namespaced logger — once services call `logger.X(...)`, the AsyncLocalStorage layer can inject `traceId` into the bindings transparently and every existing log line gets the field for free. **Inventory** (in [`docs/architecture/plans/console-callsite-inventory.md`](docs/architecture/plans/console-callsite-inventory.md)): top 20 service files by `console.*` density cover **2127 calls** = 57 % of all in-scope callsites; PR 12.2's touch list is those 20 files (~500 lines edited). Tail bucket: ~1623 calls across ~108 files (average ~15 calls/file) — PR 12.3's touch list. The headline-density-top-three is the Phase-11 ViewBot pair plus VisualFx: `server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js` (369, the Phase 11 extraction), `server/services/ViewBotClientService.js` (197, post-extraction orchestrator), `server/services/VisualFxService.js` (163). Per-directory breakdown: services 3256/96, routes 409/25, database 44/2, bootstrap 23/3, middleware 18/2. The methodology block is in the inventory so PR 12.2 / PR 12.3 can re-run the grep against the merge-tip-of-main for a fresh snapshot before scoping. **Strict sequencing constraint preserved**: Phase 12 lands AFTER Phases 7, 8, 9, 10, 11 — the logging sweep touches every service file, and if it landed before, every Phase 7–11 diff would be contaminated by logger churn. PR 12.1 ships now that all of Phases 7–11 are merged on main (PRs #134, #142–149, #150, #151). **Bonus docs cleanup**: the ADR README index ([`docs/architecture/adr/README.md`](docs/architecture/adr/README.md)) at the Phase 11 close was missing the ADR-0019 row that PR 11.1 (#150) should have added. PR 12.1 adds both the missing 0019 row and the new 0020 row in one shot — same table, defensible scope creep given this PR is docs-only. **Diff**: `docs/architecture/adr/0020-namespaced-logging-with-pino.md` +110 (new); `docs/architecture/plans/console-callsite-inventory.md` +95 (new); `docs/architecture/adr/README.md` -1 / +3 (two new ADR rows); `CHANGELOG.md` +1 entry. Zero changes under `server/`, `client/`, `chat-service/`, `scripts/`. **Tests**: not run for this PR (docs-only — no code surface to break). PR 12.2's touch will re-establish the suite baseline. **Risk**: LOW (per Phase 12 brief — docs-only). **No reviewer subagent pass** — docs-only PR, the convention is straightforward and matches the existing logger.js docstring's stated migration intent ("new code (and any of the noisiest existing sites a refactor touches) has a structured target"). **Live smoke**: N/A (no behaviour change). **Phase 12 status**: 1/3 PRs done. Next: PR 12.2 sweeps the top 20 services to namespaced pino; PR 12.3 sweeps the tail + adds the `_traceId` propagation helper.

### Fixed
- **Three latent ViewBot bugs surfaced + unused-import trim (PR 11.2, Phase 11 closing cleanup, stacked on PR 11.1).** Second PR of Phase 11. Closes Phase 11 with the post-extraction cleanup that PR 11.1 deliberately deferred to keep that PR a strict file split (per CLAUDE.md "Don't refactor adjacent code while fixing a specific bug"). Four fixes; three of them sit on the *same* 12-line block of `ViewBotClientService.updateRotationSettings` (post-PR-11.1 lines 188–200) — discovered as a coupled set by PR 11.2's adversarial reviewer pass, which also surfaced the third typo that the first reviewer pass missed. The three are coupled: fixing fewer than all three converts one kind of failure into a strictly worse kind. **(1) `ViewBotClientService.updateRotationSettings` — `this.viewBots` typo, adjacent broken-receiver call, AND a third bug: filter using a function reference instead of an invocation.** Pre-PR-11.2 the block read: `const activeBots = Array.from(this.viewBots.values()).filter(bot => bot.isStreaming);` followed by `bot.rotationCheckTimer` clear + `this.startRotationCheckTimer(bot.botId);`. Three bugs here. (a) The field is `this.activeBots` (set in the constructor); `this.viewBots` was always `undefined`, so the `.values()` access would `TypeError` and the *entire* block was unreachable on `main`. PR 11.1's adversarial reviewer surfaced this typo. (b) Six lines lower, the same block called `this.startRotationCheckTimer(bot.botId)` — but `startRotationCheckTimer` is an instance method of `ViewBotInstance` (not the orchestrator), and it takes no args. Fixing only (a) would convert one `TypeError` into a different `TypeError`, strictly worse — the path now begins to run instead of failing fast. (c) PR 11.2's *own* reviewer pass caught a third bug in the same block — `.filter(bot => bot.isStreaming)` uses `bot.isStreaming` as a function REFERENCE, never invoking it. Function references are always truthy, so the filter was a no-op pre-fix. After (a) and (b) alone, every bot in the map (including not-streaming placeholders from `restoreViewBots`) would have hit the `clearTimeout` + `bot.startRotationCheckTimer()` path. `startRotationCheckTimer` short-circuits cleanly via `scheduleNextRotationCheck → performRotationCheck`'s `!this.streaming` guard, so it's not catastrophic — but it schedules a 65-s-ish timer for every bot in the map, including ones that have no business being rotated. Fixed by matching the dominant defensive pattern already used at orchestrator lines 1514 and 1562: `(bot) => (typeof bot.isStreaming === 'function' ? bot.isStreaming() : bot.streaming)` — handles `ViewBotInstance` objects (call the method) and `restoreViewBots` placeholder objects (read the `streaming` property fallback). All three are fixed in one block, and an 8-line in-file comment block now documents all three pre-existing bugs to deter a future "tidy" from re-introducing any of them. The call path (`updateRotationSettings` ← admin endpoint `POST /admin/viewbot/rotation-settings` or the like, when invoked while bots are streaming and configured rotation intervals change) was broken end-to-end on `main`. After this PR it works: when an admin updates rotation intervals while bots are streaming, only actually-streaming bots have their rotation-check timer cleared and restarted with the new intervals via `bot.startRotationCheckTimer()` (which itself stops + reschedules through `scheduleNextRotationCheck`). **(2) `ViewBotInstance.startFFmpegVideoGeneration` — `this.ffmpegPath` reference.** Line 1894 of `server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js`: `this.videoFFmpeg = spawn(this.ffmpegPath, ffmpegArgs, …)`. `ffmpegPath` is owned by `ViewBotClientService` (set by `detectFFmpegPath()` during `initialize`); `ViewBotInstance` never sets it. The bare `this.ffmpegPath` on the instance was always `undefined`, and `spawn(undefined, …)` would throw `TypeError: "file" argument must be a non-empty string`. Every other `spawn(…ffmpeg…)` callsite in `ViewBotInstance.js` already uses `this.parentService?.ffmpegPath || 'ffmpeg'` — confirmed by `grep -nE "spawn\(this\.parentService\?\.ffmpegPath" server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js`, which reports the six surviving callsites at lines 592 (`startCombinedFFmpegGeneration`), 744 (`startMultiplexedFFmpegGeneration`), 893 (`startPlainTransportFFmpegGeneration`), 2031 (`startFFmpegVideoGeneration` second method definition; the file has two methods named `startFFmpegVideoGeneration` and only the first was broken), 2083 (`startFFmpegAudioGeneration`), 2818 (`initializeVideoFileStreaming`), plus the now-fixed 1894. Fix matches the established pattern. **(3) Drop unused `uuidv4` + `puppeteer` requires from `ViewBotClientService.js`.** PR 11.1 deliberately kept all the original top-of-file requires to keep the split mechanical. Post-split inventory: `uuidv4` (`require('uuid').v4`) was never referenced anywhere in the orchestrator class — verified by `grep -nE "\\buuidv4\\b" server/services/ViewBotClientService.js`: only the import line. `puppeteer` (the npm package) was referenced *only* inside shell-command strings at `killOrphanedPuppeteerProcesses` (`taskkill … *puppeteer* …`, `pkill -f "puppeteer.*chrome"`) — those are pkill / taskkill argument patterns matching against the process command line, not JS references to the puppeteer module. Verified: `grep -nE "puppeteer\\.[a-z]" server/services/ViewBotClientService.js` returns only the `"puppeteer.*chrome"` shell-glob string at line 1097, no `puppeteer.launch(…)` etc. Both requires dropped. Behaviour-preserving — neither was carrying load. **Diff**: `server/services/ViewBotClientService.js` -3 / +13 (net +10: two require lines removed, three typo-block lines edited in place, eight new comment lines documenting the bug-cluster); `server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js` -1 / +1 (one-line in-place fix). **Tests**: not modified (the typo-affected admin code path has no existing unit coverage; full-suite baseline run exercises the surrounding modules end-to-end). Full suite under `--runInBand` with the standard exclusion list (`worktrees|EgressFrameCaptureService|TranscriptionDrivenBotService|ChatBotLLMService.vision|VisionBotService`): **858/859** — exact match to PR 11.1 baseline and to `main` baseline. The single pre-existing teardown-race flake (between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js`) remains the floor; reproducible on `main` without this PR. **Risk**: LOW. All four fixes are surgical (single-line typo edits and one short comment block) restoring code that was either unreachable (the orchestrator's three-typo block) or that would throw on first call (`this.ffmpegPath`). No callsite signature change; no API change. **Stacking**: PR 11.2's branch (`viewbot-phase11-cleanup`) is stacked on `viewbot-instance-extraction` (PR 11.1's branch). PR 11.2's base on GitHub is `viewbot-instance-extraction` until 11.1 merges, at which point GitHub auto-rebases to `main`. Maintainer should merge 11.1 first, then 11.2. **Live smoke (maintainer-gated)**: the previously-broken `updateRotationSettings` admin path now works — toggle rotation intervals via the admin panel while a ViewBot is streaming and confirm that (a) no `TypeError` in server logs and (b) only the streaming bot's rotation-check timer restarts (not every entry in the activeBots map). Other smoke items inherited from PR 11.1's gate. **Phase 11 closes** with this PR. Success criterion ("ViewBotClientService is structurally improved, operator can find what they're looking for in <60 s") delivered by PR 11.1's 6015 → 2290 split; PR 11.2 closes out the three coupled latent runtime bugs PR 11.1's reviewer pass surfaced, plus the matching `ffmpegPath` typo in `ViewBotInstance.js`, plus the two import-noise lines. Phase 11's brief allowed PR 11.2 to be either a second mode extraction (not applicable — see PR 11.1 / ADR-0019, no separable modes existed) or follow-up cleanup; this is the cleanup. Phase 12 (observability sweep — logging + trace IDs) is next per the roadmap; the larger `ViewBotInstance` decomposition candidates surfaced in ADR-0019 ("further decomposition of `ViewBotInstance`" — FFmpeg argument builders, cooldown subsystem) are deferred to a future refactor phase and are not pre-conditions for Phase 12.

### Changed
- **Extract `ViewBotInstance` to `server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js` (PR 11.1, Phase 11 — [ADR-0019](docs/architecture/adr/0019-viewbot-instance-extraction.md)).** First PR of Phase 11 (`ViewBotClientService` decomposition). `server/services/ViewBotClientService.js` was 6015 lines — the single largest server file. The Phase 11 brief inherited a hypothesis from the codebase-hotspot agent that the file held "2–3 separate rotation modes tangled together" and that the right move was per-mode strategy extraction, with a path-B fallback for the non-separable case (in-file reorganization + pull DB code into [`ViewBotRepository`](server/database/repository/ViewBotRepository.js)). Reality on opening the file: **neither path as framed applied**. (i) The file is **two classes**, not one — `class ViewBotClientService` (lines 1–2287, orchestrator) and `class ViewBotInstance` (lines 2289–6012, per-bot streaming client). Only the orchestrator is exported (`module.exports = ViewBotClientService;`); `ViewBotInstance` is constructed exclusively by the orchestrator (two callsites — `createBot` fast path + `ensureBotConnected` rehydrate path) and is not imported anywhere else in the repo (`grep -rn "ViewBotInstance"` outside the file: zero hits). (ii) The orchestrator has **one** rotation system, not multiple modes — rotation config, bot lifecycle, rotation control, rotation queue, and the cooldown subsystem all share `this.activeBots`, `this.currentLiveBot`, `this.rotationLock`, and the queue; extracting any one part would create artificial state coupling. (iii) **Path B was already done** — `ViewBotClientService.js` contains zero SQL (verified by grep); PR 6.1's `ViewBotRepository` extraction was exhaustive, and persistence flows through `this.dbService` (`ViewBotDatabaseService` → `ViewBotRepository`). (iv) **The bot-instance class is the giant** — 3724 lines, owning its own state (socket, browser, page, mediaStream, videoFFmpeg, audioFFmpeg, gstreamerVideoProcess, etc.) and reaching upward only through `this.parentService.X` (read-mostly: `ffmpegPath`, `dbService`, `dbInitialized`, `realStreamerActive`, `rotationProbability`, `rotationCheckIntervalMin`, `rotationCheckIntervalMax`, `rotationEnabled`; two writes: `currentLiveBot`, `currentLiveBotSetTime`; DB writes via `parentService.dbService`). Coupling is unidirectional and clean. **Decision (ADR-0019)**: class-level file split. `ViewBotInstance` moves to `server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js` with its own require header (the requires it actually uses: `child_process.spawn`, `path`, `fs`, `socket.io-client`, `puppeteer`, `../ProcessManager`, `../ViewBotStateManager` — `../` prefix because sibling services live one directory up from `viewbot/`); `ViewBotClientService.js` adds `const ViewBotInstance = require('./viewbot/ViewBotInstance');` at the top of its requires block and keeps everything else verbatim. **Behaviour-preserving**: runtime semantics of `this.parentService.X` are identical whether the class lives in the same file or a sibling module. Node's module cache makes the additional `require()` free after first load. No API change. No constructor-signature change. `server/bootstrap/services.js:157` + `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js:226` (the only external readers of `ViewBotClientService`) require no edit. **Diff**: `server/services/ViewBotClientService.js` 6015 → **2290 lines** (-3725, -62%); `server/services/viewbot/ViewBotInstance.js` **+3750 lines** (new file — 24-line header comment + requires + the moved 3724-line class body + footer); net +25 lines (header + require line + footer trailing newlines). **Tests**: not modified. Full suite under `--runInBand` with the standard exclusion list (`worktrees|EgressFrameCaptureService|TranscriptionDrivenBotService|ChatBotLLMService.vision|VisionBotService`): **858/859** post-PR vs. **858/859** baseline on `main` — exact match. The 1 failure is the pre-existing teardown-race flake from the Phase 6 handoff (note #8 in the Phase 10 hand-off — flips between `database-better.test.js` and `transaction.test.js` between runs depending on Jest worker ordering; reproducible on `main` without this PR). Passing ViewBot-adjacent suites this run: `UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog.test.js`, `ViewBotRepository.test.js`, `ViewBotURLService.whitelist-gate.test.js`, `bootstrap/start-streaming-backend.test.js`, `bootstrap/services.test.js`. **Risk**: HIGH-per-Phase-11-plan / actually-low-given-mechanical-shape (no behavior change, no API change, pure file move; the reviewer agent's pass focused on import-coupling and parentService-state access patterns). **Things deliberately deferred** (the brief's "honest about partial extractions" rule): (a) pre-existing typo at *post-extraction* orchestrator line 192 — `Array.from(this.viewBots.values())` should be `this.activeBots`; the call path (`updateRotationSettings` → restart timers for active bots) would `TypeError` if invoked while bots are streaming; pre-existing on `main`; honoring "Don't refactor adjacent code while fixing a specific bug" — left as-is for PR 11.2 cleanup; (b) the orchestrator's `uuidv4` import is unused inside the surviving class, and `puppeteer` is referenced only inside `killOrphanedPuppeteerProcesses` command-string matches (never invoked as a JS API); both stay in `ViewBotClientService.js` to keep this PR strictly a split — drop in PR 11.2; (c) further decomposition of the 3750-line `ViewBotInstance` file is the natural follow-up — candidates surfaced for PR 11.2 include the FFmpeg argument builders (`createVideoFFmpegArgs`, `createH264VideoFFmpegArgs`, `createAudioFFmpegArgs`, `createVideoRtpParameters`, `createAudioRtpParameters` — ~300 lines of pure functions, trivially extractable to `viewbot/ffmpeg-args.js`) and the orchestrator-side cooldown subsystem (`applyBotCooldown`, `getBotProbabilityMultiplier`, `selectViewBotWithCooldown`, `startCooldownCleanup` — ~120 lines that take the cooldown `Map` as constructor arg and would expose a thin facade from the orchestrator); PR 11.1 deliberately keeps both deferred so the file split lands clean and reviewable on its own. **Live smoke** (maintainer-gated; the autonomous agent can't run `npm run dev` — needs webcam, real takeover, and the LiveKit/MediaSoup runtime): walk [`docs/getting-started/first-stream.md`](docs/getting-started/first-stream.md) — sign up, take over a stream, then create + start + destroy a ViewBot through the admin panel, then trigger the real-streamer takeover path, then trigger a rotation. The split is behaviour-equivalent at the runtime level (verified by the unchanged 858/859 result), but `ViewBotInstance` carries the full FFmpeg/GStreamer/MediaSoup transport surface — live smoke is the maintainer's gate before merge.
- **`AccountService` non-users-table SQL extracted into two sibling repositories (PR 10.3, Phase 10 — closes Phase 10).** Final PR of Phase 10. Continues — and concludes — the repository-pattern rollout for the top-8 DB-touching services. 16 of the 17 inline `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites in [`server/services/AccountService.js`](server/services/AccountService.js) against tables OTHER than `users` collapse to method calls on two new repositories. The remaining one is the cascade-delete enumeration loop in `permanentlyDeleteAccount`, which stays inline by design (see scope note below). **`AccountStatsRepository`** ([new file](server/database/repository/AccountStatsRepository.js)) owns the user-economy tables — `user_stats` (the points-balance row + cumulative stream/view counters) and `points_transactions` (the audit log). Ten methods: `insertEmptyStats(userId)` (createUserStats path), `insertStatsWithBalance({userId, balance})` (atomicAddPoints fallback path), `updateStats(userId, setFragments, values)` (dynamic SET-builder; the relative-vs-absolute decision stays in the service since it's per-column and domain-specific, but the repo appends `updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP` and the WHERE-by-user_id; empty fragments short-circuit to `{changes: 0}` without a DB call), `getStatsByUserId` (single-table SELECT *), `getPointsBalanceByUserId` (narrow projection used by the subtractPoints error-message disambiguation), `atomicAddPoints({userId, amount})` + `atomicSubtractPoints({userId, amount})` (**PR 5.1 / [ADR-0013a](docs/architecture/adr/0013a-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md) atomic-counter shape preserved byte-for-byte** — `UPDATE … SET points_balance = points_balance ± ? … RETURNING points_balance`, plus the guarded debit's `AND points_balance >= ?` fence — DO NOT refactor; the single-statement shape is what closes the lost-update race), `deleteStatsByUserId`, `insertTransaction({userId, amount, balanceAfter, type, description, metadataJson})` (note: `metadataJson` is pre-stringified by the caller — keeps the repo type-uniform), `listTransactionsByUserId(userId, limit)`. **`UserSessionRepository`** ([new file](server/database/repository/UserSessionRepository.js)) owns the session/lifecycle tables — `user_sessions` (active cookie-token → user mappings with `expires_at` TTL), `account_deletion_logs` (audit trail for the deletion-request → confirm → purge lifecycle), and `ip_to_user_transfers` (anonymous-IP-session → logged-in-user migration audit). Seven methods: `insertSession`, `getActiveSessionByUserId` (newest non-expired row), `deleteSessionById`, `deleteExpiredSessions` (the cleanup tick — no params, `datetime('now')` literal), `deleteSessionsByUserId` (called from soft-delete `deleteUser`), `insertDeletionLog` (the 7-column audit row with `created_at = datetime('now')` baked in), and `insertIpTransfer`. **Two repos because the concerns are separable** — user-economy vs. session/lifecycle. The brief's split holds; the call-site spread across the AccountService methods cleanly lines up with the two groupings. **`logDeletionAction` lifted off raw `db.run` callbacks**: the legacy `logDeletionAction` used a Promise wrapper around the raw sqlite3 `db.run` callback shape, which had two oddities — (a) it swallowed errors (logged + `resolve(false)` instead of rejecting), and (b) it bypassed the `runAsync` wrapper entirely, so it predated the better-sqlite3 adapter path. PR 10.3 moves the INSERT onto `userSessionRepository.insertDeletionLog` and reproduces the swallow shape at the service level with try/catch. Observable behaviour is identical (audit-log INSERT failures still log + resolve-false the calling promise without throwing upstream) — the change is structural: from "callback-style pseudo-Promise that swallowed at the DB layer" to "real Promise that the service swallows in its try/catch wrapper." This also means the deletion-log INSERT now runs under `USE_BETTER_SQLITE3=true` correctly, which the legacy `db.run` path didn't. **Inline by design** (1 callsite — the cascade-delete loop in `permanentlyDeleteAccount`): the loop iterates seven table names and runs `DELETE FROM ${table} WHERE user_id = ?` for each. PR 10.3 deliberately does NOT extract this into N repo calls because: (a) the enumerated table list IS the audit trail for what permanent deletion covers — splitting it across repos would make "what gets deleted?" harder to read; (b) three of the seven tables (`user_inventory`, `item_usage_history`, `user_points_log`) aren't owned by any repo yet — a hybrid loop with some repo calls and some inline-SQL DELETEs would be confusing; (c) the loop's `this.db.run` callback shape is otherwise unused in the file, so it doesn't fit any existing repo idiom. The loop is annotated with `// **Cascade-delete loop stays inline by design**` naming PR 10.3 so the next round of repo work knows to revisit. **PR 5.1 atomic-points UPDATE shape preserved**: the bootstrap brief specifically flagged this as a load-bearing invariant. The two atomic methods on `AccountStatsRepository` use single-statement `UPDATE … SET col = col ± ? … RETURNING col` exactly as PR 5.1 wrote them; the regression-pin tests in `server/tests/services/AccountService.points-race.test.js` (12 `it()` blocks across 4 backend-flag matrix combinations) still pass against the repo-extracted code, confirming behaviour-equivalence. The repo's class JSDoc explicitly forbids refactoring to a read-compute-write loop. **Diff**: `server/services/AccountService.js` -106 / +82 = -24 net (692 → 668 LoC; SQL bodies collapse but the repo construction in the constructor + the rationale comments add some lines back). `server/database/repository/AccountStatsRepository.js` +217 (new file, including 90 lines of JSDoc citing ADR-0013a + the relative-arithmetic discipline). `server/database/repository/UserSessionRepository.js` +184 (new file, including the cascade-delete scope-note). `server/tests/database/repository/AccountStatsRepository.test.js` +237 (new, **30 test cases** via `describe.each` × USE_BETTER_SQLITE3 = 15 logical × 2 = 30). `server/tests/database/repository/UserSessionRepository.test.js` +181 (new, **20 test cases** = 10 logical × 2). Total: **+50 new test cases** (30 + 20). **Constructor wiring**: AccountService's constructor gains two new optional deps (`accountStatsRepository` and `userSessionRepository`) alongside the existing `userRepository`. All three default to fresh `new XRepository({getAsync, runAsync, allAsync})` instances so the dozens of `new AccountService()` callsites scattered throughout the codebase continue to work unchanged. **Tests** — repo level: every method's SQL string (whitespace-normalized) + parameter ordering pinned. `atomicAddPoints` and `atomicSubtractPoints` each get an explicit ADR-0013a-shape assertion that the test header names as a regression gate. `atomicSubtractPoints` gets the **"amount bound twice"** test — pinning that `params[0] === params[2]` so a future "tidy" of the SQL to bind amount once breaks the guard visibly. `updateStats` gets the empty-fragments short-circuit test (no DB call, returns `{changes: 0}`). `insertTransaction` gets a null-metadataJson test for the no-metadata case. `insertDeletionLog` gets a null-ipAddress + null-userAgent test for the server-side-action case. Constructor sections cover the fallback-to-real-primitives and inject-deps paths for both repos. Service level: the pre-existing 12-case `AccountService.points-race.test.js` suite continues to pass against the repo-extracted code — the test mocks the DB primitives at the module level, and the repo's pass-through-to-primitives shape preserves the bind sequences exactly. **Full slice**: **908/909 under `--runInBand`** on the slice excluding the four VisionBot test files (`EgressFrameCaptureService`, `TranscriptionDrivenBotService`, `ChatBotLLMService.vision`, `VisionBotService`); was 858/859 same slice pre-PR; +50. The slice exclusion matches PR 10.1 + PR 10.2 for direct comparability — the VisionBot phase landing at PRs 142/143/146/149 added slow tests that don't run cleanly under `--runInBand`. Same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` flake from the Phase 6 handoff, untouched. **Risk**: LOW-MEDIUM per the Phase 10 brief. The two repos are read-mostly except for the atomic-points UPDATE-RETURNING calls, which are byte-equivalent to the legacy SQL and pinned by the points-race regression test. The session/lifecycle methods are short single-statement queries. The behaviour-change in `logDeletionAction` is structural-only (the swallow shape moves from DB layer to service layer; observable behaviour identical). **No new ADR** — PR 10.3 is a straight extraction without a new architectural decision. Two architectural decisions are reapplied: [ADR-0013a](docs/architecture/adr/0013a-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md) (atomic-counter shape, preserved in `atomicAddPoints` / `atomicSubtractPoints`) and the established single-domain-repo convention. **ADR register**: VisionBot's [PR #145](https://github.com/onestreamer/onestreamer/pull/145) took ADR-0018 (visionbot screenshot comments). Next free slot is now **0019** (the Phase 11 brief's prior reservation of 0018 for ViewBotClientService decomposition is invalidated — Phase 11's ADR will be 0019). **Phase 10 closure**: **3/3 PRs done**. After Phase 10 merges: every DB-touching service in the top-8 has a repository (User, Item, ChatBot, ViewBot, Buff, ContinuousRecording, Shop [PR 7.4, still open], Clip [PR 10.2]), plus the admin-recordings route's three repos (extended-ContinuousRecording, SessionChatMessage, AdminReviewSettings) and AccountService's two new sibling repos (AccountStats, UserSession). AccountService is now a thin orchestrator over UserRepository + AccountStatsRepository + UserSessionRepository, with only the cascade-delete loop and the bcrypt/oauth flows remaining as inline logic. The success criterion from the roadmap is met. **Next phase**: Phase 11 — ViewBotClientService decomposition (HIGH risk, mode discovery + extraction); next free ADR slot is 0019. **Live smoke**: not strictly required (the repo-extracted code is behaviour-equivalent to the legacy inline form), but the maintainer can spot-check the user-money flow: signup → check `user_stats` row created → admin-award-points → check `points_transactions` audit row + balance → spend-points → confirm the guarded debit logic still rejects insufficient balance. Same for session lifecycle: login → check `user_sessions` row → logout → check row deleted → wait for TTL or trigger cleanup → check expired-row sweep.
- **`ClipService` repository extraction with atomic write wraps (PR 10.2, Phase 10 — second PR of Phase 10, applies [ADR-0015](docs/architecture/adr/0015-transaction-shape-for-multi-statement.md)).** Continues the repository-pattern rollout AND introduces the first production caller of the `withTransaction` helper (PR 7.1 / ADR-0015). 15 of the 18 inline `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites in [`server/services/ClipService.js`](server/services/ClipService.js) collapse to method calls on a new `ClipRepository`. The remaining 3 are cross-table JOINs against `users` (for the creator-username enrichment) and stay inline per the single-domain-repository convention. **The headline atomic-write addition**: the two multi-statement write paths in ClipService — `recordView` (audit-log INSERT + counter UPDATE) and `deleteClip` (clip_views DELETE + clips DELETE) — now wrap in `withTransaction(async (tx) => …)` scopes per [ADR-0015](docs/architecture/adr/0015-transaction-shape-for-multi-statement.md). Pre-PR-10.2 a crash between the two statements (or any unrelated tx claim on the shared sqlite3 handle) could leave: (a) for `recordView` — a clip_views row without the matching `clips.view_count` bump, or vice-versa; (b) for `deleteClip` — clip_views rows orphaned against a deleted clips row, or vice-versa. Both paths are now observably all-or-nothing. **Naming-divergence from roadmap brief**: the Phase 10 brief described the atomicization as wrapping ClipService's *CREATE* path ("clip + chat-message snapshot + view counter init"). Inspection of the current code shows that CREATE doesn't fit that description — `createLiveClip` runs ONE `INSERT INTO clips` statement and then fires `captureChatForClip` with an explicit `.catch()` (fire-and-forget, NOT awaited) and never writes to `clip_views` at all (the counter starts at 0; rows in `clip_views` are appended by `recordView`, not `createLiveClip`). The brief's described atomicization surface doesn't exist in this codebase as written; the genuinely-non-atomic multi-statement surfaces are `recordView` and `deleteClip`. PR 10.2 wraps those instead. CHANGELOG honesty over CHANGELOG fidelity-to-brief. **`ClipRepository` shape** ([new file](server/database/repository/ClipRepository.js)) — 15 methods across three tables. `clips`: `insertClip({...streamerUserId defaults to NULL...})` (consolidates the two legacy CREATE callsites into one method), `getClipById` (single-table SELECT *), `updateClipFields(clipId, fieldValues)` (dynamic SET-builder; appends `updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP`; returns `{changes: 0}` without hitting DB on empty input), `deleteClipById`, `incrementViewCount` (PR 5.1 / ADR-0013a atomic-counter shape preserved: `view_count = view_count + 1`), `setClipReady({filePath, thumbnailPath, fileSize})`, `setClipFailed`, `getStats` (5-column aggregate). `clip_views`: `findRecentView({clipId, userId, ipAddress})` (1-hour window via `datetime('now', '-1 hour')` literal preserved), `insertView`, `deleteViewsByClipId`. `clip_chat_messages`: `insertClipChatMessage` (single-row), `listChatByClip` (4-col projection, ASC), `countChatByClip` (returns `{count}`). **Transactional re-use pattern** (the ADR-0015 convention's first production application): callers wrap a multi-statement scope in `withTransaction(async (tx) => …)` and construct a temporary `new ClipRepository(tx)` *inside* the body. Every method on the temp repo's instance routes its SQL through the tx primitives. Pinned by an explicit unit test (the "a tx-bound repo routes its writes to the tx primitives" case in [`ClipRepository.test.js`](server/tests/database/repository/ClipRepository.test.js)) AND by the service-level test suite. **Inline by design** (3 callsites that did NOT move): (i) `getClip(clipId)` — `LEFT JOIN users` for creator-username display; (ii) `listClips(options)` — same `LEFT JOIN users` plus a count query against `clips c` that shares the dynamic WHERE-builder (extracting the count alone would force WHERE-builder duplication across service+repo, a clear lose); (iii) `getUserClips(userId, options)` — same JOIN. All three are annotated with `// **Inline by design**` comments naming PR 10.2 so future readers don't try to "complete" the extraction. The reasoning matches PR 6.3 + PR 10.1's convention exactly: single-domain repositories don't reach across tables. **Diff**: `server/services/ClipService.js` -74 / +92 (705 → 723 LoC; SQL bodies collapse but the new `withTransaction` wraps + the `// Inline by design` comments + the explicit `new ClipRepository(tx)` lines add a few lines back; the net +18 LoC is the legitimate cost of the atomic-wrap rationale comments). `server/database/repository/ClipRepository.js` +291 (new file, including 80 lines of JSDoc that cite ADR-0015 + ADR-0013a + the single-domain-repo convention). `server/tests/database/repository/ClipRepository.test.js` +321 (new test, 19 `describe` blocks × `it()` blocks × `describe.each` over USE_BETTER_SQLITE3 flag = **38 test cases** counted by Jest). `server/tests/services/ClipService.atomic-writes.test.js` +174 (new test, 7 `it()` blocks). Total: **+45 new test cases** (38 + 7). **Tests** — repository level: every method's SQL shape (whitespace-normalized) + parameter ordering pinned. `insertClip` gets two tests (streamerUserId-passed and streamerUserId-defaults-to-NULL paths). `updateClipFields` gets the dynamic-SET happy path + the empty-input short-circuit (no DB call, returns `{changes: 0}`). `incrementViewCount` pins the relative-arithmetic shape (`view_count = view_count + 1`, not read-then-write). Constructor section adds the **"a tx-bound repo routes its writes to the tx primitives"** test — the first explicit pin of the ADR-0015 dep-injection convention. Service level: the seven `ClipService.atomic-writes.test.js` cases pin both wrap surfaces. For `recordView`: (1) "inside one withTransaction scope" — `withTransaction` called once, both writes hit the tx primitives, base `runAsync` never touched; (2) "short-circuit path opens no tx scope" — if `findRecentView` returns a row, no tx is opened; (3) "INSERT precedes UPDATE" — causal ordering pinned in case a future refactor swaps them. For `deleteClip`: (4) "inside one withTransaction scope" — same shape; (5) "auth-fail does NOT open a tx scope" — the `'Not authorized'` throw happens before the wrap; (6) "clip_views DELETE precedes clips DELETE" — FK-safe ordering pinned (SQLite's `PRAGMA foreign_keys` is off in this codebase but a future on-toggle would make this ordering load-bearing); (7) "admin bypass opens the wrap" — `isAdmin=true` lets a non-owner delete and the wrap still happens. **Full suite**: **903/904 under `--runInBand`** (was 858/859 post-PR-9.3 on the slice that excludes the three new VisionBot test files — those files were added by the parallel VisionBot phase landing at PRs 142/143/146 and are slow under `--runInBand` due to the 5–10s LLM-call mocks they exercise; my baseline measurement uses the slice that excludes them, matching the same exclusion list pre- and post-PR-10.2; the absolute count including VisionBot files is also +45 from main but not measured here to avoid the noise). Same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` flake from the Phase 6 handoff — reproducible on `main` without this PR, untouched. **Risk**: MEDIUM per the Phase 10 brief (clip CREATE / read / delete is user-visible; rate-limit logic untouched; storage-service side-effects untouched). The atomic-wrap is a strict improvement — pre-PR-10.2 the multi-statement paths had no atomicity guarantee, so any consumer expecting atomicity was already losing. The wrap can't introduce new partial-state hazards. **Cross-references**: [ADR-0015](docs/architecture/adr/0015-transaction-shape-for-multi-statement.md) (transaction shape — first production caller); [ADR-0013a](docs/architecture/adr/0013a-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md) (atomic-counter shape preserved in `incrementViewCount`). **No new ADR** — both architectural decisions already exist; PR 10.2 is the first application. **Live smoke**: recommended but not strictly required — maintainer can hit `POST /api/clips/:clipId/view` rapidly enough that the 1-hour window matters (or wait an hour for the window to clear) to exercise the recordView wrap; `DELETE /api/clips/:clipId` for the deleteClip wrap. The wrap is observably indistinguishable from the legacy back-to-back path on the happy path; the difference is the error-/crash-path which can't be reasonably triggered in smoke. **`getStats` numerics**: the new `getStats()` repo method returns the same five-column aggregate row; the service still spreads it with the storage-stats object exactly as the legacy code did. **Phase 10 status**: 2/3 PRs done. Next: PR 10.3 (`AccountStatsRepository` + `UserSessionRepository`) closes the phase.
- **Admin-recordings route SQL extracted into repositories (PR 10.1, Phase 10 — first PR of Phase 10).** Continues the repository-pattern rollout. 20 of the 24 inline `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites in `server/routes/admin-recordings.js` collapse to method calls on three repositories — one **extended**, two **new**. The remaining 4 callsites are intentionally left inline and itemised below. **Repository touches**: (a) **`ContinuousRecordingRepository`** (extended from PR 6.3) gains 9 new methods covering the admin-side reads against `recording_sessions` and `recording_stream_segments`: `listSessionsForAdmin({status, streamer, dateFromMs, dateToMs, limit, offset})` (admin-paginated, LIKE-on-two-columns filter), `countSessionsForAdmin({...same filters minus pagination})` (matching count for the page header), `getSessionLocalPath(sessionId)` (narrow projection), `countAllSessions()` + `countSessionsByStatus(status)` (the 3-call `/status` endpoint collapses to two methods, one parameterised on status), `listSessionsWithLocalPathBasic()` / `listSessionsWithLocalPathFull()` / `listSessionsWithLocalPathIdsOnly()` (three projections of `WHERE local_path IS NOT NULL ORDER BY start_time ASC` — 5/7/2 columns respectively, one per consumer site), and `listStreamSegmentsSince(sinceMs)` (9-column timeline projection). (b) **`SessionChatMessageRepository`** (new file, [`server/database/repository/SessionChatMessageRepository.js`](server/database/repository/SessionChatMessageRepository.js)) owns `session_chat_messages` with two methods: `listBySession(sessionId, {fromMs, toMs})` (dynamic time bounds; **critical bound-check fix** — the legacy `if (fromMs)` skipped a `fromMs=0` value, which is a valid "from the recording start" bound; the repo uses `!== undefined && !== null` so `0` is preserved), and `countBySessionIds(sessionIds)` (batch `IN (?, ?, ...)` placeholder-generated; **defensive empty-array guard** returns `{count: 0}` rather than emitting an `IN ()` syntax-error SQL). (c) **`AdminReviewSettingsRepository`** (new file, [`server/database/repository/AdminReviewSettingsRepository.js`](server/database/repository/AdminReviewSettingsRepository.js)) owns `admin_review_settings` with two methods: `listAll()` (raw rows; route shapes the response) and `upsertSetting(key, value)` (the `INSERT … ON CONFLICT(key) DO UPDATE SET value = ?` shape — **value bound twice** to match the conflict-branch re-bind in the legacy SQL). Pre-extraction the route had three byte-identical UPSERTs that differed only in the hardcoded key literal; collapsed to one method called three times. **Inline by design** (4 callsites that did NOT move): (i) `url_streams` batch SELECT at admin-recordings.js:612 — cross-domain (URL-stream routing); (ii) `url_streams` LIKE-by-channel-id at :627 — cross-domain (same); (iii) `streaming_logs` IN-batch at :643 — cross-domain (audit log used only as a username-display fallback); (iv) the `session_chat_messages ⋈ recording_sessions` JOIN at :984 in the `/chat-stream` route — cross-table queries belong to the route layer per the single-domain-repository convention PR 6.3 set. These four are documented in a comment block at the top of `admin-recordings.js` and will be revisited if/when the URL-stream-routing and streaming-logs domains get their own repos. **Naming-divergence from roadmap brief**: the Phase 10 brief proposed a new `RecordingSessionRepository` + `AdminReviewSettingsRepository`. `ContinuousRecordingRepository` (PR 6.3) already owned `recording_sessions` and `recording_stream_segments`; creating a sibling repo against the same tables would split single-table ownership across two files (a known smell). The extension absorbs the 14 admin-side callsites into the existing repo and PR 10.1 adds **two** new repos for the **genuinely-new** tables: `session_chat_messages` and `admin_review_settings`. The "two new repos" headline count is preserved — it just trades the speculatively-named `RecordingSessionRepository` for `SessionChatMessageRepository`. Documented in the extended repo's class JSDoc + this entry. **Diff**: `server/routes/admin-recordings.js` -116 / +24 (1074 → 982 net = -92 LoC, mostly from inlined SQL strings collapsing to single-line repo calls + the count-SQL `sql.replace('SELECT *', 'SELECT COUNT(*) as count')` trickery at the old line 121 being replaced with a structurally-shared filters object); `server/database/repository/ContinuousRecordingRepository.js` +159 (9 new methods + extended docstring, 231 → 390); `server/database/repository/SessionChatMessageRepository.js` +95 (new file); `server/database/repository/AdminReviewSettingsRepository.js` +65 (new file). Total new repo LoC: +319 (above the brief's ~250 estimate, driven by the 9-method ContinuousRecording extension the brief did not predict, plus the JSDoc convention from PR 6.3 / PR 7.x that documents each method's legacy callsite — kept for parity with the existing entries). **`sql.replace` trickery removed**: pre-PR-10.1 the route built the WHERE clause once and ran `sql.replace('SELECT *', 'SELECT COUNT(*) as count')` to derive the count query. The two repo methods rebuild the WHERE-fragments independently from the same filters object — clearer contract, no implicit replace-once dependency. **Behaviour-preserving, not byte-equivalent**: indentation whitespace collapses; the dynamic-bound check in `listBySession` is **a behaviour-change documented in the test** — `fromMs=0` previously dropped the WHERE fragment, now correctly preserves it. Inspection of the chat-message playback code suggests no consumer was depending on the bug, but the change is called out for honesty rather than hidden. **Sequencing within Phase 10**: PR 10.1 is the easiest of the three Phase 10 PRs (read-mostly route extraction; no atomic-CREATE wrap; no cross-service write paths). PR 10.2 (`ClipRepository` + `withTransaction`-wrapped CREATE) follows; PR 10.3 (`AccountStatsRepository` + `UserSessionRepository`) closes the phase. **Tests**: 54 new test cases across three files (jest `describe.each` × USE_BETTER_SQLITE3 backend-flag parameterisation, matching the precedent set in PR 6.3 / PR 5.x). [`server/tests/database/repository/ContinuousRecordingRepository.test.js`](server/tests/database/repository/ContinuousRecordingRepository.test.js) adds 9 new `describe` blocks (16 `it()` blocks × 2 flags = 32 new test cases) covering each new method's SQL shape + parameter ordering; `listSessionsForAdmin` gets three dedicated tests (no-options baseline with limit+offset always trailing, streamer-LIKE-wrap on both placeholders, full happy-path with all four filter fragments in documented order); `countSessionsForAdmin` gets the matching-shape test + an empty-options test confirming raw `{count}` row shape. ### Fixed
- **Recording-cleanup vs upload-retry data-loss race (PR 8.4, Phase 8).** Fourth and final functional PR of Phase 8 (reliability hardening). Closes the database half of the cleanup-vs-upload race documented in [`docs/architecture/background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) under "Notable hazards → Recording cleanup races recording upload". PR 2.6 already closed the **filesystem** half (`ContinuousRecordingService.cleanupOldRecordings` skips directories whose `recording_sessions.b2_file_id IS NULL`); this PR closes the matching gap in `RecordingCleanupScheduler.runCleanup` which deletes the `recording_sessions` **database row** (and the B2 file if present) after retention. Pre-fix SQL was `WHERE start_time < ? AND status IN ('completed', 'uploaded')` — age + status only, with no `b2_file_id` check. If B2 was down for a long stretch (and `RecordingUploadScheduler` was retrying every 30 min with `localBufferHours=2` initial wait), the DB row could be deleted before the upload ever succeeded — silent loss of the metadata binding to whatever remained of the local segments. **Fix**: the cleanup SQL now reads `WHERE start_time < ? AND status IN ('completed', 'uploaded') AND (b2_file_id IS NOT NULL OR start_time < ?)` where the second bind is `cutoff - retryWindowMs`. **Semantics**: an UPLOADED session (`b2_file_id IS NOT NULL`) gets cleaned at the normal retention boundary. An UN-uploaded session gets the retry-window extension — its effective deletion boundary is `retentionDays + retryWindowMs`, giving the upload scheduler that extra time to finish retrying. After retention + retryWindow elapses, the safety-valve OR fires and the un-uploaded row is deleted anyway (else a permanently-failed upload would leak local storage and DB rows forever). **Configuration**: new constructor option `retryWindowMs` defaults to 24 h. `retryWindowMs: 0` is the explicit opt-out for operators in storage-pressure emergencies (restores pre-PR-8.4 behavior). **`getStatus` mirrored**: the admin status endpoint's `pendingDeletion` count uses the same SQL filter so the next tick's actual delete count matches what the API reports. New `retryWindowMs` and `extendedCutoffTime` fields are surfaced in the response so admins can see why an expected-to-be-cleaned session is still around. **Tests**: 9 new `it()` blocks in `server/tests/services/RecordingCleanupScheduler.upload-race.test.js`: (a) UPLOADED session past retention → deleted; (b) UN-uploaded past retention but within retry window → SURVIVES (the headline fix); (c) UN-uploaded past retention + retry window → deleted (safety valve); (d) fresh sessions never touched; (e) mixed batch correctly discriminates per-session; (f) status filter still rejects `'recording'` / `'failed'` sessions regardless of age; (g) `getStatus.pendingDeletion` reflects the new filter; (h) constructor default = 24 h; (i) `retryWindowMs: 0` opt-out path. The test replicates the new SQL filter in the DB mock so the bind-shape matches production exactly; the assertions exercise the real `runCleanup` and `getStatus` paths. Full suite: **845/846 under `--runInBand`** (same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` flake from the Phase 6 handoff; reproducible on main without this PR; 9/9 new tests pass). **Risk**: MEDIUM (data-loss avoidance — the fix is small and the test covers each branch of the new SQL guard). **No ADR** — single-statement SQL-clause addition without an architectural decision; the design is fully described in this entry and in the in-file comments. **Honesty**: the existing `RecordingCleanupScheduler.deleteSession` still deletes the B2 file via `b2Storage.deleteFile(session.b2_file_name)` before deleting the DB row — that order is preserved, and a deletion that gets past the new guard already has `b2_file_name` set (or null, in which case the B2 call is a no-op for un-uploaded safety-valve deletions). No change to the per-row delete flow; the fix is at the **filter** level only.

the extraction is straightforward (behavior-equivalent to the now-merged PR 9.2 inline block), the 13 new unit tests pin the contract, and there's no behavior-change surface. **Live smoke**: not strictly required for PR 9.3 (extraction is behavior-equivalent to the smoked PR 9.2 inline), but the same dual-backend smoke from PR 9.2 would re-prove the extraction observably equivalent. **Phase 9 closure**: `server/index.js` ends Phase 9 at 5622 lines (started Phase 9 at 5762 → 5762 after PR 9.1 docs-only → 5762 after PR 9.2 -100 LoC → 5622 after PR 9.3 -140 LoC). The 5100-line success criterion from `phases-6-plus.md` §"Phase 9" is **NOT hit** — Phase 9 cleared the if/else branch and lifted the aligned block out, but the broader 5100-target work (moderation pipeline, ViewBotClientService init, ViewBotRotationService init, ChatBot init, etc.) is Phase 10 / Phase 11 / Phase 12 scope.
