Phase 9's three PRs delivered the alignment-and-extraction of the ADR-0012-flagged headline target as scoped, and the surviving in-file orchestration is now topical (mediasoup init → ViewBot factory → SimpleViewBotRotation.setStreamService → whitelistService → moderation pipeline → streamingBackend → viewbotService → recording + clips → ViewBotClientService → globals → ViewBotRotationService + UnifiedViewBotRotation + PortMonitor → ViewBot API routes). The "two near-identical blocks added by hand" hazard PR 3.1 / PR 4.2 / PR-W4 / PR-M3 grew is closed: new streaming-backend features now live in one module, not two.

### Changed
- **MediaSoup/LiveKit branch alignment in `startServer()` (PR 9.2, Phase 9 — applies [ADR-0017](docs/architecture/adr/0017-mediasoup-livekit-alignment-plan.md)).** Second PR of Phase 9. Implements the per-divergence recommendations from PR 9.1's archaeology doc ([`docs/architecture/plans/mediasoup-livekit-divergences.md`](docs/architecture/plans/mediasoup-livekit-divergences.md)). The ~261-line `if (!livekitService) { … MediaSoup branch … } else { … LiveKit branch … }` block in `server/index.js`'s `startServer()` collapses to ~123 lines of hoisted common orchestration plus a single ~46-line `if (livekitService) { … }` block of legitimately LiveKit-only wires. **Diff**: `server/index.js` -235 / +135 = net -100 LoC (5862 → 5762 → 5771 after C1 reviewer fix). **What hoisted (10 divergences classified as `accidental` in PR 9.1)**: D1 `new ViewBotURLService()` + `URLStreamHealthService` construction + `.start()` + `source-offline` / `stream-stale` handlers; D5 `new RandomStreamRotationService()` + setters + global; D6 `ModerationActionArbiter` wiring (`if (moderationService)`); D7 `WhitelistEnforcer` wiring (`if (whitelistService)`); D8 `/api/random-stream` route mount; D9 `lifecycleManager.schedule` autostart — schedule name unified from `'random-rotation-autostart-mediasoup'` / `'-livekit'` to `'random-rotation-autostart'` (verified by `grep -rn 'random-rotation-autostart'` across `server/ chat-service/ client/src/ scripts/`: only the new schedule site appears, no other readers); D11 `(MediaSoup backend)` log suffix stripped from 4 log lines (verified by `grep -rn '(MediaSoup backend)'` across `server/ chat-service/ client/src/ scripts/ docs/operations/runbooks/`: no log-based alerts or grep callers depend on the suffix); D12 URL-service rotation-registration shared steps hoisted, LiveKit-only cross-wire kept inside the surviving guard. **What stayed branch-specific (2 divergences classified as `intentional`)**: D2 `viewBotURLService.setSocketIO(io)` + `setStreamNotifier(streamNotifier)` — the PR 3.1 deliberate-dormancy guard. The two setters wire emit paths inside `ViewBotURLService._handleStreamEnd` / `stopURLStream` that the MediaSoup branch deliberately keeps suppressed via internal `if (this.io)` / `if (this.streamNotifier)` guards. Verified: `ViewBotURLService` constructor (lines 20–76) never assigns `this.io` or `this.streamNotifier`; both remain `undefined` until the setters run, and the internal guards at `ViewBotURLService.js:289, 349, 1199, 1272, 1484` continue to short-circuit in MediaSoup mode. **Wiring these on the MediaSoup rollback path (ADR-0008) would silently activate two previously-dormant socket-emit paths.** A 9-line in-file comment block at the new location preserves the rationale and explicitly forbids moving the setters out of the guard without a separate behaviour-change PR + smoke pass. D3 LiveKit-only service registrations (`SimpleViewBotRotation.setLiveKitService`, `viewBotURLService.setLiveKitService`, `viewBotLiveKitService.setURLViewBotService`) and D10 LiveKit-only lifecycle (`global.viewBotLiveKitService`, `livekitService.startStreamerHealthCheck`) — these are LiveKit-only by definition. **What deleted (1 divergence classified as `stale`)**: D4 line 5126's `✅ VIEWBOT: Registered StreamService with SimpleViewBotRotation for real streamer protection` log line. PR-I4 (`539fa757`, 2026-05-23) hoisted the underlying `setStreamService` call out of the branch to line 4856; the log line that announced it stayed behind. Now deleted. Verified safe by `grep -rn 'Registered StreamService with SimpleViewBotRotation'`: only the archaeology doc references the string; no test, runbook, or alert depends on it. **`if (livekitService)` block structure (post-reviewer C1 fix)**: the surviving guard is divided into three labeled sub-zones — (a) rotation + LiveKit-service cross-wires, (b) PR 3.1 deliberate-dormancy zone marked `DO NOT MOVE` with the 9-line rationale comment, (c) LiveKit-process lifecycle. The labeled fences resist the "two near-identical blocks added by hand" pattern PR 3.1 / PR 4.2 / PR-W4 / PR-M3 grew. **Reviewer subagent**: general-purpose reviewer with a harsh adversarial prompt before push. Found 0 blockers + 3 concerns: (C1) the `if (livekitService)` block lacks visible sub-zone fences for future maintainers — addressed by folding in the (a)/(b)/(c) labels and the `DO NOT MOVE` marker on the dormancy zone in the same commit; (C2) ADR-0017 open-question #4 asked the reviewer to verify `startStreamerHealthCheck`'s interval clears on shutdown — verified at `LiveKitService.js:596–700` (`stop()` → `stopStreamerHealthCheck` → `clearInterval(this.healthCheckTimer)`) and `stoppables.push(livekitService)` at `server/index.js:4838`; the leaked-interval hazard PR 9.3's extraction would inherit is closed; (C3) record the grep results for D9 + D11 in the PR body — done above. All concerns addressed before push; no follow-up commit needed. **Boot-window reorder safety**: the reviewer verified that `RandomStreamRotationService`, `WhitelistEnforcer`, `URLStreamHealthService`, and `/api/url-stream` route handlers do not read `viewBotURLService.io` / `viewBotURLService.streamNotifier` / `viewBotURLService.liveKitService` synchronously during the boot window between the hoisted construction and the `if (livekitService)` block. Health-service + enforcer use `setInterval` (next-tick), the lifecycle-autostart fires at +5 s, by which time the `if (livekitService)` block has executed. The reorder is observably equivalent to the prior LiveKit-branch ordering. **Tests**: not modified — same 845/846 under `--runInBand` (same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` flake from Phase 6 handoff; reproducible on `main` without this PR). **Risk**: HIGH per Phase 9 plan (production-path on both backends). **Live smoke required on BOTH backends before merge** per [ADR-0008](docs/architecture/adr/0008-revive-livekit-for-url-streams-and-recording.md)'s rollback procedure — toggle `USE_WEBRTC_ADAPTER` between true/false and walk [`docs/getting-started/first-stream.md`](docs/getting-started/first-stream.md) (streamer takeover + URL relay smoke + WhitelistEnforcer tick + ActionArbiter wiring observable + random rotation autostart). The autonomous agent cannot run the full smoke (needs webcam + real takeover flow); maintainer smoke is the gate. **MediaSoup-mode-specific smoke check**: trigger a stop on a URL stream while in `USE_WEBRTC_ADAPTER=false` mode; tail the server log and confirm NO new `stream-ended` / `stream-started` socket emits show up — proves the D2 dormancy is intact. **No new ADR** — the alignment fixes are governed by [ADR-0017](docs/architecture/adr/0017-mediasoup-livekit-alignment-plan.md) from PR 9.1; this PR is the implementation.

### Added
- **VisionBot — multi-modal screenshot commentary bot ([ADR-0018](docs/architecture/adr/0018-visionbot-screenshot-comments.md)).** Sibling of MovieBot. On each transcription-window completion, captures a still frame from the LiveKit Egress HLS recording aligned to the transcription's `endTime` (NOT "now" — Whisper has 5–30 s latency so the latest segment is content after the transcript), pairs it with the transcript, and sends the pair to Groq's Llama 4 Scout vision model. Posts the commentary through the existing chatbot accounts. Defaults to disabled. Shipped as a 4-PR sequence: (1) `refactor(bots): extract TranscriptionDrivenBotService` — pure refactor of MovieBotService boilerplate into a shared base class (no behavior change); (2) `feat(visionbot): EgressFrameCaptureService` — server-side ffmpeg frame extraction from the egress HLS playlist with second-newest-segment selection (avoids partial-write), SIGTERM/SIGKILL escalation at 6s/8s, concurrency cap of 2, 10s cache invalidated on `streamGeneration` change (takeover safety), 1-hour default audit-copy retention with hourly purge; (3) `feat(visionbot): generateVisionComment LLM method` — OpenAI-compatible Groq call with base64 `image_url` content part, typed `GroqRateLimitError` / `GroqUnavailableError`, AbortSignal propagation, Authorization-header redaction in error logs, prompt-injection defense (untrusted-image-content disclaimer in both system + user roles); (4) `feat(visionbot): VisionBotService + admin routes + DB migration + ADR + CHANGELOG` — orchestrator service with BotEventBus subscription to `moviebot-transcription-complete` (deduped + filtered by streamerId), own scheduler when MovieBot is disabled, hard cap of 3 bots per cycle (admin-configurable up to 5), persisted exponential backoff state on Groq 429 (30s × 2^failures, capped 30 min), `VISIONBOT_KILL_SWITCH` env var for emergency disable, URL-relay refusal unless `allow_url_relay=1` (TOS — relayed streams carry third-party copyright), stream-takeover guard at emit time (snapshot+verify `streamGeneration`), redacted `exact_prompt` in `chatbot_message_history` (no raw chat usernames / no raw transcription alongside the frame audit metadata), `visionbot_config` singleton table, `chatbots.vision_bot_enabled` and `users.vision_audit_optout` columns, `/admin/visionbot/{enable,disable,status,config,logs}` endpoints behind `adminKeyAuth` matching the MovieBot pattern. New tests: `TranscriptionDrivenBotService.test.js` (17), `EgressFrameCaptureService.test.js` (12 — mocks `child_process.spawn` so no ffmpeg dependency), `ChatBotLLMService.vision.test.js` (10 — mocks `global.fetch`), `VisionBotService.test.js` (16). `services.test.js` updated for the two new bag entries (`egressFrameCaptureService`, `visionBotService`). Note: ADR slot renumbered from 0017 → 0018 in resolution merge — PR 9.1 had claimed 0017 (`0017-mediasoup-livekit-alignment-plan.md`) while this PR series was in flight. Risk: MEDIUM — new external API dependency (Groq Scout single point of failure on the model, accepted in v1 per ADR), new disk write path under `logs/visionbot/frames/`, new ffmpeg subprocess. Mitigated by kill-switch, persisted backoff, hard fan-out cap, retention purge, structured skip-reason taxonomy in the status payload. **Deferred to follow-up PRs**: `BotsPanel.tsx` UI panel (server + endpoints work via curl / Postman in this PR; UI wiring needs its own client RTL tests), OpenAI / Gemini fallback provider, `users.vision_audit_optout` enforcement at the FrameCaptureService write path, per-streamer prompts, TTS output, frame-content pre-classifier. See ADR-0018 for the full decision record including the four critical fixes (frame-transcript sync window, EventEmitter double-fire avoidance via BotEventBus, takeover-race guard, ffmpeg lifecycle) caught during the design-review red-team pass.

- **MediaSoup/LiveKit branch divergence archaeology (PR 9.1, Phase 9 — [ADR-0017](docs/architecture/adr/0017-mediasoup-livekit-alignment-plan.md), docs-only).** First PR of Phase 9 (`server/index.js` MediaSoup/LiveKit alignment + extraction). No code change — an archaeology PR that classifies every divergence between the two backend branches in `startServer()` and writes a per-divergence recommended fix that PR 9.2 will implement. Output: new [`docs/architecture/plans/mediasoup-livekit-divergences.md`](docs/architecture/plans/mediasoup-livekit-divergences.md) + new [ADR-0017](docs/architecture/adr/0017-mediasoup-livekit-alignment-plan.md). **Why this PR exists**: [ADR-0012](docs/architecture/adr/0012-startserver-decomposition-partial.md) flagged the ~500-line `if (!livekitService) { … } else { … }` branch in `startServer()` as Phase 4's biggest acknowledged deferral. [ADR-0008](docs/architecture/adr/0008-revive-livekit-for-url-streams-and-recording.md) then revived LiveKit as the production backend, making both branches live code. Of the four feature PRs that landed in `startServer()` in the last week (PR 3.1, PR 4.2, PR-W4, PR-M3), three added two near-identical blocks by hand into the two branches; PR-M3's own comments are self-aware about the duplication. The roadmap's Red-team #2 caught that "alignment is HOURS of investigation per divergence, not ~50–150 LoC of changes" — splitting the archaeology into its own PR makes the work shape honest. **Findings**: 13 divergences across 11 categories. Catalog classifies each as **intentional** (2 sites), **accidental** (10 sites), or **stale** (1 site). The headline divergence is **D2** — the PR 3.1 deliberately-suppressed `viewBotURLService.setSocketIO(io)` + `setStreamNotifier(streamNotifier)` on the MediaSoup branch, with a 9-line code comment at `server/index.js:5000–5008` explaining that wiring them would silently activate two previously-dormant emit paths in MediaSoup-mode production. PR 9.2 must preserve that dormancy. The 10 accidental-duplication divergences (URLStreamHealthService event handlers, `RandomStreamRotationService` construction, `ModerationActionArbiter` wiring, `WhitelistEnforcer` wiring, route mount, `lifecycleManager.schedule` autostart, comment-text drift, `(MediaSoup backend)` log-suffix on 4 sites, etc.) are all byte-equivalent bodies whose only divergence is comment text and one schedule name — they hoist cleanly. The stale divergence is line 5126's `✅ VIEWBOT: Registered StreamService with SimpleViewBotRotation for real streamer protection` log line; PR-I4 (`539fa757`) hoisted the actual `setStreamService` call out of the branch back on 2026-05-23 but didn't delete the log line that announced it — the log has been lying about a registration that no longer happens locally for 4 days. **Sequencing**: PR 9.2 must apply the 10 hoists in dependency order (`new ViewBotURLService` first → `new RandomStreamRotationService` → ActionArbiter + WhitelistEnforcer which both read rotation → route mount + autostart) so each intermediate state stays correct. **Post-PR-9.2 shape** (documented in the archaeology doc): the 261-line if/else collapses to ~130 lines of hoisted common orchestration + a single ~15-line `if (livekitService) { … }` block holding the deliberate-intentional asymmetries (D2's two setters, the three LiveKit-only service registrations, the LiveKit-only `setURLViewBotService` cross-wire, the LiveKit-only `global.viewBotLiveKitService` + `startStreamerHealthCheck`). **PR 9.3** then extracts that aligned block into `server/bootstrap/start-streaming-backend.js` via the same shape as the [`start-listeners.js`](server/bootstrap/start-listeners.js) extraction from PR 4.3. **Risk**: NONE — docs-only. **Tests**: not modified. **Live smoke**: not required for PR 9.1 (docs-only); **mandatory for PR 9.2** on both backends per [ADR-0008](docs/architecture/adr/0008-revive-livekit-for-url-streams-and-recording.md)'s rollback procedure (toggle `USE_WEBRTC_ADAPTER` between true/false and walk the streaming smoke). **No reviewer subagent** for PR 9.1 — the analysis IS the doc; the value is correctness of the per-divergence classification, which the maintainer can spot-check by re-reading the cited line numbers + `git blame` output. The reviewer pass is mandatory for PR 9.2. **ADR-0017** documents the staged plan (PR 9.1 archaeology → PR 9.2 align → PR 9.3 extract), explicitly names the rejected alternatives (skip archaeology and dedupe by inspection during 9.2; align + extract in a single PR; extract with the if/else intact), and pins D2 as the load-bearing classification that PR 9.2's reviewer must specifically verify. **ADR register**: 0017 added; next free slot is 0018 (reserved for PR 11.1 — ViewBotClientService decomposition outcome). **Suite count**: 845/846 under `--runInBand` — same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` flake from the Phase 6 handoff; not touched by this PR. **Honesty**: the doc says "9 lines of code comment" at lines 5000–5008 for D2; that count is the comment block from `// PR 3.1 (post-review fix)` through `// activate two previously-dormant emit paths in MediaSoup-mode` — verify by reading those lines if a future contributor edits the comment. The doc also names "the merge tip of PR 8.4 (PR #138)" as the line-range basis; future renumbering as `server/index.js` is edited is expected, but the if/else **structure** (the divergence anchors) is stable.

- **ViewBot child-process force-reap on shutdown (PR 8.3, Phase 8 — extends [ADR-0011](docs/architecture/adr/0011-lifecycle-manager.md)).** Third PR of Phase 8 (reliability hardening). Closes the orphan-process leak documented in [`docs/operations/runbooks/viewbot-fleet-misbehaving.md`](docs/operations/runbooks/viewbot-fleet-misbehaving.md): a ViewBot `gst-launch-1.0` spawned by `SimpleViewBotRotation` whose lifecycle is interrupted (server SIGTERM mid-rotation, lifecycle exception during teardown) was being orphaned because the legacy `global.processManager.trackProcess(...)` registration paths were no-ops (the global was never assigned, so the typeof-guarded calls silently did nothing). **Mechanism**: extends the existing `ProcessManager` singleton with `reapAll({ graceMs = 2000 })` / `stop()` methods, wired into the shutdown loop's `stoppables` array immediately before `lifecycleManager`. The reaper iterates every tracked PID: skip if already dead at entry; otherwise SIGTERM via process-group kill (negative-PID), poll every 100 ms until grace expires, then SIGKILL anything still alive. Both signal phases are gated by a comm-snapshot PID-reuse defense — `/proc/<pid>/comm` is captured at register time and re-read before each signal; if it drifted, the kernel recycled the PID into an unrelated process and the signal is skipped (better to leak a real orphan than to SIGTERM/SIGKILL an innocent sshd). The signal-send path tries process-group kill first (cheaper, brings down gst-launch + children together) and falls back to direct-PID kill if the process wasn't a group leader. **Production-path coverage**: the registry call in `SimpleViewBotRotation.startMediaSoupBot` now actually populates via `processManager.registerProcess(bot.id, 'gstreamer', this.gstreamerProcess.pid)`; the gst-launch spawn gains `detached: true` (non-Windows) so the child becomes its own process-group leader — matches the precedent in `ViewBotClientService` and ensures the reaper's negative-PID kill targets the gst-launch group, not Node's own PGID. A natural-exit handler (`gstreamerProcess.once('exit', ...)`) deregisters via `processManager.onBotStopped(bot.id)` so the registry doesn't accumulate ghost PIDs that could collide with PID-reused unrelated processes at shutdown time. **Stoppables ordering**: `processManager` sits immediately above `lifecycleManager` in the factory array — reverse-iteration of `stoppables` runs `lifecycleManager.stop()` FIRST (cancel deferred work), then `processManager.stop()` (reap straggler PIDs). ViewBot stoppables (`viewbotService`, `viewBotClientService`) are pushed AFTER the factory array in `server/index.js`, so they actually drain BEFORE `processManager` — their per-bot `stop()` paths call `processManager.onBotStopped(botId)` and the registry is near-empty in the happy path. The reaper exists for the **unhappy path** (a service crashed mid-`stop()`, or a PID was registered but never deregistered). **Recording-write safety**: ffmpeg PIDs from `ContinuousRecordingService` / `RecordingService` / `ClipProcessorService` (which write recording segments to disk) are NEVER registered with `ProcessManager` — the reaper has no way to find or SIGKILL them. This invariant is now pinned by a static test (`ProcessManager.scope invariant`) that greps `server/services/` for `processManager.registerProcess` callsites and asserts none appear in Recording/Clip/Transcription paths. **Scope deferred (called out in ADR amendment)**: Puppeteer-managed Chrome PIDs across `WebRTCViewBot`, `ViewBotClientService`, and `TranscriptionAudioAdapter` — these have a `browser.close()` canonical-shutdown path; folding them into the registry requires threading through Puppeteer's internal process map and is deferred. `ViewBotURLService` / general ffmpeg PIDs are also out of scope per the PR brief. **Tests**: 16 new `it()` blocks in `server/tests/services/ProcessManager.reaper.test.js`: 12 deps-injected unit tests covering empty-registry, already-dead, SIGTERM-graceful-exit, SIGTERM-then-SIGKILL, PID-reuse defense (both signal phases), comm-match-doesn't-trip-defense, registry-cleared, `stop()` delegates with default `graceMs`, idempotency under concurrent invocation, multi-PID-per-bot, registry-not-corrupted-mid-iteration; plus 2 production-code-path integration tests that spawn real Node child processes (`process.on("SIGTERM", () => {})` to force the SIGKILL branch + already-dead PID); plus 2 scope-invariant tests that grep `server/services/` for non-ViewBot callers. Also +1 new `services.test.js` assertion pinning the `processManager`→`lifecycleManager` ordering. **Adversarial reviewer pass**: a general-purpose reviewer subagent found 3 blockers + 5 concerns, all addressed in the same commit before push: (1) `detached: true` added to the gst-launch spawn (negative-PID kill targets correct group); (2) exit-handler deregistration added (no ghost PIDs at shutdown); (3) SIGTERM phase also gated by comm-check (many daemons treat SIGTERM as clean-exit, so reuse-defense covers both signals, not just SIGKILL); plus idempotency guard, integration test against real child process, scope-invariant test for recording-services, ADR enumeration extended to include `TranscriptionAudioAdapter` puppeteer launches, ADR "calibrated against what" → "estimated" honesty fix, dead `trackProcess` alias removed. **Full suite**: 836/837 under `--runInBand` (1 pre-existing `database-better.test.js` flake from the Phase 6 handoff; 16/16 new reaper tests + 1 services-ordering test pass). **Risk**: MEDIUM — process kills during shutdown have sharp edges (PID reuse, mid-write race), all addressed via the comm-snapshot defense + the recording-services scope invariant. **Cross-phase pin**: must close before PR 12.3 (trace IDs), so Phase 12 doesn't need to retrofit trace IDs into child-process logging. Pinned first.

- **ViewBot rotation tick-loop watchdog (PR 8.2, Phase 8 — [ADR-0016](docs/architecture/adr/0016-tick-loop-watchdog-observability-only.md)).** Second PR of Phase 8 (reliability hardening). Closes the runbook hazard at [`docs/operations/runbooks/viewbot-fleet-misbehaving.md`](docs/operations/runbooks/viewbot-fleet-misbehaving.md) where an unhandled exception inside `rotateToNextBot()` breaks the `setTimeout` chain and the rotation freezes on one channel with no operator signal. **Mechanism**: each sub-rotation (`SimpleViewBotRotation`, `WebRTCViewBotRotation`) records `this.lastTickAt = Date.now()` at the **entry** of every `rotateToNextBot()` (before any early-return guards, so the watchdog also notices "blocked by real streamer" wedges — distinguished via the log context). `UnifiedViewBotRotation` runs a `setInterval` watchdog (every 30 s in production, injectable for tests) that fires a `level: error` log line when `isRotating === true && activeRotation.lastTickAt != null && Date.now() - lastTickAt > activeRotation.settings.maxRotationInterval * 2`. The log line carries structured context (`event: viewbot-rotation-stalled`, `mode`, `backend`, `sinceLastTickMs`, `thresholdMs`, `maxRotationIntervalMs`, `isRotating`, `realStreamerActive`) so a future structured-logging pipeline (Phase 12) can route on `event` without parsing free-text. **The watchdog deliberately does NOT restart the rotation**: red-team #2 caught that "restart on top of a still-hung promise just queues a second hung promise" — `stopRotation()`/`startRotation()` from inside the watchdog runs concurrently with the original hung `rotateToNextBot()`, holding closures and locks, producing two competing rotation chains rather than a recovery. The supervisor restart (pm2) is the recovery agent; the watchdog wakes a human via the log line. ADR-0016 codifies log-and-alert as the chosen recovery mode and documents why active-restart is the wrong choice for hung event-loop code. **Constructor signature**: `UnifiedViewBotRotation` now accepts an optional 6th `deps = {}` parameter for test injection (`watchdogCheckMs`, `watchdogLogger`, `now`); existing 5-arg callsite in `server/index.js` is unchanged. The watchdog handle is stored on `this.watchdogInterval` per the [`docs/architecture/background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) "Owned" pattern, cleared in `stopRotation()` and (defensively) `shutdown()`. **Tests**: 10 new `it()` blocks in `server/tests/services/UnifiedViewBotRotation.watchdog.test.js` covering: fires when stale, does NOT fire when fresh / never-ticked / not-started, clears interval on stop, clears on shutdown, does NOT restart the sub-rotation (just logs), context includes mode + backend for structured-log filtering, and sub-rotation `lastTickAt` property contracts. Tests use jest fake timers + an injected clock + a spy logger; no real `setInterval` ever runs. Full suite: 819/820 under `--runInBand` (same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` "rejects on SQL syntax error" flake from the Phase 6 handoff; reproducible on main without these changes; 10/10 new tests pass). **Risk**: LOW — purely additive. No behavior change to the rotation tick itself; the only mutation in the existing tick path is setting `this.lastTickAt = Date.now()` at function entry. **Cross-phase pin**: when Phase 12 (observability / structured logging) lands, the watchdog log line is already structured for routing — no retrofit needed.

- **Atomic-SQL audit closure (PR 8.1, Phase 8 — docs-only).** First PR of Phase 8 (reliability hardening). No code change — a verification PR that documents what the six mutable-counter columns called out in the [ADR-0013a](docs/architecture/adr/0013a-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md) follow-up actually do at the write layer. Output is a new "Atomic-SQL audit closure" section in [`docs/architecture/background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) with a per-column classification table. **Findings**: five of the six counters use the relative-arithmetic `SET col = col + ?` pattern — `user_stats.total_stream_time`, `user_stats.total_view_time`, `user_stats.stream_count`, `user_stats.chat_message_count` all flow through `AccountService.updateUserStats`, and `clips.view_count` flows through `ClipService.incrementClipViews`. The remaining two writers are absolute-set but verified safe in context: `recording_sessions.chat_message_count` is a derived counter recomputed each tick by `SessionChatCaptureService.updateSessionChatCount` (`SELECT COUNT(*) FROM session_chat_messages` followed by absolute UPDATE) — a missed message becomes lag, not loss, because the next tick re-derives, and only one capture-service instance owns each session_id; `user_inventory.quantity` is absolute-set in `UserInventoryRepository.updateQuantity` (read-compute-write in `InventoryService.addItemToInventory`/`removeItemFromInventory`), and the only race-vulnerable caller (purchase) is closed by PR 7.4's `withTransaction` wrap — other callers are sequential per (user_id, item_id) under the single-streamer scope. The `quantity` columns on `item_transactions` and `gift_transactions` are also called out as **not** mutable counters — they're insert-only audit ledgers with no UPDATE/DELETE callsites anywhere in the codebase. **Why this PR even exists**: red-team #2 (per the Phase 6+ plan) verified that the originally-proposed PR 8.1 ("audit TimeTrackingService for read-compute-write hazard") was fixing a non-existent hazard — `TimeTrackingService` writes flow through `AccountService.updateUserStats`'s relative-arithmetic path. Rather than delete the slot entirely, the slot was repurposed to **document what was checked**, so a future contributor (or audit) can re-run the grep and have a baseline to compare against. The doc names the exact grep command (`grep -rnE "(SELECT|getAsync|allAsync|UPDATE).*(stream_time|view_time|chat_message_count|stream_count|quantity|view_count)" server/ --include='*.js' | grep -v tests/`) and what each row of output classified as. **Risk**: NONE — docs-only.

- **AI moderation pipeline — DB-backed global enforce toggle with admin-panel UI.** Replaces the boot-time-only `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE` env flag with a runtime-mutable, DB-backed singleton: an admin can now flip enforcement ON/OFF without a process restart, and the change is propagated to the live `ModerationActionArbiter` instance via a new `setEnforce()` method. **New schema**: `moderation_global_config(id INTEGER PRIMARY KEY CHECK (id = 1), enforce INTEGER, updated_at, updated_by)` singleton, seeded with `enforce=0, updated_by='seed'`. **Env-flag upgrade path**: on first install / pre-toggle-build upgrade, if the row still carries the `'seed'` marker AND `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE=true` in env, `ModerationService._loadGlobalConfig()` upgrades the row to `enforce=1, updated_by='env'` — operators whose env-flag was already enabling enforcement don't silently lose it. Once any admin has touched the row (via the UI or the API), the env is permanently ignored. **`ModerationService` new methods**: `isEnforced()` (in-memory cache read), `getGlobalConfig()` (DB row for UI), `setEnforce(enforce, adminId)` (DB write + arbiter propagation), plus internal `_loadGlobalConfig()` invoked from `initialize()` between cache load and event subscription. The constructor-injected arbiter is now synced to the DB value during init (covers the case where the arbiter was passed via deps and then init loaded the authoritative value), in addition to the existing `setActionArbiter()` sync (which covers late-injected arbiters). **`ModerationActionArbiter` new method**: `setEnforce(value)` — mutates `this.enforce` so the next `arbitrate()` call uses the new value without a restart. **New API endpoints** under `/api/moderation-ai`: `GET /global-config` (returns `{row: { enforce, updated_at, updated_by }}`) and `POST /global-config` body `{enforce: boolean}` (writes DB + propagates to arbiter + returns `{ok, enforce}`). Both `authenticateAdmin`. The POST handler rejects non-boolean `enforce` with 400 — guards against truthy-but-not-true values like `1` or `'true'` silently flipping to ON. **Admin UI**: a new top-of-tab card on the existing AI Moderation tab in AdminPanelV3 shows ENFORCING/LOG-ONLY status with a red/green theme, a one-click Turn ON / Turn OFF button, the last-changed timestamp + actor, and a description block of exactly what enforcement does (bans webcam streamers, blocklists URL-relay sources). The Turn ON path triggers a `window.confirm` dialog spelling out the consequences (real bans on false positives; reversible via the events tab) so an admin can't accidentally flip it. The Turn OFF path skips the confirm (turning off is the safer direction). **`server/index.js` wiring**: the existing ActionArbiter construction still passes the env-flag-derived value as the initial `enforce` (paranoid fallback for the case where ModerationService failed to init), but the canonical source is now the DB and the env value is overridden immediately on `moderationService.setActionArbiter(arbiter)`. **Tests**: 6 new ModerationService tests covering initialize-reads-seeded-row, setEnforce-writes-DB-and-propagates-to-arbiter, idempotency-and-round-trip, env-flag-upgrade-on-first-install, env-flag-does-NOT-override-admin-set-value, and setActionArbiter-syncs-to-late-injected-arbiter. 4 new route tests covering GET /global-config, POST /global-config { enforce: true }, POST /global-config { enforce: false }, and 400-on-non-boolean. 728/728 server tests pass (+10 new). TypeScript compiles cleanly against the updated admin UI component. **Adjacent bug found-and-fixed during test development**: prior to this PR, a constructor-injected arbiter was NOT synced with the DB enforce state — only `setActionArbiter()` calls did the sync, so a server that passed the arbiter via `new ModerationService({ ..., actionArbiter })` and then ran `initialize()` would end up with `arbiter.enforce` stuck at whatever the deps-bag initial value was, ignoring the DB. Fixed by moving the propagation into `_loadGlobalConfig()` so it covers both injection paths.
- **`ShopService.purchaseItem` atomic refactor + ShopRepository mutation half (PR 7.4, Phase 7 — closes Phase 7).** Final and highest-risk PR of Phase 7. Wraps the multi-statement money flow of `purchaseItem` in the PR 7.1 `withTransaction` helper. The five-step body is: (1) `accountService.subtractPoints` (atomic guarded UPDATE per ADR-0013a, INSIDE the tx so a downstream throw rolls it back), (2) guarded `shopRepository.decrementStockLimit` (returns no row if stock < quantity → throw "Insufficient stock" → ROLLBACK), (3) inside-tx max-stack re-check (re-reads inventory; the pre-tx check is a UX fast-fail, this is the source of truth), (4) `inventoryService.addItemToInventory`, (5) `itemTransactionRepository.insertPurchase`. **What the helper buys**: if any step throws, ROLLBACK undoes ALL of: the user_stats UPDATE, the points_transactions INSERT (which AccountService writes inside subtractPoints), the inventory credit, and the item_transactions audit row. The Phase 7 roadmap's specific hazard — "server crashes between subtractPoints and the inventory INSERT, user paid for nothing" — closes in the same way: SQLite's standard recovery rolls back the un-committed tx on next open. **Scope-honest claim**: the helper makes the FIVE specific writes above all-or-nothing. It does NOT make the overall flow race-free against unrelated concurrent writes (the mutex serializes withTransaction scopes, but bare-runAsync writes elsewhere can still interleave per the documented sharp edge in ADR-0015). The audit log's `points_before` is now computed from the post-debit balance + totalCost (mathematically exact for the row's pre-our-UPDATE value), more accurate than the pre-tx read it replaces. **ShopRepository mutation half**: 4 new write methods extracted from ShopService — `insertShopItem` (7-col INSERT), `updateShopItemFields` (dynamic SET with allowlist-in-the-repo as defense in depth — keys outside the allowlist throw before any SQL touches the DB), `deleteShopItemById`, `decrementStockLimit` (guarded UPDATE ... RETURNING for the relative-arithmetic + cap-check shape; returns undefined when the guard fails so the caller can throw inside the tx). ShopService callsites now use only repositories. **Tests** (largest test addition in the phase): 25 new `it()` blocks across three files. (a) `server/tests/database/repository/ShopRepository.test.js` gains 8 write-method tests (insertShopItem, updateShopItemFields with allowlist accept + reject + empty-throw, deleteShopItemById, decrementStockLimit happy + guard-fail) × 2 backends = 16. (b) `server/tests/services/ShopService.purchaseItem.atomic.test.js` is NEW — 7 integration tests against real `:memory:` connections covering happy path, body-throw rollback, audit-write-failure rollback, intra-tx stock-guard rollback, intra-tx max-stack rollback, pre-tx insufficient-balance, pre-tx max-stack — × 2 backends = 14. (c) `server/tests/services/ShopService.purchaseItem.realAccount.test.js` is NEW — uses `jest.mock` to redirect `database.js`'s module-level wrappers to in-memory primitives, then constructs the REAL `AccountService` (not a stub) and verifies that the load-bearing claim of the atomic refactor — module-level runAsync/getAsync route through the tx scope — is true: 2 tests, one backend (sqlite3 only, because jest.mock pinning makes the better-sqlite3 toggle moot for this scenario). **Why the separate real-AccountService file**: the reviewer pass on PR 7.4 caught that the original atomic test used a stub AccountService, which wouldn't have exercised the actual production AccountService.subtractPoints + recordTransaction code path. The new file proves that under the actual production wiring, a body throw rolls back BOTH AccountService writes (the user_stats UPDATE AND the points_transactions audit INSERT) — the precise hazard that would have escaped the stub test. **Reviewer subagent pass** (MANDATORY for PR 7.4 per the roadmap): two BLOCKERS flagged (test-doesn't-cover-production-wiring + ADR-0015 overpromises crash-safety as "verified empirically"), both addressed in the same pre-push commit before this entry was written. Two CONCERNS flagged (stock-limit-can-go-negative + max-stack-overflow-window) — both fixed by moving the checks INTO the tx scope with guarded SQL and an inside-tx re-read respectively. Sharp-edge concerns (`updateShopItemFields` SQL surface, setImmediate-in-test brittleness) also addressed. **Live smoke through `docs/getting-started/first-stream.md` is OUTSTANDING**: the roadmap mandates a manual buff-purchase walkthrough before close, and the autonomous agent who built this PR cannot drive a UI. The integration tests cover the SQL-level atomicity claim; what they don't cover is the route handler, the Socket.IO emit shape, the React client's `points-updated` handling, and any WAL/busy_timeout interaction the file-backed production DB has but the `:memory:` test fixture doesn't. Maintainer is requested to walk first-stream.md's buy-an-item step end-to-end before merging. Full suite: 841/842 under `--runInBand` (same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` "rejects on SQL syntax error" flake from the Phase 6 handoff). **Risk**: HIGH per roadmap (money flow). Closes Phase 7.

- **`ShopRepository` (read-only methods) + `ItemTransactionRepository` extraction (PR 7.3, Phase 7).** Third PR of Phase 7. Two new repositories landed together because their callsites are interleaved in `ShopService` (a purchase reads shop_items, debits points, inserts into user_inventory, inserts into item_transactions, updates shop_items.stock_limit — splitting one repo per PR would have produced two awkward seams). **ShopRepository (read-only)**: 6 SELECT-shaped methods covering the customer-facing shop view (with availability-window filter), the admin shop list (no filter), the existence-check by item_id, the purchase-time single-row fetch, and the featured / discounted sub-views. **All JOINs to `items` live in this repo** — same precedent as BuffRepository (PR 6.2) and UserInventoryRepository (PR 7.2), because the SELECT shape is shop-centric and breaking the composite query into two repo calls plus a JS-side join would be a pessimization with no abstraction win. **ItemTransactionRepository**: 3 INSERT methods (one per transaction_type — purchase, sell, admin_grant) + 3 SELECT methods (per-user history, admin-facing aggregate, top-N popular items). The append-only-by-design table has no UPDATEs or DELETEs anywhere in the codebase; the repo deliberately exposes none. **The 3 INSERT methods are extracted now even though PR 7.4 will atomicize purchase**: the repo methods accept the dep-injection shape, so PR 7.4 will compose them under a `withTransaction` scope via the `tx` proxy without further refactoring. Same applies to InventoryService.grantItemsToUser (already migrated to `insertAdminGrant`) and ShopService.sellItem (now uses `insertSell`). **ShopService MUTATION SQL stays inline** for the 4 remaining shop_items writes (INSERT new row, UPDATE existing fields, DELETE by id, UPDATE stock_limit after purchase) — those are PR 7.4 territory; separating read from write keeps this PR mechanical and reviewable. **InventoryService callsites cleaned to zero**: the last direct `runAsync` from PR 7.2 (the `item_transactions` admin-grant INSERT) is now `this.itemTransactionRepository.insertAdminGrant(...)`. **Service constructor signatures**: `ShopService` constructor now takes an optional fifth `deps = {}` parameter; existing 4-arg callers unchanged. `InventoryService` constructor was already extended in PR 7.2 with `deps = {}`; the new `itemTransactionRepository` slot is added there. **Tests**: 17 `it()` blocks total across the two new test files (8 for ItemTransactionRepository + 9 for ShopRepository, the latter higher because `findShopItemIdByItemId` gets two cases — hit + miss). 17 × 2 backend flags = 34 distinct invocations. Mirrors the established BuffRepository / UserInventoryRepository test shape: jest-mocked DB primitives, SQL text normalized via `s.replace(/\s+/g, ' ').trim()` and asserted verbatim, params asserted in placeholder order. Constructor wiring tested both ways (default-fallback + injected) for each repo. **Honesty**: the roadmap mentioned "8 SELECT-shaped queries" for ShopRepository and "5 item_transactions callsites" for ItemTransactionRepository; the actual counts came in at 6 + 6 — the roadmap counts were approximate. Full suite: 809/810 under `--runInBand` (same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` "rejects on SQL syntax error" flake from the Phase 6 handoff). **Risk**: LOW — purely read-and-audit-write extractions; no atomicity changes (those are PR 7.4). The byte-equivalent claim is preserved at the SQL-text level for every extracted method via the test assertions.

- **`UserInventoryRepository` extraction from `InventoryService` (PR 7.2, Phase 7).** Second PR of Phase 7. Moves 11 inline `user_inventory` SQL calls out of `server/services/InventoryService.js` into a new `server/database/repository/UserInventoryRepository.js`. Follows the now-six-PR-old repository pattern (UserRepository → ChatBotRepository → ItemRepository → ViewBotRepository → BuffRepository → ContinuousRecordingRepository → UserInventoryRepository): constructor takes optional `{ getAsync, runAsync, allAsync }` dep overrides and falls back to the module-level wrappers from `server/database/database.js`. Pure SQL — no business logic, no projection, no domain serialization (stack-limit clamping, cooldown application, the result objects InventoryService returns to callers all stay in the service). **9 repo methods** cover the 11 callsites (one update-quantity shape is reused for both stack-increase and stack-decrease paths): `findInventoryWithItemsForUser`, `findInventoryItem`, `aggregateValueForUser`, `aggregateByRarity`, `findRecentlyUsed`, `insertItem`, `updateQuantity`, `markUsed`, `deleteItem`, `deleteAllForUser`. **JOINs to `items` live in this repo** (not split across UserInventoryRepository + ItemRepository), matching the BuffRepository (PR 6.2) precedent: the SELECT shape is inventory-centric, the JOIN is anchored on `user_inventory`, and breaking the composite query into two repo calls plus a JS-side join would be a pessimization of a clean SQL query for an abstraction that doesn't pay rent. **Deliberately NOT extracted in this PR**: the one `INSERT INTO item_transactions` callsite in `InventoryService.grantItemsToUser` (line 244 of the post-PR file) — that table belongs to PR 7.3's `ItemTransactionRepository`. Also NOT extracted: any of the JS-side guards (`if (inventoryItem.quantity < quantity) throw …`, the `max_stack` clamping math) — those are domain logic, not data access. **Service constructor signature change**: `InventoryService` constructor now accepts an optional third `deps = {}` parameter, defaulting `userInventoryRepository` to a default-constructed instance (`new UserInventoryRepository()`). Existing callers that pass only `(itemService, buffDebuffService)` are unchanged. **Tests**: 14 `it()` blocks × 2 backend flags = 28 distinct invocations in `server/tests/database/repository/UserInventoryRepository.test.js`, mirroring the BuffRepository test shape (jest-mocked DB primitives; SQL text normalized via `s.replace(/\s+/g, ' ').trim()` and asserted verbatim; params asserted in placeholder order, not human-arg order). Constructor wiring tested both ways (default-fallback + injected). Full suite: 765/766 under `--runInBand` (same pre-existing `database-better.test.js` "rejects on SQL syntax error" flake; reproducible on main without these changes). **Risk**: LOW — inventory mutations are non-financial; the read-side JOIN shapes are byte-equivalent (preserved through SQL-normalization-then-verbatim assertion in the tests). **Phase 7 sequencing**: PR 7.3 will extract `item_transactions` (the one INSERT still inline here) plus the read-only ShopService SQL. PR 7.4 then re-does ShopService.purchaseItem atomically via the PR 7.1 `withTransaction` helper, with UserInventoryRepository + ItemTransactionRepository methods composing under a single tx scope.
- **`withTransaction` helper (PR 7.1, Phase 7 — [ADR-0015](docs/architecture/adr/0015-transaction-shape-for-multi-statement.md)).** First foundational PR of the Phase 7 money-flow refactor. Adds `withTransaction(fn, { busyTimeoutMs })` to `server/database/database.js`. Wraps a body fn in `BEGIN IMMEDIATE … COMMIT` (or `ROLLBACK` on throw), serialized at the JS layer via a process-wide Promise-chain mutex so two concurrent scopes cannot interleave statements on the shared connection. Body fn receives a `tx = { runAsync, getAsync, allAsync }` proxy that routes through the same wrappers — repo methods accept `tx` as a dep override and work unchanged whether invoked inside or outside a transaction. Works under **both backends** (`USE_BETTER_SQLITE3=true` and `=false`) using `BEGIN`/`COMMIT` as SQL statements via the existing `runAsync` wrapper — deliberately NOT better-sqlite3's `db.transaction(fn)` because that requires a sync body and the extracted repos return promises. The optional `busyTimeoutMs` parameter applies a per-scope `PRAGMA busy_timeout` (restored to the 5000 ms default on exit, success OR failure) for callers that want to fail fast under writer-lock contention; defaults to whatever the connection currently has set (the 5000 ms default established by `applyPragmas.js` / `database-better.js`). **Red-team finding closed**: under sqlite3, `await runAsync('BEGIN IMMEDIATE')` does NOT by itself serialize subsequent `await runAsync(...)` against the same handle — between the BEGIN's resolution and the next statement's submission, any unrelated caller can submit a statement that runs on the same connection inside our open tx. The mutex closes the in-process hole; the IMMEDIATE lock closes the cross-handle hole. The remaining hazard (a fire-and-forget `runAsync` from a timer/socket handler during an open scope) is documented as a sharp edge in the helper's doc-comment and the ADR — discipline-enforced rather than code-enforced, because funneling every write in the codebase through `withTransaction` would be massively over-scoped for this PR. Implemented as a factory (`createWithTransaction({ runAsync, getAsync, allAsync })`) so tests can instantiate isolated instances against in-memory DBs; production `database.js` instantiates once at module-load time with the post-`USE_BETTER_SQLITE3`-swap wrappers and exports a singleton. **Tests**: 10 contract `it()` blocks in `server/tests/database/transaction.test.js` cover happy-path commit, body-throw rollback, statement-error rollback (UNIQUE constraint violation), post-rollback recovery, two-concurrent-scopes serialization order (asserts the labels arrive A,A,B,B not A,B,A,B), error-scope-doesn't-block-next-scope (mutex releases on throw), busy_timeout PRAGMA application + restore on success + restore on failure. Each runs under both backends via `describe.each([{flag:'true'},{flag:'false'}])`, so 20 distinct test invocations total. **Side cleanup — ADR-0013 number collision resolved**: `0013-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md` (PR 5.1's atomic-points ADR) and `0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md` (the AI moderation ADR) both shipped on main with the same number from parallel branches. Renamed the atomic-SQL ADR to `0013a-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md` to break the collision without touching content; ADR-0014's cross-references and CHANGELOG references updated. The AI moderation ADR keeps the bare `0013` slug (it's the more-referenced of the two and renaming it would touch more files; the `a` suffix communicates the "split out of an existing slot" provenance cleanly). The ADR register in `docs/architecture/adr/README.md` adds both 0013a and the new 0015. **Blocking constraint for downstream PRs**: PR 7.4 (atomic `purchaseItem`) consumes this helper; PR 10.2 (`ClipRepository` atomic CREATE) also consumes it. 20/20 new tests pass; full suite at 737/738 under `--runInBand` (the single failure is the pre-existing `database-better.test.js` "rejects on SQL syntax error" flake called out in the Phase 6 handoff, reproducible on main without these changes).

### Fixed
- **AI moderation pipeline — URL-relay `stream_type` mislabel + Stage 2 Groq key load from DB (production follow-up).** Two production-observed issues from the post-deploy verification of the LiveKit chunk-shape hotfix. (1) **`stream_type` mislabel for URL-relay sessions.** `ViewBotURLService` calls `streamService.setStreamer(urlId)` WITHOUT a second `streamType` argument, so `StreamService.setStreamer` defaults the missing arg to `'webcam'` — which means `getStreamType()` reports `'webcam'` for what's really a URL-relay session. Every `moderation_events` row produced by a URL-relay session was getting `stream_type='webcam'`. Under `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE=true` this would route the ActionArbiter to `_actWebcam` (attempting to ban a `user_id` that doesn't exist for URL relays) instead of `_actUrlRelay` (which adds a `WhitelistService` block entry — the correct action). The fix is local to `ModerationService._resolveStreamType(streamerId)`: detect the `url-stream-` id prefix (canonical naming, established at `ViewBotURLService.js:447` where the id is minted as `url-stream-${Date.now()}-${++this.streamCounter}` and also matched at `:1564` via `participantIdentity?.startsWith('url-stream-')`) and return `'url-relay'` regardless of what `streamService` says. Pinned-prefix detection is intentionally narrower than the broader fix of teaching `ViewBotURLService` to pass `'url-relay'` to `setStreamer` — that broader change touches multiple call sites and could surprise other consumers of `getStreamType()`, so it's tracked as a follow-up. (2) **Stage 2 Groq key never loaded from `groq_config` DB row.** Production has `GROQ_API_KEY` stored ONLY in the `groq_config` table (admin-set via the existing Groq admin UI), with the env unset. `ChatBotLLMService.loadGroqConfig()` reads from this table at boot, so MovieBot worked — but `ModerationStage2` only consulted `process.env.MODERATION_GROQ_API_KEY` and `process.env.GROQ_API_KEY`, both empty, so its `isReady()` returned false and every Stage 1 hit produced an `admin_review` row with empty `stage2_verdict_json`. The LLM classifier was dark. The fix in `server/index.js` resolves the key in priority order (`MODERATION_GROQ_API_KEY` env → `GROQ_API_KEY` env → `groq_config.api_key` DB row where `enabled=1`) before instantiating `ModerationStage2`. Boot logs a clear `✅ ModerationStage2: Groq key loaded from groq_config table (env unset)` when the DB path fires, and a `⚠️ no Groq key in env OR groq_config` when neither source has it. **Tests**: 2 new regression tests in `server/tests/services/ModerationService.test.js` — one pins that an `url-stream-...` streamerId resolves to `stream_type='url-relay'` even when `streamService.getStreamType()` returns `'webcam'` (the production failure mode), one pins that a non-prefixed streamerId still falls through to `streamService.getStreamType()` (preserves the existing path for viewbot / webcam / etc.). The Stage 2 DB-key load is orchestration code in `server/index.js` and validated by production verification rather than a unit test (the change is a straight inline DB read into the env-fallback chain). 718/718 server tests pass (+2 new).
- **AI moderation pipeline — LiveKit `transcription-chunk` payload shape (production hotfix to [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md) chain).** Discovered while verifying the freshly-deployed AI moderation service against the live URL-relay: every chunk was being silently dropped by `ModerationService.handleTranscriptChunk` because of a payload-shape divergence in `TranscriptionService`. The MediaSoup branch of `startTimedTranscription` emits `transcription-chunk` with `{ ..., text }` (`server/services/TranscriptionService.js` around line 1061) but the LiveKit branch — which is the path URL-relay streams actually take — emits `{ ..., transcription }` (around line 997). `handleTranscriptChunk` strictly read `chunk.text`, so the production URL-relay path was unmoderated end-to-end despite the service initializing successfully (the API endpoints, seed data, and event-emitter subscription all reported healthy). Verified empirically against the live module: the same call with `{text}` writes a `moderation_events` row + fires the notifier; the same call with `{transcription}` (and the same offending phrase) returned null with no row. The fix is a defensive read in `handleTranscriptChunk` — `chunk.text || chunk.transcription` — that normalizes both shapes down to a single `text` field before passing the chunk through `_processChunk`, so the rest of the pipeline (sliding-overlap matching, Stage 2 call payload, the `transcript_excerpt` we persist) doesn't need a per-callsite ternary. Tie-breaker: when both fields are present, `text` wins (the MediaSoup-emit shape is canonical; LiveKit is the legacy outlier). The proper structural fix — normalizing the emit shape inside `TranscriptionService` so consumers don't have to read both fields — expands the blast radius (every `transcription-chunk` consumer in the codebase has to be re-audited) and is intentionally left as a tracked follow-up; the defensive read carries the production responsibility in the meantime. **Tests**: 3 new regression tests in `server/tests/services/ModerationService.test.js` pinning the contract: LiveKit-shape `{transcription}` produces the same `admin_review` row and notifier emit as MediaSoup-shape `{text}`; empty `{transcription: ""}` is rejected like empty `{text: ""}`; when both fields are present, `text` is preferred. End-to-end verified via a one-off diagnostic against the actual `ModerationService` module: `{transcription: "this is a faggot test"}` now writes id=1 with `decision=admin_review` and fires `notifier.eventCreated`. 602/602 server tests pass (+3 new).

### Added
- **AI moderation pipeline — retention purge + GDPR Article 15 export (PR-M6 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** Seventh of eight planned PRs landing the AI moderation pipeline. Closes the two compliance essentials the plan calls out as non-negotiable for production: data retention enforcement (so we're not silently growing a 1-million-row hate-speech audit log) and a GDPR Article 15 right-of-access export endpoint. Defers (with explicit notes in the deferred list at the bottom of this entry) the lower-priority M6 items: two-admin approval, hash-chained audit, Prometheus metrics, automatic `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE=true` flip. **Retention scheduler**: new `ModerationService.startRetentionScheduler({ flaggedRetentionDays = 90, cleanRetentionDays = 30, intervalMs })` schedules a 24-hour `setInterval` that calls `purgeOldEvents()` — deletes `moderation_events` rows older than 90 days where `final_decision <> 'clean'` and rows older than 30 days where `final_decision = 'clean'` (the latter is a placeholder window — PR-M1 doesn't write `clean` rows, only Stage 1 hits — but the constraint is wired so a future PR that starts logging clean classifications gets the right retention without code changes). First tick is delayed 60s after boot so retention doesn't compete with other boot-time IO. Both the first-run timeout and the recurring interval are `.unref()`'d so SIGTERM exits cleanly. `moderationService.stop()` now also clears both timers. Retention windows are env-overridable via `AI_MODERATION_RETENTION_FLAGGED_DAYS` / `AI_MODERATION_RETENTION_CLEAN_DAYS` for the rare case (data-deletion request, legal hold, etc.) where ops needs a non-default window. **GDPR export endpoint**: new `GET /api/moderation-ai/me/export` (note: `authenticateToken`, not `authenticateAdmin` — every authenticated user can pull their own data per GDPR Article 15). Returns `{user_id, generated_at, notice, legal_basis: 'GDPR Article 6(1)(f) — legitimate safety interest', event_count, events: [...]}`. Match logic walks `sessionService.socketToUserId` for socket ids currently mapped to the caller's user id, then pulls all `moderation_events` rows with `streamer_id` in that set. **This is best-effort and explicitly documented as such in the response `notice` field**: the SessionService map reflects CURRENT live sockets only — a user whose moderation event was captured against a now-disconnected socket id will see those events ONLY if they're reconnected on a socket that still maps to the same user id. Persistent socketId → userId history (which would give us full historical recall) is deferred to a future PR; M6's "best-effort + notice" stance is the GDPR-defensible minimum for v1. **Right-to-erasure (GDPR Article 17)** is NOT implemented as a self-service endpoint: some moderation_events retention is "necessary for legitimate safety interest" per GDPR Article 6(1)(f) and cannot be erased on demand, so erasure runs through a separate request-and-review flow (admin-mediated; deferred to follow-up). The response notice spells this out so end users have a clear expectation. **Wiring**: `server/index.js` calls `moderationService.startRetentionScheduler()` right after the existing `moderationService.initialize()` resolves, before chatBotService gets the moderation gate. The route file imports `authenticateToken` alongside the existing `authenticateAdmin`. **Tests**: 4 new ModerationService tests covering flagged-row retention (100-day-old row deleted, fresh row kept), clean-row retention (40 days deleted, 10 days kept), different-window cross-check (50d flagged stays, 50d clean dies), and scheduler idempotency + stop() clears the timer. 3 new route tests covering /me/export returning events for the caller's session-mapped socket ids, returning empty when the caller has no socket history, and returning 400 when the token has no user id. 541/541 server tests pass (+7 new). **Deferred from M6 to a future PR (M6.5 / M7 / M8)**: (1) two-admin approval for moderation_terms mutations and ban reversals — single-admin is acceptable per the M0 "out of scope" note; (2) hash-chained `moderation_terms_audit.prev_hash` / `row_hash` for tamper evidence — rows are written today and useful, the chain itself can be backfilled; (3) Prometheus-shaped metrics — `console.log` lines suffice until ops actually has an observability target; (4) automatic flip of `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE=true` — that's an operator decision in the env file, not a code change; (5) Article 17 self-service erasure flow; (6) persistent socketId → userId history for full GDPR recall. **PR-M7 (URL-relay numeric-ID hardening)** also remains deferred. The current ActionArbiter already passes `event.external_user_id` to the WhitelistService when one exists on the event row, but neither the schema (`url_relay_filter_entries`) nor the matcher consults that column yet. The next-PR work is a small migration adding `external_user_id` to the schema with an idempotent ALTER, plus extending `WhitelistService._refreshCache` to build a `blockStreamerIds: Set` and `WhitelistService.checkAllowed` to OR-match against it — bounded ~150 lines + tests, naturally a small follow-up.
- **AI moderation pipeline — admin events viewer + API surface (PR-M5 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** Sixth of eight PRs landing the AI moderation pipeline. Ships the operator-facing surface: a paginated events log with decision-filter dropdown, expandable detail panel (Stage 1 matches + Stage 2 verdict + Stage 3 verdict + action_taken + reversal metadata + model versions), one-click ban reversal that flips both `moderation_events.reversed_at` and `users.streaming_banned = 0` for the affected user. **API routes** (10 endpoints under `/api/moderation-ai`, all behind `authenticateAdmin`, mounted unconditionally so the handlers themselves return 503 when `moderationService` is unset — matches the PR-W5 whitelist pattern). Events: `GET /events` (limit/offset/decision filters, default 50, max 500), `GET /events/:id`, `POST /events/:id/reverse` (writes the audit fields AND unbans the user via the action arbiter's userRepository when the event was `auto_ban`). Terms CRUD: `GET /terms` (filters enabled/category/source), `POST /terms` (admin-source only — embedded rows are seeded at boot and can't be created via the API), `POST /terms/:id/enabled` (soft-disable; embedded terms are re-enabled on next boot per the seed-wins policy), `DELETE /terms/:id` (returns 409 `cannot_remove_embedded` for embedded rows), `GET /terms/audit`. Config: `GET /config` and `POST /config` (per-category `action_mode` ∈ {auto_ban, admin_review, mute_pending}, `stage2_threshold`, `stage3_required`, `enabled`). **New service methods** on `ModerationService`: `reverseEvent`, `getTerms`, `addTerm`, `setTermEnabled`, `removeTerm`, `_auditTerm` (writes to `moderation_terms_audit` — hash-chain wiring deferred to M6, the rows themselves are useful for the events tab today), `getTermsAudit`, `getCategoryConfig`, `setCategoryConfig`. The `addTerm` path normalizes the input via `Stage1.normalize()` and refuses terms that normalize to an empty string. The audit log entries currently ship without `prev_hash`/`row_hash` populated (M6 will backfill once a hash function is chosen). **React admin tab**: `AIModerationManagement.tsx` rendered inside `AdminPanelV3.tsx` as a new "AI Moderation" entry in the Moderation category (icon 🤖, between Chat Moderation and IP Ban Management). Paginates 25 rows per page with prev/next controls, decision-filter dropdown, expandable per-row detail panel, and a "Reverse ban" button gated to `final_decision='auto_ban' && !reversed_at` rows. The button prompts for a reason (stored in `reversed_at`/`reversed_by`/`reversal_reason`) and refreshes the list. Reversed rows render at 0.55 opacity with a "reversed" badge. Per-row badges use the existing AdminPanelV3 dark palette. **New client service**: `aiModerationApi.ts` — thin typed wrapper over the 10 endpoints, accepts the `makeApiCall` helper AdminPanelV3 injects (preserves auth-header threading + log-line behaviour from other admin components). **Deferred to a follow-up** to keep this PR focused on validating the API end-to-end: full terms-management CRUD UI (admins can POST via curl for now), per-category config UI, live socket subscription to `moderation-event-created` for real-time refresh (current UI uses a polling-refresh button), and the streamer-side `AIModerationBanner.tsx` that renders on receiving the `moderation-streamer-banner` socket event (needs a host component on every page, separate from the admin panel). **Tests**: 17 new server tests in `server/tests/routes/moderation-ai.test.js` covering: 503 when service unset; events list/detail/filter; reverse 200 / 404 / 409-already-reversed paths + the userRepository unban side-effect; terms list/add/enable/remove + the cannot_remove_embedded path; terms audit; config get/set + validation 400. RTL UI tests deferred per existing admin-side test infrastructure precedent (services-not-components focus — `WhitelistManagement.test.tsx` was likewise deferred in PR-W5). TypeScript compiles cleanly against the new components. 534/534 server tests pass (+17 new).
- **AI moderation pipeline — Whisper hardening + MovieBot output gate (PR-M4 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** Fifth of eight PRs landing the AI moderation pipeline. Closes the two known mid-pipeline holes that PR-M0/M1/M2/M3 left open: (1) Whisper's default behaviour of redacting profanity to `***` (which defeats the Stage 1 word-filter) and (2) the MovieBot output path, where the bot's LLM reply could itself contain offensive content (especially under prompt injection from the transcript). **Whisper hardening**: `TranscriptionService.transcribeWithWhisperCpp` now passes `--temperature 0.0` (deterministic output — re-running produces the same transcript, important for moderation evidence) and `--prompt "Transcribe verbatim, including any profanity."` (steers Whisper away from the asterisk-redaction behaviour documented in the OpenAI Whisper community discussions). The prompt is short and stylistically neutral so it can't fight the user's language or accent. **Full JSON confidence parsing** (`-oj --word-thold 0.6 --no-speech-thold 0.6` + `whisper_avg_logprob` / `whisper_no_speech_prob` columns wired into `transcription-chunk` event payload) and the **two-confirming-chunks rule** for the slur category are deferred — both require either reading whisper.cpp's `<audiofile>.json` sidecar (a second IO operation) or stitching word-level probability data through the transcription emit shape, and are tracked as M4.5 follow-ups. The chunk-level confidence drop is the cleanest defense against the documented Whisper "violent-content hallucination" failure mode; the deferred work is the load-bearing v1.5 hardening. **MovieBot output gate**: new `ModerationService.checkBotOutput(text, ctx)` runs Stage 1 + Stage 2 (no Stage 3, no ActionArbiter — drop is the only action) on every generated bot reply before chat-service relay. Decision rule is slightly stricter than the streamer-audio pipeline: drop on (a) any hard-tier word match OR (b) Stage 1 match + Stage 2 risk_level >= 2. Threshold is lower than the streamer pipeline (which auto-bans only on 2-of-2 + risk_level=3) because bot output is a controlled surface — we'd rather drop a borderline reply than emit it under the platform's identity. Dropped events write `stream_type='moviebot-output'`, `final_decision='mb_output_dropped'`, and one of `action_taken='dropped_hard_tier_word'` / `'dropped_stage2_risk'`; `ModerationNotifier.botOutputDropped()` fans the row to admin sockets. `ChatBotService.generateMovieComment` now takes a `setModerationService()` setter (late-injected from `server/index.js` right after `moderationService.initialize()` resolves) and gates the existing `socket.emit('send-message', ...)` path — flagged replies return `{success: false, error: 'moderation_dropped:<reason>', moderation_event_id}` which MovieBotService's existing `if (response.success && response.message)` guard already treats as a no-op, so no MovieBot-side change is required to suppress the chat emission. **Fail-open on bug**: if the moderation gate throws (rather than returning `{allowed: false}`), ChatBotService swallows the error and lets the message through — a bug in the gate should not silence the bot. The streamer-audio pipeline (Stage 1+2+3 on Whisper transcripts) is the next-tier defense for that case. **Tests**: 6 new tests in `ModerationService.test.js` covering clean-text pass-through, hard-tier-word drop, soft-tier-without-Stage-2-risk pass-through (the reclaimed AAVE / "nigga" case is the load-bearing one — Stage 2 returning risk_level=1 means we DON'T drop), soft-tier + Stage 2 risk=2 drop, empty/null input pass-through, and post-stop short-circuit. 517/517 server tests pass (+6 new).
- **AI moderation pipeline — Stage 3 OpenAI cross-check + ActionArbiter, enforcement behind feature flag (PR-M3 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** Fourth of eight PRs landing the AI moderation pipeline. This is the first PR with a runtime action surface — but it's gated behind `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE=true` (default false), so a host that ships through M3 sees the full pipeline running in log-only mode with `final_decision='admin_review'` rows until ops flips the flag in M6. New `ModerationStage3.js` is a self-contained client for OpenAI's free `omni-moderation-latest` endpoint — fires ONLY when Stage 2 returns `risk_level=3`, returns the standard `{flagged, categories, scores, model, latency_ms}` shape, has the same circuit-breaker contract as Stage 2 (5 consecutive failures opens a 60s window, single success resets). Unlike Stage 2 it does NOT wrap input in anti-injection delimiters because omni-moderation is a classifier endpoint (not chat-completions) — prompt injection is structurally impossible against a model that doesn't follow instructions. `OPENAI_API_KEY` is optional: when absent, high-risk events route to `admin_review` rather than auto-action, which is the safe default. New `ModerationActionArbiter.js` is a stateless service that takes a fully-classified event and turns it into the appropriate action. **Decision tree**: stale-session check first (if `event.stream_session_id !== streamService.getStreamGeneration()` the offending streamer has already rotated for an unrelated reason — downgrade to `admin_review` so we don't ban whoever is currently on-air); `enforce=false` gate (M3 default — downgrade to `admin_review` even on 2-of-2 HIGH agreement); then branch on `stream_type`: `'webcam'` → `userRepository.banFromStreaming(userId, 'ai-moderation')` if the streamer is authenticated, emit streamer-banner via the notifier (with `/admin/moderation/events/:id` appeal URL), call `randomStreamRotationService._rotateToNewStream()`, final_decision = `auto_ban`; `'url-relay'` → `whitelistService.addEntry({platform, entry_type:'streamer', value: login, list:'block'}, 'ai-moderator')` (login-keyed for M3; PR-M7 schema-bumps to numeric `external_user_id` for spoof resistance), rotation, final_decision = `auto_skip`; `'viewbot'` / `'moviebot-output'` / unknown → log only, no action. The arbiter never throws — every step is wrapped so a failing ban write or rotation produces a structured `action_taken` string rather than corrupting the event row. UNIQUE-constraint hits on the URL-relay blocklist (the streamer is already blocked) are treated as no-op success. **`ModerationService` 2-of-2 agreement gate**: when `stage2.risk_level=3` and Stage 3 is ready and the per-streamer quota allows (default 20 calls/hour, rolling-window enforced), Stage 3 is called with `surroundingContext + currentText`. If Stage 3 flags, the arbiter runs; if Stage 3 doesn't flag the event downgrades to `admin_review` with `action_taken='stage3_disagreed'`; if Stage 3 returns degraded the event becomes `deferred_degraded`. Per-streamer Stage 3 quota uses a per-streamer rolling timestamp list trimmed to the last hour on every check — defeats the "Stage-3 burn" cost attack from the red-team review. Two new `setActionArbiter()` / `setStage3()` setters on ModerationService support the late-injection pattern that `server/index.js` needs: ModerationService is constructed eagerly in the bootstrap section before `RandomStreamRotationService` exists, then both the MediaSoup and the LiveKit branches construct an ActionArbiter (with `enforce: process.env.AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE === 'true'`) once their rotation service is wired and call `moderationService.setActionArbiter()`. The arbiter is also exposed on `app.locals.moderationActionArbiter` for the future admin reversal route (PR-M5). **Tests**: 33 new tests across two new test files plus 7 added to `ModerationService.test.js`. `ModerationStage3.test.js` covers contract + happy path + error paths (non-2xx, malformed envelope, missing results) + circuit-breaker lifecycle, plus an explicit assertion that the body is sent as raw `input` without the anti-injection wrapper (classifier endpoint, structurally injection-immune). `ModerationActionArbiter.test.js` covers all four branches (stale-session, enforce-off, webcam authenticated/anonymous/rotation-fail/ban-fail, url-relay add/UNIQUE-already-blocked/cannot_block, viewbot/unknown). `ModerationService.test.js` adds the integration tests for Stage 3 not-called-when-low-risk, Stage 3 called on risk=3 → agreement → arbiter, disagreement → admin_review, degraded → deferred_degraded, not-ready → admin_review, per-streamer quota gating, and setActionArbiter replacement. 511/511 server tests pass (+33 new).
- **AI moderation pipeline — Stage 2 Groq classifier with anti-injection wrapper + circuit breaker, log-only (PR-M2 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** Third of eight PRs landing the AI moderation pipeline. New `ModerationStage2` service is a self-contained Groq client (does NOT depend on ChatBotLLMService so a noisy MovieBot neighbour can't starve moderation calls — separate `MODERATION_GROQ_API_KEY` env override is available for ops who want quota isolation). The system prompt pins three category definitions (hate_speech / threat / sexual), explicit use-vs-mention rules, AAVE / reclamation / song-lyric / educational-use guidance, and the **anti-prompt-injection contract**: every chunk of untrusted user content is wrapped in `<transcript untrusted="true">…</transcript>` and the system prompt explicitly tells the model that content inside is data, never instructions. JSON schema is enforced via `response_format: { type: 'json_object' }`; the sanitizer drops unknown categories, clamps `risk_level` to 0..3, and slices `explanation` to 2000 chars. Per-call `AbortController` timeout (8s default). **Circuit breaker**: 5 consecutive failures (5xx, 429, network error, JSON parse failure, verdict-shape failure) open the breaker for 60s during which `classify()` returns `{degraded: true, reason: 'breaker_open'}` without making the API call. A single success resets the failure counter. `ModerationService` now consumes the Stage 2 instance via constructor injection, only calls `classify()` when Stage 1 returned matches (demand-gated, so we don't pay Groq for clean chunks), passes a 60-second per-streamer rolling context buffer alongside the Stage 1-tripping chunk, and persists the full Stage 2 verdict (`stage2_verdict_json`, `stage2_risk_level`, `stage2_categories_json`) into `moderation_events`. A Stage 2 verdict of `degraded` or `error` produces `final_decision = 'deferred_degraded'` — the system never auto-acts during a Groq outage; admin review picks up the slack (M3 wires the action arbiter, this PR stays log-only so even `risk_level=3` stays `admin_review`). **Sliding-overlap Stage 1 matching**: the matcher now runs over `previousChunkText + currentChunkText` so a multi-word threat phrase split across the 5s chunk boundary still lands intact in at least one window — defeats the cross-window-fragmentation attack from the red-team review. Per-streamer rolling buffers (`_contextBuffers`, `_previousChunkText`) are time-trimmed against `contextWindowMs` (default 60s) on every push so memory doesn't grow unbounded for long sessions; `stop()` clears them alongside the mutex chain. `server/index.js` instantiates `ModerationStage2` immediately before `ModerationService` and injects it via the constructor's `stage2` dep, falling back to `process.env.GROQ_API_KEY` when `MODERATION_GROQ_API_KEY` isn't set. **Tests**: 27 new tests across two files. `ModerationStage2.test.js` (~21 tests) covers prompt construction (system-prompt anti-injection contract present, user-prompt wrapping, surrounding-context ordering), happy-path verdict parsing with the exact `response_format` request shape, degraded paths (no API key, empty transcript, non-2xx status, malformed envelope, malformed verdict JSON, verdict missing required fields, unknown categories dropped by sanitizer), circuit-breaker lifecycle (opens at threshold, refuses calls without invoking fetch during the open window, closes after `cbOpenMs`, single success resets counter), and a **prompt-injection corpus** of 5 payloads (D1 classifier-override monologue, D2 tool-hijack, D3 fabricated medical exemption, closing-tag injection, role-juggling) asserting that every payload lands fully enclosed inside the untrusted delimiters when the user message is built. `ModerationService.test.js` adds Stage 2 integration tests: classify only called on Stage 1 hit, surrounding context plumbed through, verdict persisted to the row, degraded → `deferred_degraded`, error → `deferred_degraded`, Stage 2 not ready → row still written with `admin_review` (no Stage 2 call), and the sliding-overlap split-phrase test ("i would never kill" + "all jews i swear" → caught on the second chunk). 478/478 server tests pass (+27 new).
- **AI moderation pipeline — ModerationService scaffold + Stage 1 word filter, log-only (PR-M1 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** Second of eight PRs landing the AI moderation pipeline. New `ModerationService` (stateful, EventEmitter, registered as `app.locals.moderationService` and `global.moderationService` per the conventions) subscribes to `TranscriptionService`'s `transcription-chunk` event and runs each chunk through Stage 1: normalize (NFKC + lowercase + homoglyph fold for Cyrillic/Greek look-alikes + leetspeak fold for `0→o`, `1→i`, `3→e`, `4→a`, `5→s`, `7→t`, `8→b`, `@→a`, `$→s`, `!→i` + non-alphanumeric strip + 3+-repeat collapse + whitespace collapse), then match against an in-memory cache of all `enabled=1` rows from `moderation_terms`. Stage 1 is **recall-only**: every hit lands in a `moderation_events` row with `final_decision='admin_review'`, never `auto_ban` — Stage 2 (PR-M2, Groq classifier) and Stage 3 (PR-M3, OpenAI omni cross-check) are the gates that produce action verdicts. On any hit, `ModerationNotifier.eventCreated()` fans the new row to the `'admin'` Socket.IO room so the admin events tab (PR-M5) refreshes live; clean chunks write no row to avoid blowing up `moderation_events` with negative data. New `ModerationStage1.js` is the pure normalize/match module (no DB, no IO); new `ModerationNotifier.js` is the emit chokepoint mirroring the BuffNotifier/ViewerCountNotifier/StreamNotifier pattern with four methods (`eventCreated`, `actionTaken`, `streamerBanner`, `botOutputDropped`) and a `MODERATION_EVENT_DECISIONS` Set that mirrors the schema CHECK constraint. **Per-streamer mutex** serializes processing for the same streamer via a `Map<streamerId, Promise>` chain — chunks from different streamers run concurrently, chunks from the same streamer run FIFO so PR-M2's Stage-2-latency coalescing has a stable insertion point.
