The mutex chain is cleaned up lazily when the streamer's chain settles to avoid unbounded map growth on transient streamers. **`ModerationService.initialize()` is async**: applies `ai-moderation-schema.sql` (idempotent — same `CREATE TABLE IF NOT EXISTS` pattern WhitelistService uses), verifies the embedded seed's SHA-256 against the sibling `.sha256` file (**fails closed** by default — refuses to start on mismatch, matching the WhitelistService pattern; toggleable via `AI_MODERATION_FAIL_CLOSED=false` for dev), upserts the embedded seed into `moderation_terms` with `source='embedded'` (re-enables embedded rows that an admin disabled — the boot-wins policy means a permanently-off embedded term needs the seed file edited and the SHA-256 refreshed, not a runtime override that vanishes on restart), and loads the enabled-terms cache. **Wired into the bootstrap**: `ModerationNotifier` joins the other three notifiers in `server/bootstrap/services.js`'s factory (constructed with `io`, added to the services bag — expected-key count bumped 39 → 40 and pinned in the bootstrap test); `ModerationService` itself is instantiated inline in `server/index.js` immediately after the `WhitelistService` init block because its `initialize()` is async, with the same try/catch + env-gated require-or-degrade pattern (`AI_MODERATION_REQUIRE_SERVICE=true` re-throws the init error; default is to log and continue without enforcement, the safe default for M1). **No runtime enforcement** — no bans, no rotations, no blocklist writes, no MovieBot output gating. Those land in M3, M3, M3, and M4 respectively. The `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE` flag M3 will introduce defaults to `false` so even on a host that's fully wired through M7, enforcement is opt-in until M6 flips the default. **Tests**: 59 new tests across three new files. `ModerationStage1.test.js` covers normalization invariants (NFKC fullwidth fold, Cyrillic/Greek homoglyph fold, leet substitutions, punctuation strip, 3+-repeat collapse with doubles preserved, whitespace collapse, combined attacks) plus matching semantics (word-boundary for single-word terms, substring for multi-word phrases, regex-special-char safety in needles, span reporting, multi-match ordering, integration tests proving leetspeak/fullwidth/homoglyph/punctuation-padded slurs survive normalization to match the embedded seed terms; one regression-pinned known limitation where the 3+-repeat collapse can break a real doubled char in a slur — the test documents it as accepted because Stage 2 LLM catches intent regardless). `ModerationNotifier.test.js` covers constructor validation, room targeting (admin vs streamer-socket), payload shape pinning, and the schema-mirroring decisions Set. `ModerationService.test.js` opens an in-memory sqlite per test (same wrapper shape as the production database module), exercises full initialize() including schema apply + seed verify + cache load + event subscription, asserts the boot-wins SHA-256 fail-closed path, asserts handleTranscriptChunk writes `moderation_events` rows on Stage 1 hits but not on clean chunks, asserts per-streamer mutex preserves FIFO order, asserts different streamers process concurrently, asserts end-to-end event subscription (emit on TranscriptionService → notifier eventCreated called), and asserts stop() unsubscribes + drains in-flight chains. **Adjacent fix** caught by ModerationService.getEvents test: SQLite `CURRENT_TIMESTAMP` has 1-second resolution, so `ORDER BY created_at DESC` alone is non-deterministic for same-second inserts; secondary `id DESC` tiebreak added inline. 451/451 server tests pass (+59).
- **AI moderation pipeline — foundation (PR-M0 of [ADR-0013](docs/architecture/adr/0013-ai-moderation-pipeline.md)).** First of eight PRs landing the three-stage moderation gate (word filter → Groq classifier → OpenAI omni-moderation cross-check) that subscribes to the existing `transcription-chunk` event and acts on confirmed hate-speech, threat, or sexual/CSAM-adjacent content. **This PR ships schema and seeds only — no runtime behaviour.** New `server/database/ai-moderation-schema.sql` defines four tables: `moderation_terms` (embedded + admin-editable word list with `source` discriminator and `severity` ∈ {hard, soft}), `moderation_terms_audit` (append-only with `prev_hash`/`row_hash` columns for tamper evidence to be wired in PR-M6), `moderation_events` (one row per decision with DSA-Article-17 statement-of-reasons fields: `automated_decision`, `legal_basis`, `redress_url`, `reversed_at`/`reversed_by`, plus Whisper confidence and ML model version fields used by later PRs), and `moderation_config` (per-category dial — `auto_ban`/`admin_review`/`mute_pending`, configurable Stage 2 threshold and Stage 3 requirement) seeded with all three categories defaulting to `auto_ban` + threshold=3 + Stage-3-required. New `server/data/seeds/moderation-core-list.json` ships ~30 hand-curated hard-tier and soft-tier entries spanning hate-speech, threat, and sexual/CSAM-adjacent categories; the seed is intentionally conservative and admins are expected to extend the DB-backed table (`source='admin'`) based on observed patterns. Sibling `server/data/seeds/moderation-core-list.sha256` carries the SHA-256 integrity hash — PR-M1's `ModerationService.initialize()` will verify the hash at boot and **fail closed** (refuse to start) on a mismatch, matching the `WhitelistService` startup pattern from PR-W6. New `server/migrations/add_ai_moderation_tables.js` applies the schema; idempotent so it can be re-run safely. ADR-0013 documents the full pipeline design, all 11 architectural decisions (engine, action policy, categories, word-list management, retention, MovieBot output handling, AAVE-bias mitigation, URL-relay numeric-ID keying, voiceprint deferral, etc.), and explicitly records the accepted residual risks (AAVE/dialect bias on permaban path, audio-injection framing without voiceprint, Whisper hallucination on long segments). No tests in this PR — the schema is data-only and the migration is mechanical; PR-M1 ships the first behavioural code and its unit tests. **No wire-up** in `server/index.js` yet: PR-M1 introduces `ModerationService` + `ModerationNotifier` in log-only mode subscribing to `transcription-chunk`; PR-M2 adds Stage 2 (Groq classifier); PR-M3 adds Stage 3 (OpenAI) + `ModerationActionArbiter` behind an `AI_MODERATION_ENFORCE=false` env flag; PR-M4 hardens Whisper (word-level confidence + VAD) and adds the MovieBot output gate; PR-M5 ships the admin UI tabs in AdminPanelV3; PR-M6 turns enforcement on plus retention/audit hardening; PR-M7 schema-bumps `url_relay_filter_entries` to add `external_user_id` for numeric-ID-keyed URL-relay blocklisting.

### Changed
- **`ContinuousRecordingService` recording-table SQL extracted into `ContinuousRecordingRepository` (PR 6.3, third Phase 6 PR — [phases-6-plus.md](docs/architecture/plans/phases-6-plus.md), closes Phase 6).** Continues the repository-pattern rollout. 10 of the 12 inline `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites in `server/services/ContinuousRecordingService.js` collapse to method calls on a new `ContinuousRecordingRepository`. Two tables covered: `recording_sessions` (7 methods: insert-if-missing + set-recording + update-end + get-start-time-only + get-by-id + list-with-filters + list-pending-upload) and `recording_stream_segments` (3 methods: insert + end-by-id + end-all-open-for-session). Service line count drops from 1512 → 1463 (net −49). **Scope note** (called out for honesty — the phases-6-plus.md roadmap brief stated "12 SQL calls" against the two recording tables, but the actual count is **10 against the two recording tables + 2 cross-table reads against `url_streams` and `streaming_logs`**). The two cross-table reads stay inline in the service because: (a) `url_streams` belongs to the URL-stream-routing domain (the existing `URLStreamDatabaseService` owns that table — but does not yet have its own repo), (b) `streaming_logs` is an unrelated audit log used only as a username-display fallback (a 1-row tail query), and (c) a single-domain repo named "ContinuousRecording" reaching across to those tables would defeat the architectural value of the move. Phase 10 follow-ups can revisit those domains. **Behaviour-preserving, not byte-equivalent**: indentation whitespace collapses; the dynamic-filtered SELECT in `getSessionRecords` moves the SQL-builder logic from the service to the repo's `listSessions({status, streamerIdentity, fromTime, toTime, limit, offset})` — the destructured option whitelist replaces the legacy `if (options.foo)` check pattern; SQL output is identical for equivalent inputs. **Falsy-fragment-skip semantics preserved**: `if (limit)` (the legacy check) skips a `limit=0` value, so `listSessions({limit: 0})` produces SQL with no LIMIT clause. Pinned in a unit test. **Reaches-across-key safety**: extra keys outside the destructured whitelist are silently ignored — pinned in a unit test that passes `{evilKey: 'DROP TABLE users'}` and asserts `sql` does not contain `evilKey` and `params` only has the whitelisted values. **`segment_count = segment_count + ?` relative arithmetic** in `updateSessionEnd` preserved — same atomic-counter discipline ADR-0013 codified. **`INSERT OR IGNORE`** in `insertSessionIfMissing` preserved (the legacy behavior: re-entering `createSessionRecord` for the same daily session is a no-op because the unique session_id lands on the IGNORE branch). **`ended_at IS NULL` guard** in `endStreamSegment` and `endAllOpenSegments` preserved — accidentally re-ending an already-closed segment is rejected at the SQL level rather than relying on an in-memory check. **Constructor wiring**: the existing `userRepository` field gains a sibling `recordingRepository` field, both built inline in the constructor with `new ContinuousRecordingRepository({ getAsync, runAsync, allAsync })`. The service does not accept either repo as an explicit dep — the wiring is hidden behind `new` calls because the service's constructor signature is positional (`config = {}`), not dep-injection-shaped. Following PR 10.x's repository rollout would be the natural time to thread these through as opt-in deps. `expectedKeys` in `bootstrap/services.test.js` stays at 40; no bootstrap change. **Tests**: 16 logical tests in [`server/tests/database/repository/ContinuousRecordingRepository.test.js`](server/tests/database/repository/ContinuousRecordingRepository.test.js) × 2 backend flags via `describe.each` = **32 test cases** counted by Jest. Every repo method covered; SQL shape (whitespace-normalized) + parameter ordering pinned per method. The `listSessions` method gets 4 dedicated tests (no-options baseline, all-options happy path, falsy-fragment-skip, reach-across-key safety) because it's the only method with dynamic SQL composition. Constructor fallback + dep-injection paths covered. **Suite count**: 716/716 passes under `--runInBand` (was 684/684 post-PR-6.2; +32). The pre-existing `database-better.test.js` parallel-worker flake documented in PR 6.1 still surfaces in full-parallel `npm test` runs — unchanged by this PR. **Phase 6 closes** with this PR. Three new repository modules landed (ViewBotRepository, BuffRepository, ContinuousRecordingRepository). 42 of 44 callsites identified in the Phase 6 scope migrated (20/20 ViewBot + 12/12 Buff + 10/12 ContinuousRecording — the 2 cross-table reads documented above). Six total repository modules now exist (User, Item, ChatBot, ViewBot, Buff, ContinuousRecording). The repository pattern is at this point well-grooved; PR 10.x will tackle the remaining major DB-touching services (admin-recordings, ClipService, AccountService residuals, ShopService — gated on Phase 7's `withTransaction` helper for the ones that need atomic CREATE).
- **`BuffDebuffService` inline SQL extracted into `BuffRepository` (PR 6.2, second Phase 6 PR — [phases-6-plus.md](docs/architecture/plans/phases-6-plus.md)).** Continues the repository-pattern rollout. The 12 inline `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites in `server/services/BuffDebuffService.js` collapse to method calls on a new `BuffRepository`. Single primary table (`active_buffs`); several methods JOIN to `items` for display columns (`name`, `display_name`, `emoji`, `effect_data`) — the SELECT is buff-centric so the JOIN lives in this repo rather than crossing over to `ItemRepository`. Service line count drops from 842 → 788 (net −54). New file at [`server/database/repository/BuffRepository.js`](server/database/repository/BuffRepository.js) with 12 methods grouped by intent: CRUD (`insertBuff`, `getById`, `getByIdWithItem`, `updateRemainingSeconds`, `markInactive`, `incrementStreamingTime`), listings (`listActiveWithItems`, `listActiveWithItemsOrdered`, `listActiveForUser`, `getActiveByUserAndItem`, `findExpired`), analytics (`getStatsLast7Days`). The previously-anonymous "all active buffs ORDER BY applied_at DESC" fallback SELECT used in `getActiveBuffsForCurrentStreamer` becomes the named `listActiveWithItemsOrdered` — same SQL shape, easier to find. **Behaviour-preserving, not byte-equivalent**: the repo collapses indentation whitespace; the `insertBuff` SQL pulls the prior inline `const insertQuery = ...` into the repo method body (the service still logs the params with `console.log(...)` immediately before the call, so the observable log line is unchanged). One specifically-flagged textual delta: the `listActiveWithItemsOrdered` SQL keeps the legacy `SELECT ab.*, ..., ab.user_id` shape — `ab.*` already projects `user_id`, but the inline original explicitly listed `ab.user_id` a second time. SQLite tolerates duplicate column projections (the consumer sees `user_id` once because JavaScript object keys deduplicate). Preserved here for byte-equivalent wire output. **Serialization stays in the service**: `JSON.parse(metadata)` and `JSON.parse(effect_data)` in `formatBuffForClient` run in `BuffDebuffService` after the repo call; the repo only returns raw strings. **`duration` bound twice**: `insertBuff` binds `duration` to BOTH `duration_seconds` (the total) AND `remaining_seconds` (the live counter, which starts equal to total and ticks down). Mirrors the legacy SQL exactly — verified in the unit test (`expect(params).toEqual([..., 600, 600, ...])`). **`incrementStreamingTime` uses relative arithmetic** (`UPDATE ... SET streaming_time_used = streaming_time_used + 1`) so it's a single statement; ticks for the same buff serialize through the service's update loop so a read-then-write race is not a concern. Same atomic-counter discipline ADR-0013 codified. **Constructor**: `BuffDebuffService.constructor` gains an optional `buffRepository` dep alongside the existing `itemRepository`. Defaults to `new BuffRepository({ getAsync, runAsync, allAsync })` using the destructured primitives from `database.js`. No bootstrap change; `expectedKeys` stays at 40, no `services.test.js` change. The trade-off is the same one the other repos carry — fail-fast guard can't detect a shimmed buff repo. **Tests**: 15 logical tests in [`server/tests/database/repository/BuffRepository.test.js`](server/tests/database/repository/BuffRepository.test.js) × 2 backend flags via `describe.each` = **30 test cases**. Every method covered: SQL shape (whitespace-normalized), parameter ordering (specifically calling out the `insertBuff` duration-bound-twice case, the `updateRemainingSeconds` parameter-ordering case where remainingSeconds is leading and id is trailing, and the `getActiveByUserAndItem` two-key WHERE), constructor fallback + dep-injection paths. **Suite count**: 684/684 passes under `--runInBand` (was 654/654 post-PR-6.1 and post-PR-124-deploy-fix; +30). Full-parallel `npm test` shows the same pre-existing ~20% flake on `database-better.test.js` documented in PR 6.1's entry — not caused by this PR. **No bootstrap change, no ADR** (extends the established pattern). **No service-side public-method-signature change** — all 18 public methods on `BuffDebuffService` keep their existing signatures.
- **`ViewBotDatabaseService` inline SQL extracted into `ViewBotRepository` (PR 6.1, first Phase 6 PR — [phases-6-plus.md](docs/architecture/plans/phases-6-plus.md)).** Continues the repository-pattern rollout that started with `UserRepository` (PR-Q), `ItemRepository`, and `ChatBotRepository` (PR 5.3). The 20 inline `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites in `server/services/ViewBotDatabaseService.js` collapse to method calls on a new `ViewBotRepository`. Five tables covered: `viewbots` (8 methods: existence-check + upsert + find-enabled + list-enabled + delete + set-enabled + increment-usage + update-name), `viewbot_system_state` (2: upsert + get of the id=1 singleton row), `viewbot_sessions` (2: insert + end), `viewbot_rotation_history` (1: insert), `viewbot_metrics` (1: insert). Plus 2 analytics-aggregate methods that take pre-built `timeCondition` / `botCondition` SQL fragments from the service (the service owns the fragment whitelist, the repo owns the SELECT template — same "whitelisting stays in the service" pattern PR 5.3 codified) and 3 retention-cleanup methods that interpolate `retentionDays` into `datetime('now', '-N days')` (the modifier argument is parsed at SQL-compile time, not bind time, so it cannot be a `?` placeholder — callers MUST pass a numeric value, which the service layer controls). **Behaviour-preserving, not byte-equivalent**: the repo collapses whitespace in some of the longer SQL strings vs. the inline originals' literal indentation, and the cleanup path no longer hoists the `cutoffDate` template into a local var (the repo computes it inside each method). SQLite parses both identically; named here for honesty. **Specific textual deltas worth flagging by name**: (1) the inline original built the analytics SELECT with a *double* space after `WHERE 1=1` (`WHERE 1=1  ${timeCondition} ${botCondition}`); the repo collapses that to a single space. SQLite tokenizes both the same. (2) The `disable`/`enable` paths previously had two separate SQL string literals (`SET is_enabled = 0` and `SET is_enabled = 1`); the repo collapses them into a single parameterized statement `SET is_enabled = ?` taking 0 or 1 as a bound value. Functionally identical — the service still owns the two `console.log` messages and the two callsites — but it's a SQL-shape change worth naming. (3) The cleanup path's `cutoffDate` local-var hoist (one declaration, three uses) is gone; each repo cleanup method computes the same `datetime('now', '-N days')` interpolation inline. Same output string per call site. **Serialization stays in the service**: `JSON.stringify(config)`, `JSON.stringify(metadata)` (for both `insertSession` and `insertRotation`), and `JSON.stringify(additionalData)` (for `insertMetric`) all run in ViewBotDatabaseService before the repo call — the repo only knows about strings. Boolean coercion via `Boolean(row.is_enabled)` etc. also stays in the service. **Constructor wiring**: `ViewBotDatabaseService` is a process-level singleton (the existing `if (ViewBotDatabaseService.instance) return ViewBotDatabaseService.instance;` pattern is preserved), so the repo is instantiated once inside the constructor's first-time branch (`this.repo = new ViewBotRepository()`). Mirrors the UserRepository / ChatBotRepository constructor shape — deps `{getAsync, runAsync, allAsync}` injectable for unit-test mocking, falling back to the real primitives from `database.js` when omitted. No bootstrap change (the singleton predates `bootstrap/services.js` and is not on the services bag); `expectedKeys` stays at 40, no `services.test.js` change. The trade-off (called out for honesty): the bootstrap fail-fast guard cannot detect a missing or shimmed repo dep — same trade-off the three existing repos carry. **`disableViewBot` + `enableViewBot` collapse into one repo method**: the two service methods had separate `UPDATE viewbots SET is_enabled = 0 ...` / `... = 1 ...` SQL; the repo exposes a single `setEnabledByBotId(botId, isEnabled)` that takes the value as a parameter. Functionally equivalent — the service still owns the two different `console.log` messages and the two callsites. **Analytics dynamic-fragment caveat**: the existing `getAnalytics` builds `timeCondition` and `botCondition` strings from a fixed `switch (timeframe)` over `'1h' / '24h' / '7d' / '30d' / default` and a boolean `botId ? 'AND bot_id = ?' : ''`. Those fragments cross the service-repo boundary as strings; the repo template-interpolates them. **This is safe because the fragment values are NOT user input** — they're a closed set produced by the service's switch — but it's worth flagging that the repo does NOT validate the strings it receives. Same SQL-build pattern that lived in the service pre-PR; no new attack surface, but a future contributor adding a new `timeframe` value must keep the fragment-string discipline (no user-controlled interpolation). **Tests**: 26 logical tests in [`server/tests/database/repository/ViewBotRepository.test.js`](server/tests/database/repository/ViewBotRepository.test.js) × 2 backend flags via `describe.each` = **52 test cases** counted by Jest (`Tests: 52 passed`). Every method covered — SQL shape (whitespace-normalized comparison against the documented string), parameter ordering (including the `upsertViewBot` correlated-subquery where `botId` appears twice and `endSession` where `session_id` is the trailing param), the constructor's fallback path (`new ViewBotRepository()` resolves to real primitive functions from `database.js`) and dep-injection path. The repo itself is backend-agnostic because all 26 SQL-shape tests use mocked primitives, but the `describe.each` matrix the Phase 6+ roadmap mandates is honored, and the constructor fallback test verifies the real wrapper functions resolve under either flag. **Suite count**: 651/651 passes under `--runInBand` (was 599/599 pre-PR; +52). The full-parallel `npm test` exhibits an intermittent ~20% flake on the unrelated pre-existing `server/tests/database/database-better.test.js` "rejects on SQL syntax error" test (the better-sqlite3 binding occasionally fails to throw on `db.prepare('NOT SQL')` when many native-binding-using workers run in parallel — reproducible on `main` with `for i in 1..5; do npm test; done` at the same rate, so flake is preexisting, not caused by this PR). **No bootstrap change, no ADR** (extends an established pattern; same "no ADR" footing as PR 5.3). **No service-side method-signature change** — all 14 public methods on `ViewBotDatabaseService` keep their existing signatures and return shapes. The structural affordance is that the next phase (PR 6.2 — `BuffRepository`, PR 6.3 — `ContinuousRecordingRepository`) follows the same shape mechanically.
- **`ChatBotService` inline SQL extracted into `ChatBotRepository` (PR 5.3, third and final Phase 5 PR).** Extends the repository pattern that started with `UserRepository` (PR-Q) to the heaviest DB-touching service in the codebase: 40 inline `database.runAsync`/`getAsync`/`allAsync` callsites across `server/services/ChatBotService.js` collapse to repository method calls. ChatBotService shrinks from 1364 → 1230 lines (net −134). No business-logic change; the migration is behavior-preserving (one textual delta: the `cleanupExpiredBots` cleanup SQL's `datetime("now")` corrected to the standard `datetime('now')` — SQLite treats both equivalently because the inner double-quoted token falls back to a string literal when no column matches, but single quotes is the canonical SQL-string-literal syntax and worth normalizing during a refactor). New file [`server/database/repository/ChatBotRepository.js`](server/database/repository/ChatBotRepository.js) covers the 5 tables ChatBotService touches: `chatbots` (CRUD + bulk enable/disable + temporary-bot specialization), `chatbot_sessions` (create/disconnect/touch/delete/list), `chatbot_message_history` (insert chat, insert movie_comment, query), `temporary_bots` (info/create/delete), `auto_summoned_bots` (delete-for-bot). Mirrors the UserRepository constructor pattern — deps `{getAsync, runAsync, allAsync}` injectable for unit-test mocking, falling back to the real primitives from `database.js` when omitted, so `new ChatBotRepository()` continues to work. ChatBotService's constructor gains a third optional dep `chatBotRepository` for the same purpose; defaults to `new ChatBotRepository()` so the existing factory wiring is byte-equivalent (no `expectedKeys` bump, no bootstrap test changes). **Serialization stays in the service**: `JSON.stringify(personality_traits)` and the movie-comment metadata blob are stringified by ChatBotService before the repo call — the repo only knows about strings. **`updateBot` simplification**: the old inline 11-branch `updates.push('field = ?'); params.push(value)` builder collapses into a `fields` object whose keys are then passed to a generic `repo.updateFields(id, fields)` that builds the SET clause + always appends `updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP`. The 11-column whitelist stays in `updateBot` (the request-side guard); the repo would happily SET any key passed, so the whitelist is the service's job. **`updateFields` empty-object case preserves legacy behavior**: the old inline builder unconditionally pushed `'updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP'`, so `updateBot({})` always ran an UPDATE that bumped only `updated_at`. The new `repo.updateFields(id, {})` matches that exactly. Pinned in a dedicated test (`empty fields object still bumps updated_at`). **`deleteTemporaryById` guard preserved**: the old inline `WHERE id = ? AND is_temporary = 1` clause is preserved in the repo method, so a stale expiration timer that fires after a temporary bot was promoted to permanent doesn't accidentally delete it. **Tests**: 37 new tests in [`server/tests/database/repository/ChatBotRepository.test.js`](server/tests/database/repository/ChatBotRepository.test.js) covering every method — SQL shape (whitespace-normalized regex against the documented string), parameter ordering, default values (e.g. `create`'s 7 documented defaults pin the legacy `createBot` SQL byte-for-byte: `is_enabled=1`, `response_interval_min=60`, `response_interval_max=180`, `show_robot_emoji=1`, `use_assigned_name=1`, `moviebot_enabled=0`, `response_creativity_temperature=0.7`), boolean coercion (`setEnabled` accepts `true`/`false`/`1`/`0`, all coerce to `1`/`0` via ternary), and the constructor's dep-injection / fallback paths. **Suite count**: 450/450 (was 413/413; +37 new). **Service-layer regression coverage is unchanged**: there are no pre-existing ChatBotService unit tests (`find server/tests -name "ChatBot*"` returns only the new repo test); the migration's correctness is enforced at the repo unit-test layer only, not end-to-end. The case for byte-equivalence is the mechanical 1:1 callsite swap + the repo tests pinning each SQL string + the full server-side suite continuing to pass. An end-to-end ChatBotService smoke test is a reasonable follow-up but not in this PR's scope. **No bootstrap factory change**: ChatBotRepository is instantiated inside ChatBotService.constructor (matching UserRepository's wiring inside AccountService.constructor), not exposed as a top-level service in `bootstrap/services.js`. `expectedKeys` stays at 39, no `bootstrap/services.test.js` updates required — the trade-off (called out for honesty) is that the bootstrap fail-fast guard cannot detect a missing or shimmed `chatBotRepository`. Same trade-off UserRepository carries. **No ADR**: extends an established pattern rather than making a structural decision (UserRepository's precedent is sufficient). **Scope deferred**: same shape could be applied to the next-heaviest services per the Phase 5 brief's ranking — `admin-recordings.js` (24 sites), `ViewBotDatabaseService` (20), `ClipService` (18), `AccountService` (16, partially repo'd via UserRepository), `ShopService` (15). Each is its own future PR; no PR 5.4 (per the Phase 5 brief: "There's no Phase 5.4. When PR 5.1 + PR 5.2 + maybe PR 5.3 are done, stop").

### Added
- **`better-sqlite3` adapter behind `USE_BETTER_SQLITE3` env flag (PR 5.2, second Phase 5 PR — [ADR-0014](docs/architecture/adr/0014-better-sqlite3-adapter.md)).** Lands the engine swap groundwork without changing the steady-state behavior of the 413-test suite: the adapter ships, the env flag is documented, the default is OFF. New dep `better-sqlite3@^11` alongside (not replacing) `sqlite3@^5.1.7`. New `server/database/database-better.js` exports `createBetterSqlite3Adapter(dbPath, {tuneForLargeReads, stmtCacheLimit})` → `{db, runAsync, getAsync, allAsync, close, walActive, cacheStats}`. The async wrappers are `Promise.resolve(syncCall)` — preserving the existing API across all paths a grep finds in use today (~357 `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` callsites), no migrations needed; the one drift is `runAsync(...).id` after a non-INSERT call where sqlite3 returns the last INSERT ever on the connection and better-sqlite3 returns 0 — grep finds zero consumers of that value, so it's dead state on either backend. **Prepared-statement cache**: `Map<sql_text, Statement>` keyed on verbatim SQL, insertion-order eviction at `stmtCacheLimit` (default 500). Hits/misses tracked via `cacheStats()`. The 357 callsites use string-literal SQL with bounded keyspace, so the cache effectively never evicts in steady state — first call parses, every subsequent call is one map lookup + a sync engine call. **PRAGMAs**: same contract as `server/database/applyPragmas.js` — `journal_mode = WAL`, `synchronous = NORMAL` (if WAL took), `foreign_keys = ON`, `busy_timeout = 5000`, plus the `tuneForLargeReads` block (`temp_store = MEMORY`, `mmap_size = 268435456`, `cache_size = -64000`) on the main handle. Verified against the live 2.2 GB DB snapshot copied to `/tmp/` — WAL stays active, all reads through the wrappers succeed, the 20-way concurrent +5/-5 PR-5.1 race against user_id=49's actual balance lands exact arithmetic and restores cleanly. **Wiring**: `server/database/database.js` modified to inspect `process.env.USE_BETTER_SQLITE3 === 'true'` at module load; on `true`, opens a second connection via the adapter, applies pragmas, reassigns the module-level `runAsync` / `getAsync` / `allAsync` to the adapter's wrappers, logs `better-sqlite3 adapter active`. **The sqlite3 `db` handle stays open and exported unchanged** — the ~14 callsites that bypass the wrappers and grab `db` directly (`server/routes/auth.js`, `moderation.js`, `admin.js`, `bug-reports.js`; `server/services/ChatBotLLMService.js`, `StreamBotService.js`; the ~6 migrations using `db.run` with callback shape) continue working on the sqlite3 path. **Connection count is four or more, not two**: WhitelistService and URLStreamDatabaseService each instantiate their own `new sqlite3.Database(...)` against the same file, so with the adapter active the process holds the sqlite3 main handle + the better-sqlite3 adapter + two service-owned sqlite3 handles. SQLite tolerates this; cost is one file descriptor + per-connection page cache per extra handle. **Worst-case event-loop hazard**: a better-sqlite3 write that hits SQLITE_BUSY blocks the event loop synchronously up to `busy_timeout=5000` ms while it spins for the writer lock. Real onestreamer.db writes are short (single-row UPDATEs, especially after PR 5.1's atomic refactor), so contention windows are microseconds — but a future long-running write would surface this as a tail-latency hazard; called out in ADR-0014's "Negative" section with a mitigation (drop the busy_timeout on the adapter handle to ~500 ms if it ever bites). **Failure mode**: if `require('better-sqlite3')` throws at module-load (e.g. native binding mismatch — common on Ubuntu noble's `libnode109`-patched Node 18.19.1 where the pre-built NMV-108 binary doesn't match the runtime NMV-109), the adapter loader catches, logs structured error, and leaves the sqlite3-backed wrappers in place. The flag is best-effort, not fail-stop. Runbook at [`docs/operations/runbooks/better-sqlite3-rebuild.md`](docs/operations/runbooks/better-sqlite3-rebuild.md) covers the one-time `node-gyp rebuild --nodedir=/usr/include/nodejs` step. **Tests**: 18 contract tests in `server/tests/database/database-better.test.js` cover `runAsync`/`getAsync`/`allAsync` return shapes, RETURNING semantics (SELECT, UPDATE RETURNING, no-match → undefined, guarded subtract floor-miss → undefined), prepared-statement cache (hits don't grow size, distinct SQL → distinct entries, eviction at limit respects insertion order), PRAGMA contract (file-backed handle gets WAL + tuneForLargeReads mmap/cache; `:memory:` ignores the latter as expected). 3 integration tests in `server/tests/database/database-better-points-race.test.js` re-run PR 5.1's atomic-points SQL through the real adapter (no mock) — 20-way concurrent +5/-5 against an in-memory better-sqlite3 DB seeded with a single `user_stats` row, plus a guarded-floor test where seed=30/amount=5/N=20 → exactly 6 succeed and final balance is exactly 0 (never below). 413/413 server-side suite still passes with the flag unset (steady state unchanged). 21/21 new adapter tests pass. **Engine note**: better-sqlite3@11 statically bundles SQLite engine 3.49.2 vs. sqlite3@5.1.7's 3.44.2 — both ≥ 3.35 (ADR-0013's RETURNING floor), the newer engine is a minor freebie. **Native-binding install hazard**: pinned to `better-sqlite3@11` because v12+ requires Node 20+ (current host is Node 18.19.1). On hosts where the pre-built binary doesn't match the runtime NMV, the one-time rebuild step is documented in the runbook above and gracefully degrades to sqlite3 if not run. **`runAsync(...).id` semantic drift after non-INSERT** (called out in ADR-0014's "Negative" section): sqlite3 returns the *last INSERT ever on this connection*'s rowid after an UPDATE/DELETE; better-sqlite3 returns `0`. Either is meaningless data; grep finds zero callsites that consume `runAsync(...).id` after a non-INSERT, so this is dead state on either backend. Pinned in the contract test as `typeof result.id === 'number'` without pinning a value. **Rollout plan** (in ADR-0014): Phase A = this PR (default OFF). Phase B = operator-side, flip the flag on a non-production host, walk the smoke path. Phase C = follow-up PR after days–weeks of observation, flip the default. Phase D = future PR, drop sqlite3 entirely, migrate the ~14 raw-`db` consumers + migrations to the adapter API. **Scope deferred**: PR 5.3 (repository-pattern rollout for the 3–5 most-touched DB-touching services — independent of backend choice, easier once the adapter is steady state); the Phase D dep-drop PR; `mmap_size` tuning above the current 256 MB (the DB is 2.2 GB, larger mmap could measurably reduce cold-read page-cache misses but too many free variables to isolate the effect until Phase C is stable).

### Fixed
- **Deploy pipeline no longer ships a stale frontend.** Discovered 2026-05-27 during a "PR merged but UI missing" report: the PR-W5 Relay Whitelist admin UI (merged 2026-05-26 as commit `3b5c09e`) was invisible despite `git pull` + `pm2 restart`. Root cause: nginx's `location /` catch-all serves the SPA from `/var/www/html` (per the routing in `/etc/nginx/sites-available/onestreamer.live`), and **nothing in the deploy flow ever rebuilt `client/` or rsynced `client/build` into that docroot**. `/var/www/html/index.html` was frozen at 2026-01-11 (bundle `main.af6f3bce.js`), meaning every client-side change merged between January and May had silently failed to reach users. Contributing factor: the `onestreamer-client` CRA dev server in `config/ecosystem.config.js` was retired 2026-05-26 with an in-file comment claiming "nginx serves the built bundle from /var/www/html" — true in topology, false in practice, because the docroot had been a stale one-time snapshot the entire time (the dev server on `:3443` was orphaned the whole time too, since the `upstream client_app` nginx block was commented out). [`scripts/deploy/start-production.sh`](scripts/deploy/start-production.sh) now runs `npm run build` and `sudo rsync -a --no-owner --no-group client/build/ /var/www/html/` between the SSL-cert check and the nginx reload — preserves `/var/www/html/blog`, `turn-test.html`, and the default nginx-debian page (no `--delete`). The `client/build` failure path aborts the deploy with the last 30 lines of build output. [`docs/operations/deployment.md`](docs/operations/deployment.md) "React build vs dev server in production" section rewritten to reflect the now-correct state and link the runbook; the "Deployment workflow (manual)" recipe gains the explicit build + rsync steps. [`config/ecosystem.config.js`](config/ecosystem.config.js)'s `onestreamer-client` comment points at the runbook and shows the manual incremental-deploy commands. New [`docs/operations/runbooks/stale-frontend-after-deploy.md`](docs/operations/runbooks/stale-frontend-after-deploy.md) gives the five-second bundle-hash comparison (`grep -oE 'main\.[a-f0-9]+\.js' /var/www/html/index.html` vs. `client/build/index.html`) as the diagnostic first move for any future "merged but missing" report — the symptom is recognizable in seconds before any code-review rabbit hole. Pre-fix `/var/www/html` snapshot preserved at `/var/www/html.bak-20260527-0205` for rollback. **No rollback was needed**: 4 months of frontend changes went live in one swap; the backend has been progressing faster than the frontend the entire time, so API contracts the new frontend uses already exist server-side. Live verification: `curl -ks https://onestreamer.live/static/js/main.7f4b6eb8.js | grep "Relay Whitelist"` returns matches; the admin UI now lists the new 🛡️ Relay Whitelist nav item under Services.

- **Atomic `addPoints` / `subtractPoints` in `AccountService` (PR 5.1, first Phase 5 PR — [ADR-0013a](docs/architecture/adr/0013a-atomic-sql-for-mutable-counters.md), renamed in PR 7.1 to break the ADR-0013 number collision with the AI moderation pipeline ADR).** Closes the lost-update race documented in `server/tests/services/AccountService.points-race.test.js` (the failing-test artifact shipped during Phase 2). Both methods were a read-compute-write loop: `SELECT points_balance` → JS arithmetic → `UPDATE user_stats SET points_balance = ?` with the absolute new value. Two concurrent callers (e.g. a buff purchase that subtracts and a chat-points award that adds in the same tick) both `SELECT`ed the same stale balance, both computed against it, both `UPDATE`d — second write overwrote first. Reproducible deterministically with a 20-way `Promise.all` of `addPoints(userId, 5)` against the existing microtask-interleaving DB mock (the race test asserted `toBeLessThan(N*amount)` while the bug was live). New impl: `addPoints` issues a single `UPDATE user_stats SET points_balance = points_balance + ?, updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP WHERE user_id = ? RETURNING points_balance` via `getAsync`; if no row is returned (target row didn't exist) it falls through to `INSERT INTO user_stats (user_id, points_balance) VALUES (?, ?)` with the increment as the initial balance. `subtractPoints` issues a guarded `UPDATE … SET points_balance = points_balance - ? … WHERE user_id = ? AND points_balance >= ? RETURNING points_balance` so the insufficient-balance check is part of the same atomic statement — two concurrent debits cannot both pass a JS-side `if (currentBalance < amount)` guard and then both succeed. On guard miss, a follow-up `SELECT points_balance` populates the error string (`Insufficient points balance. Has: X, Needs: Y`); that SELECT can race with concurrent mutations and report a slightly-stale balance in the *error message* — the *decision* (refuse the debit) is correct, only the narrative drifts. **Test contract flip**: `AccountService.points-race.test.js` now asserts `toBe(expectedIfAtomic)` for both add and subtract instead of the pre-fix `toBeLessThan` / `toBeGreaterThan` gates. The microtask-interleaving DB mock is updated to understand the new SQL shapes: the guarded subtract regex (longest pattern, with `AND points_balance >= ?`) matches before the plain add regex; both branches mutate the in-memory `userStats` row atomically per call and return `{points_balance}` for the RETURNING semantic. The third test (sequential `addPoints` control) is unchanged and still asserts the exact arithmetic answer — proves the math, not just the locking. **Callers unchanged**: the ~14 `addPoints` / `subtractPoints` consumers in `server/routes/internal.js`, `server/services/ShopService.js`, and `server/services/TimeTrackingService.js` all consume the return value (the post-write balance) which is byte-equivalent to the old impl; no signature change. **`runAsync` → `getAsync` shift**: `RETURNING` rows flow through `db.get`, not `db.run` (which discards rows), so the SQL is now issued via the existing `getAsync` helper. This bleeds slightly into PR 5.2's better-sqlite3 adapter design — the adapter must route `getAsync` through a `prepare().get()` path that understands `RETURNING`. Cross-referenced in ADR-0013's "Implementation notes". **`UNIQUE(user_id)` on `user_stats` NOT added in this PR**: a narrow second-tick race remains where two concurrent first-time `addPoints` callers both see no existing row and both `INSERT`. Production data shows zero duplicates today on the 2026-05-27 snapshot (`SELECT user_id, COUNT(*) FROM user_stats GROUP BY user_id HAVING COUNT(*) > 1` returns empty), and realistic concurrency for a *first* award to a *new* user is essentially zero (gated behind signup + first chat / first viewing minute / first stream). A follow-up PR can add the constraint + a backfill-safe `ALTER TABLE` migration when broader schema cleanup lands. **No schema change, no new dependency**, behaviour-equivalent for every non-racy code path, race-free for every racy one. **One small behaviour addition**: the new `UPDATE` now also sets `updated_at = CURRENT_TIMESTAMP` on `user_stats` rows; the pre-PR `UPDATE` didn't, so `updated_at` could lag the actual last-mutation by an arbitrary amount. Strictly more truthful; a `grep` finds zero consumers today that filter or order by `user_stats.updated_at`, but flagged here so a future query author isn't surprised. SQLite engine: `node-sqlite3@5.1.7` links engine 3.44.2 (≥ 3.35 required for `RETURNING`, confirmed via `SELECT sqlite_version()`). 3/3 tests pass on `AccountService.points-race.test.js`. **Phase 5 plan**: PR 5.2 (better-sqlite3 adapter behind an env flag, preserves the existing `runAsync`/`getAsync`/`allAsync` shape across all ~356 callsites) lands next; PR 5.3 (repository-pattern rollout for the 3–5 most-touched DB-touching services) is conditional on what 5.1 + 5.2 leave behind.

### Changed
- **Partial decomposition of `startServer()` in `server/index.js` (PR 4.3, third and last Phase 4 PR — [ADR-0012](docs/architecture/adr/0012-startserver-decomposition-partial.md)).** Closes Phase 4. The orchestrator file shrinks from 6014 lines to 5703 (~311 lines extracted in this PR; ~507 lines across all three Phase 4 PRs). Two highest-ROI, lowest-risk sections extracted: (a) **`server/routes/social-embed.js`** — both Open Graph / Twitter Card / JSON-LD rewrite handlers (`GET /blog/:slug` and `GET /clips/:clipId`) totalling ~290 lines of pure Express middleware that didn't touch any service except `clipService`. The two inline `escapeHtml` copies dedupe into one module-level helper. `renderBlogHtml` and `renderClipHtml` are separated from the route bodies so the templating can be unit-tested without booting the server (no tests added in this PR — the originals had zero coverage and we're not introducing new behaviour, but the structural affordance is now there). The Strapi fetch URL constant and the OneStreamer base URL are also lifted to module-scope constants. (b) **`server/bootstrap/start-listeners.js`** — HTTP + HTTPS `.listen(port, host, callback)` block (~20 lines). The `httpServer.on('error', ...)` handler from the same neighbourhood is deliberately left inline in `server/index.js` because it's a long-lived runtime concern, not a startup concern — moving it would imply the listener helper owns the lifecycle. **Deleted**: the 5-second-interval `setInterval(() => { /* commented log */ }, 5000)` "keep-alive" timer at the bottom of `startServer()`. Body was a commented-out `console.log`; the timer was no-op work that added to the leaked-handle tally in `background-work.md`. Node doesn't need a setInterval to stay alive (listening sockets keep the process up). Same criteria as PR 4.2's two dev-debug `setTimeout` deletions: no production value, ungated debug code. **Deliberately NOT extracted in this PR**: the ~500-line MediaSoup-vs-LiveKit branch in `startServer()` — decomposing it correctly requires first aligning the two backends' diverged URL-relay / WhitelistEnforcer / SimpleViewBotRotation wire-up (currently 90% identical but diverging in 6+ places that look symmetric but aren't), which is a behaviour-sensitive refactor that warrants its own ADR + reviewer pass. Phase 4 closes without that work; it's logged as the headline target of a future Phase-4 follow-up PR rather than reopening Phase 4 here. **`mountSocialEmbedRoutes(app, deps)` signature**: different from most existing `server/routes/*` modules (which take a service instance and return a sub-router) because the blog/clip handlers register two GET handlers on specific paths and fall through to static / React when the input doesn't match — a sub-router would obscure that semantic. Both shapes are valid Express patterns; the new one matches the "intercept-or-fall-through" intent better. **Behaviour-equivalent, not byte-equivalent** (review-feedback correction to the original draft): three concrete textual differences in the extracted module — JSON-LD object literal rewritten from double-quoted-key to ES shorthand (`JSON.stringify` output identical so wire format matches); `imageUrl` selection restructured from `if/else if/else` mutation into an early-return helper; the unused `const https = require('https')` from the inline original silently dropped. The two inline `escapeHtml` definitions were verified byte-identical (not "slightly different" as the first ADR draft hedged) and collapse into one module function. **Adjacent fix**: review pass caught a duplicate `path.join(__dirname, '..', 'client', 'build', 'index.html')` survival — once in the new `mountSocialEmbedRoutes` deps, again inline at the catch-all React route. Both now reference a single module-scope `CLIENT_BUILD_INDEX_PATH` constant declared near the existing `PORT` / `HTTPS_PORT` block. **Phase 4 close-out status** in [ADR-0012](docs/architecture/adr/0012-startserver-decomposition-partial.md), updated post-review to be explicit that this is a deferral (not "Phase 4 complete") — the 500-line MediaSoup/LiveKit branch alignment is the headline follow-up. 69/69 pass on the bootstrap + LifecycleManager + AdminHandler suites.

### Added
- **`LifecycleManager` registry for deferred one-shot work (PR 4.2, second Phase 4 PR — [ADR-0011](docs/architecture/adr/0011-lifecycle-manager.md)).** Closes the hazard documented in [`docs/architecture/background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) "Notable hazards / `setTimeout` chains in `server/index.js` startup": at the start of Phase 4 there were **9 scheduler-candidate `setTimeout` callsites** (7 in `server/index.js`, 2 inside `server/sockets/DisconnectHandler.js` after PR 4.1) where the timer handle was discarded immediately, so `clearTimeout()` was impossible and a SIGTERM landing inside any of those grace windows fired the callback against half-torn-down state — sometimes a swallowed exception, sometimes a wedged child process, occasionally a zombie rotation cycle. New [`server/services/LifecycleManager.js`](server/services/LifecycleManager.js) is the registry: `schedule(name, fn, delayMs)` returns a handle and tracks it in a `Set`; `cancel(handle)` proactively drops one; `async stop()` clears every pending handle and refuses further `schedule()` calls. Errors from `fn` are caught + logged with the task name and original `delayMs` — symmetry with the existing inline pattern where every `setTimeout(async () => {...})` site already absorbed its own exceptions, plus the structured-log line now gives production telemetry an attribution path. **Two windows, not one** (review-feedback fix on PR 4.2): `stop()` closes both the *pre-fire* race (clearTimeout on every pending handle) AND the *post-fire-mid-await* race (tracks every in-flight fn promise in `this.inFlight` and `Promise.allSettled`s them before resolving). The first draft only handled the pre-fire window — the `async stop()` qualifier was misleading because there was nothing to await, and an in-flight fn would have run free against torn-down services. The shutdown loop's per-service 5-second `Promise.race` deadline still bounds the total wait. **`delayMs` validation** (review-feedback fix): non-numeric / NaN / negative / Infinity `delayMs` warns + returns null, mirroring the existing `name` and `fn` validators. `setTimeout(fn, NaN)` would have fired immediately with no attribution. **Wiring**: constructed in [`server/bootstrap/services.js`](server/bootstrap/services.js)'s `createServices` factory with no deps (`expectedKeys` bumps 38 → 39); appended **last** to the `stoppables` array so the shutdown loop's reverse-iteration drains it **first** — any pending deferred work scheduled against the other services is cancelled before those services tear down. Threaded into `server/index.js` via the existing module-scope destructure block alongside the three notifiers, and threaded into `DisconnectHandler.js` via the existing per-connection deps bag. **Relocated callsites** (7): `server/index.js:4077` (post-stream rotation, 5 s); `:4969` (random-rotation autostart, MediaSoup branch, 5 s); `:5068` (random-rotation autostart, LiveKit branch, 5 s); `:5259` (viewBotRotation start, 10 s); `:5667` (AccountDeletionScheduler start, 5 s); `DisconnectHandler.js` (viewbot-rotation restart after real-user disconnect, 3 s); `DisconnectHandler.js` (real-streamer status validate, 1 s). Each gets a unique name (`'post-stream-rotation'`, `'random-rotation-autostart-mediasoup'`, `'random-rotation-autostart-livekit'`, `'viewbot-rotation-start'`, `'account-deletion-scheduler-start'`, `'viewbot-rotation-restart-after-disconnect'`, `'real-streamer-status-validate'`) so the structured-log attribution is real. **Deleted callsites** (2 — dev-debug code that shipped to production unguarded): `server/index.js:5150` was a 5-second `global.io.emit('test-event', {test: true})` whose only purpose was to sanity-check `global.io` was set; the two preceding `typeof` log lines already cover that diagnostic. `:5706` iterated every authenticated session at boot and logged `getStreamerDisplayName(socketId) = "..."` for each — useful when the lookup was being added, dead chatter now and never gated behind `NODE_ENV`. Both deletions are behaviour changes (a motivated dev relying on either loses their affordance), but unguarded debug code is more noise than signal; if either is wanted back it should land behind `process.env.NODE_ENV !== 'production'`. **Untouched** (3 — different shapes, not scheduler candidates): `:5749` `setTimeout` inside a `Promise.race` deadline already correctly captures + clears its handle in the loop's `finally`; `:5920` `await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 500))` is a sleep, not a deferred callback; `:5705` is commented out. **Adjacent fix** (called out by ADR-0011's "Consequences"): the `'account-deletion-scheduler-start'` task body now also pushes the scheduler onto `stoppables` after `.start()`, closing a pre-existing gap where the scheduler's `setInterval` (15-day grace check, per background-work.md "Owned" table) was leaking on SIGTERM because the scheduler was constructed inside a setTimeout and so the bootstrap factory couldn't have registered it. This is a behaviour change adjacent to the headline relocation, but it's directly in scope because the deferred construction is exactly the failure mode this PR is closing. **Tests**: new `server/tests/services/LifecycleManager.test.js` (14 tests) covers schedule + cancel + stop + validation + error swallowing + edge cases (cancel-after-fire returns false, cancel-foreign-handle returns false, schedule-after-stop returns null). Bootstrap test (`server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js`) updated: mock + identity-pin `LifecycleManager` ctor `()`; `expectedKeys` bumped to 39; 2 new tests (no-arg ctor, lifecycleManager is the last entry in `stoppables`). 65/65 pass on the bootstrap + LifecycleManager + AdminHandler suites. **Scope deferred**: PR 4.3 — full `startServer()` decomposition so Phase 5 (better-sqlite3 + atomic points updates) can start without the surrounding orchestration noise. Also requires an ADR. `background-work.md`'s "Notable hazards / `setTimeout` chains" entry is rewritten to record resolution + pointer to ADR-0011.

### Changed
- **Sweep the last six inline `socket.on(...)` listeners out of `server/index.js` (PR 4.1, first Phase 4 PR).** Per [`docs/architecture/socket-events-actual.md`](docs/architecture/socket-events-actual.md)'s "Listener concentration" table, `server/index.js` held 6 inline socket listeners as of the start of Phase 4 — the only file in the `services/` + `sockets/` tree still registering events outside an extracted handler. This PR completes the extraction. Two listeners (`request-stream`, `request-test-stream`) move into the existing [`server/sockets/StreamHandler.js`](server/sockets/StreamHandler.js) because they are the viewer-side companions to `stream-offer` / `stream-answer` / `stop-streaming`. Three listeners (`drawing-path-complete`, `drawing-path-start`, `drawing-path-update`) move into a new [`server/sockets/DrawingHandler.js`](server/sockets/DrawingHandler.js) — pure `socket.broadcast.emit` relays with no service touch, so the module takes no `deps` bag and its signature is `(io, socket)` rather than the `(io, socket, deps)` shape the other `register*Handler` modules use (review-feedback fix: an unused `_deps` parameter is dead weight). The sixth listener (`disconnect`) moves into a new [`server/sockets/DisconnectHandler.js`](server/sockets/DisconnectHandler.js) — the heaviest of the three because it orchestrates per-socket teardown across mediasoup, sessions, time tracking, ViewBot Plain RTP cleanup, takeover cooldowns, stream-ended chokepoint broadcast, and viewer-count fanout. **Behaviour preservation**: behaviour-equivalent (whitespace re-flowed when the indented inline body moved to top-level inside `module.exports = function`, so it isn't *byte*-equivalent — review feedback corrected the original CHANGELOG draft). Same control flow, same logging, same error swallowing on the transport-close `try/catch`. The 16-key `deps` bag for `DisconnectHandler` threads `mediasoupService`, `sessionService`, `timeTrackingService`, `notifiedStreamers`, `viewbotSocketIds`, `cleanupViewbotUsername`, `plainTransportService`, `streamService`, `takeoverService`, `streamingLogsService`, `streamNotifier`, `notifyViewersStreamEnded`, `viewerCountNotifier`, `SimpleViewBotRotation`, plus `getViewbotService` / `getViewBotClientService` as lazy getters (both are late-init, reassigned by `startServer` after MediaSoup setup — the getter pattern is the same one `StreamHandler` and `ViewBotHandler` use). The getter result is captured once per disconnect at the top of the handler so a mid-handler re-init can't half-apply across branches. **Registration order preserved**: `DisconnectHandler` registers its `disconnect` listener at the same point in the `io.on('connection', ...)` block where the inline one used to sit — after `registerGameHandler` (which also registers a scoped `disconnect`) and before `registerEffectHandler`. Same firing order as before. **Two nested `setTimeout`s in the disconnect body** (3 s viewbot-rotation restart after a real-user disconnect; 1 s real-streamer-status validation) are deliberately preserved in-place rather than relocated — PR 4.2 (the LifecycleManager work) takes them as part of the broader scheduler-registry effort, alongside the four boot-autostart `setTimeout`s in `startServer()` and the rotation-restart `setTimeout` after stream end. Inline TODO comments on both sites name PR 4.2 so a reviewer doesn't repropose the same relocation. **`server/index.js` shrinks by ~196 lines** (6198 → 6002). The file is now free of inline `socket.on(...)` calls; future drift back into inline-handler territory will be caught by the existing `grep` recipe at the bottom of `socket-events-actual.md`. **No new tests**: following the existing handler-extraction pattern. `AdminHandler` was the pilot and got a full integration-test file (`server/tests/sockets/AdminHandler.test.js`); subsequent extractions (BuffHandler, EffectHandler, GameHandler, MediaSoupHandler, StreamHandler, ViewBotHandler) all moved listeners and did not ship their own per-handler integration tests — the existing 49 bootstrap + AdminHandler tests still pass. This PR matches that precedent: the relocations are mechanical, the destination handlers are wired through the same `register*Handler(io, socket, deps)` shape that the other 7 handlers already use, and the bootstrap fail-fast guard (PR 2.3 / #99) continues to catch missing deps at the service-construction layer. **No ADR**: the brief flagged this as the smallest of the three Phase 4 PRs and "probably doesn't qualify" — confirmed, since the extraction continues an established pattern rather than making a structural choice. **Scope deferred**: (a) PR 4.2 — LifecycleManager for the 7 real scheduler-candidate `setTimeout` sites (4 boot autostarts at `server/index.js:5158/5257/5448/5856`; 3 event-reactive at `:4075/4899/4939` — the latter two are now inside `DisconnectHandler`). The two debug-only sites (`:5339` test emit, `:5895` `getStreamerDisplayName` smoke) are deletion candidates rather than scheduler candidates. The two non-scheduler shapes at `:5940` (Promise.race deadline with `clearTimeout`) and `:6111` (sleep) stay untouched. (b) PR 4.3 — full `startServer()` decomposition so Phase 5 (better-sqlite3 + atomic points updates) can start without the surrounding orchestration noise. Requires an ADR.

### Added
- **URL-relay whitelist finalization (PR-W6, Phase 5 of ADR-0010 — the last phase).** Closes the six-PR feature series. No new runtime behavior; pure documentation + env scaffolding. `URL_RELAY_REQUIRE_WHITELIST_SERVICE` is now documented in `.env.example` with its semantics: when set to `"true"` the server fails to start if `WhitelistService.initialize()` throws, vs. degrading to the Phase-0 pass-through (no policy enforcement) when unset. Recommended for production once the feature is live; left unset on dev hosts where the DB might not yet be migrated. The flag is **not** enabled by default in `.env.example` because the env file is a template — operators set it themselves on the live host. `docs/architecture/service-catalog.md` "Rotation + external feeds" section gains two rows for `WhitelistService.js` (per-platform `off`/`blacklist`/`whitelist` content filter, pure policy + DB + in-memory cache) and `WhitelistEnforcer.js` (mid-stream drift checker). `docs/architecture/overview.md` "See also" section now points at ADR-0010 and the implementation plan. The seed file (`server/data/seeds/url-relay-whitelist.seed.json`) already ships defaults `twitch: blacklist, kick: whitelist` per the ADR-0010 decision — that was set in PR-W1 and remains the canonical first-install state. The feature is now **operationally complete**: PR-W1 shipped the service + schema + seed, PR-W2 the direct-submission gate, PR-W3 the rotation candidate filter, PR-W4 the mid-stream drift enforcer, PR-W5 the admin UI + 7 API endpoints, and this PR closes the documentation loop. **Six PRs, ~3.6k lines added across server + client + tests + docs, no behavior regression in any existing path on any of the six rollouts.** Live smoke-test plan for operators (the only remaining step): on the host, set `URL_RELAY_REQUIRE_WHITELIST_SERVICE=true` in `/root/onestreamer/.env`, `pm2 restart onestreamer-server`, confirm `✅ WhitelistService initialized` + `✅ WhitelistEnforcer started (interval 60s)` in the log; hit the admin panel's "Relay Whitelist" tab, confirm both platforms load with the seeded modes (`twitch: blacklist`, `kick: whitelist`); submit a known-blocked URL (`twitch.tv/dreamwastaken` is on the seeded block list) and confirm 400 with `error: "Content policy: streamer_blocked:dreamwastaken", gateThatBlocked: "blacklist_streamer"`. The [operations runbook](docs/operations/runbooks/url-relay-whitelist.md) shipped in PR-W1 covers the rest.

### Removed
- **Three dead-code module-scope helpers in `server/index.js` + their `global.viewBotIntervals` Map (PR 3.4, the last Phase 3 PR).** The Phase 3 plan called out `server/index.js:859-883`'s `global.viewBotIntervals` Map as a "partial-cleanup leak — some paths clear, others don't" and the briefing's PR 3.4 was to relocate the Map into a ViewBot service instance. Mapping the actual callsites turned the work upside down: the three helpers that wrote to the Map — `createViewBotProducer` (defined `server/index.js:807-865` pre-PR), `startSyntheticMediaGeneration` (`:867-909`), and `generateViewBotRtpParameters` (`:911-1001`) — have **zero callers anywhere in the codebase since the initial commit**. Confirmed by: `grep -rn "createViewBotProducer" /root/onestreamer/server /root/onestreamer/client /root/onestreamer/chat-service` returns only the function's own `const X = async ...` definition; `git log --all -S "createViewBotProducer("` finds no commit that ever added a call site (only the definition's introduction commit). The "leak" was structurally impossible because the Map was never populated. The same is true of the two sibling helpers — they were only ever called from `createViewBotProducer`, so they share its dead-code status. PR 3.4 deletes all three helpers + the `global.viewBotIntervals` references (net ~195 lines removed from `server/index.js`); the truest "state unification" for an unreachable Map is no Map. The deletion is byte-equivalent at runtime (dead code can't have runtime effects), so no behaviour change, no test changes needed beyond the existing suites confirming nothing references the deleted symbols. [`docs/architecture/background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) updated: the two table rows at `:867` and `:879` are struck through with a pointer to this CHANGELOG entry; the standalone "Notable hazards / `global.viewBotIntervals` Map" section is rewritten to record that the briefing's reading-the-file-not-tracing-callers framing was wrong and that the fix is removal, not relocation. **Phase 3 status**: this closes the Phase 3 plan. PR 3.1 (StreamNotifier, 17 sites), PR 3.2 (ViewerCountNotifier, 13 sites), and PR 3.3 (BuffNotifier, 28 sites) collapsed 58 socket-emit sites into three chokepoints; PR 3.4 confirmed the fourth target was already gone in practice. Phase 4 (`server/index.js` decomposition into a `LifecycleManager`) is unblocked.

### Added
- **URL-relay whitelist admin UI + routes (PR-W5, Phase 4 of ADR-0010).** Closes the operator-facing surface. PR-W1–W4 made the policy enforce itself; this PR makes it editable without touching the DB. New `server/routes/whitelist.js` exposes 7 admin-only endpoints (all behind `authenticateAdmin`): `GET /api/whitelist/config` returns both platforms' config rows + entry rows in a shape the UI can consume directly; `POST /api/whitelist/mode` takes `{platform, mode}` and routes to `WhitelistService.setMode`; `POST /api/whitelist/fallback` updates `fallback_category` / `fallback_evergreen` / `drift_check_seconds`; `POST /api/whitelist/entry` adds an allow/block entry; `DELETE /api/whitelist/entry/:id` removes one; `POST /api/whitelist/entry/:id/review` stamps `last_reviewed_at` for the 90-day re-review workflow; `GET /api/whitelist/audit?action=X&limit=N` returns the recent audit log with optional action filter (limit clamped to 500). The actor on every mutation is pulled from `req.user.username` so audit rows correctly attribute the operator. Routes are mounted unconditionally — the handlers themselves return 503 when `app.locals.whitelistService` is missing, so a host whose PR-W1 init failed still surfaces a meaningful error rather than a 404. New `client/src/services/whitelistApi.ts` is a thin typed wrapper over the 7 endpoints; it accepts the same `makeApiCall` helper that AdminPanelV3 injects into other components (preserves auth header threading + per-error log lines). New `client/src/components/admin/WhitelistManagement.tsx` is the operator UI: platform tabs (Twitch / Kick), mode dropdown with inline help text per mode, fallback-category + fallback-evergreen text inputs with a Save button, add-entry form with type/list/value/risk/notes fields, side-by-side allow + block tables with per-row Mark-Reviewed (✓) and Remove (×) buttons, and a recent-audit table at the bottom. Inline styles match the AdminPanelV3 dark theme; no new CSS file because the panel doesn't need anything beyond what the existing palette provides. Wired into AdminPanelV3's navigation as a new "Relay Whitelist" item (icon 🛡️) in the "Services" category, right after "URL Stream Relay". 10 new server tests in `server/tests/routes/whitelist.test.js` covering: 503 when service unset; config endpoint returns shaped rows; setMode delegates with actor from `req.user`; service rejection bubbles as 400; addEntry returns 201 with new ID; DELETE parses :id; review endpoint; fallback forwards all fields; audit endpoint clamps limit to 500 and forwards action filter. RTL UI tests are deferred — the existing admin-side test infrastructure focuses on services-not-components; a `WhitelistManagement.test.tsx` would be a useful addition but is out of scope for this PR. 372/372 overall (+10 new). **Phase 4/5 boundary**: this PR ships the operator-facing surface; PR-W6 (Phase 5) flips production defaults: sets `URL_RELAY_REQUIRE_WHITELIST_SERVICE=true` in the env, updates `docs/architecture/overview.md` to reflect the now-active service, and marks ADR-0010 as the canonical reference.

- **URL-relay whitelist drift enforcer (PR-W4, Phase 3 of ADR-0010).** Closes the last of three URL-relay surfaces — and the one a static allow/block list can't catch on its own: a whitelisted streamer switching their own category mid-broadcast to something not on the policy. New `WhitelistEnforcer` service runs a `setInterval` poll (default 60s) inside the main server process. Each tick: gets the active URL relay via `viewBotURLService.getActiveURLStream()`; if non-Twitch/non-Kick, skip; otherwise re-fetch a fresh snapshot via new `TwitchRandomService.getCurrentStreamSnapshot(login)` (`/helix/streams?user_login=` for game + is_mature, then `/helix/channels?broadcaster_id=` for CCL — the second is wrapped in a try/catch so a Helix degradation doesn't abort the check) or `KickRandomService.getCurrentStreamSnapshot(login)` (single `getChannelInfo` via the kick-api-helper Python subprocess); pass the snapshot to `WhitelistService.isStillAllowed`. On a non-allow decision, the enforcer calls `viewBotURLService.stopURLStream(urlId)` (the existing rotation failure handler turns this into a rotation), emits a new `whitelist-drift-stop` socket event (`{urlId, login, platform, reason, gateThatBlocked, currentGameName}`) so the admin UI in PR-W5 can surface what happened, and writes a `drift_block` audit row via `WhitelistService.logAudit`. **Platform-API degradation tolerance**: one snapshot fetch failure is silently skipped (`snapshot_failed_first`); subsequent failures inside a 3-minute window are still skipped (`snapshot_failed_recent`) — we keep last-known-good state and don't stop the stream on transient flakes. Beyond 3 minutes of failures we err on the safe side and stop (`platform_degraded_extended`), on the assumption that an extended outage shouldn't keep a possibly-out-of-policy relay running. Snapshot success clears the failure timer for that urlId. **Wiring**: instantiated in `server/index.js` on both MediaSoup and LiveKit branches immediately after `RandomStreamRotationService` is set up (the enforcer borrows the same `twitchService` + `kickService` instances the rotation service owns — no duplicate construction). Guarded by `if (whitelistService)` and `start()` is called immediately. The timer is `.unref()`'d so it doesn't keep the process alive on shutdown. **Login extraction**: `_loginFromActive(active)` delegates to `viewBotURLService.extractorService.extractIdentifier(url)` when available (PR-W2's helper pattern), with a naive regex fallback if not. **Interval source**: per the schema, `url_relay_filter_config.drift_check_seconds` exists (default 60), but `chooseFallback` doesn't currently surface it. Phase 4 (admin UI) will read this from the DB explicitly; for now the default constant is in `WhitelistEnforcer.DEFAULT_DRIFT_CHECK_SECONDS`. **Why a separate service rather than inside `WhitelistService`**: WhitelistService is pure policy (in-memory cache + DB writes). WhitelistEnforcer orchestrates I/O — platform polls, stream stops, socket emits. Keeping them separate lets us unit-test policy without mocking the world. **Tests**: 11 new tests in `server/tests/services/WhitelistEnforcer.test.js` covering: `start()` with missing deps no-ops (won't crash on a half-init host); `start()/stop()` lifecycle; tick with no active stream skips; YouTube relay skips (platform_not_gated); whitelisted streamer still in policy → no-op + no emit; streamer drifted to non-whitelisted category → stops + audits + emits with full payload shape (Should-not-leak-control-fields assertion); single snapshot failure → skipped; failure inside 3-min window → still skipped; failure beyond 3-min window → stop on the safe side; recovery after failure clears the timer; Kick path uses `kickService.getCurrentStreamSnapshot` and does NOT call `twitchService`. The `setInterval` lifecycle itself is trivial and exercised by start/stop. 360/360 overall (+11 enforcer tests + the two new `getCurrentStreamSnapshot` helpers are exercised indirectly through the enforcer's mocked stubs; integration with the live Helix API is operator-smoke-tested). **What's deferred to PR-W5 (Phase 4)**: admin UI surfacing the `whitelist-drift-stop` event, reading `drift_check_seconds` from DB, and a stats endpoint for "how many drift stops in the last 24h." **What's deferred to PR-W6 (Phase 5)**: setting `URL_RELAY_REQUIRE_WHITELIST_SERVICE=true` in prod, finalizing defaults.

- **URL-relay whitelist rotation filter (PR-W3, Phase 2 of ADR-0010).** Closes the second of three URL-relay surfaces that needed gating after PR-W1 shipped the `WhitelistService` and PR-W2 gated direct admin submissions. Now the random rotation discovery loop (`RandomStreamRotationService._rotateToNewStream` → `TwitchRandomService.findRandomStreamer` / `KickRandomService.findRandomStreamer`) also consults the service. Three new setters with identical shape: `TwitchRandomService.setWhitelistService(svc)`, `KickRandomService.setWhitelistService(svc)`, and a fan-out `RandomStreamRotationService.setWhitelistService(svc)` that thread the same instance into both inner services. Setters are guarded with `typeof inner.setWhitelistService === 'function'` so a future refactor that removes one inner service (Phase 4's bootstrap rollup) doesn't fail loudly. **Twitch flow**: cheap local filters (viewer count, exclude-list, recent cache) run first to avoid wasting Helix API budget on candidates that wouldn't be picked. Then `_attachCclData(candidates)` makes one batched `GET /helix/channels?broadcaster_id=X&broadcaster_id=Y…` call (≤100 per batch) to fetch `content_classification_labels` for every survivor and attaches them as `_ccls`. The shaped candidate `{login: user_login, currentGameName: game_name, isMature: stream.is_mature, ccls: _ccls}` is then passed to `WhitelistService.filterCandidates('twitch', ...)`. CCL fetch failure is non-fatal — we log and proceed with empty CCL data so the mature_flag/ccl_gate checks become no-ops but the streamer/category list still applies. **Kick flow**: same shape minus CCL (Kick's `/livestreams` response doesn't expose CCL-equivalent labels yet; we pass `hasMatureContent: stream.is_mature === true || stream.has_mature_content === true` as a defense-in-depth check against the rarely-populated field). **Legacy blockedCategories cutover**: the local hardcoded `blockedCategories: ['ASMR', 'Pools, Hot Tubs, and Beaches']` Set on both `TwitchRandomService` (constructor line 22) and `KickRandomService` (line 18) is preserved as a fallback — it's consulted only when `this.whitelistService === null`. The seed data already migrates both entries into the DB as blacklist rows, so when WhitelistService IS wired the local Set is redundant. **The two duplicate filter paths on `RandomStreamRotationService.js:106` settings + the `_rotateToNewStream` pass-through** are untouched — they're operator-tunable per-rotation config (e.g. an admin can extend the runtime block list via the random-rotation settings without going through the DB whitelist), and removing them would be a behavior change for operators who've already added to the settings. Wired in `server/index.js` on both MediaSoup and LiveKit branches immediately after `setStreamNotifier`, guarded by `if (whitelistService)`. **Tests**: 13 new server tests across three new files — `server/tests/services/TwitchRandomService.whitelist.test.js` (9 tests: setter, `_attachCclData` no-op on empty, no-op on missing user_id, single batch with mocked /helix/channels response, batches in groups of 100 with a 250-item input fan-out to 3 calls, defaults missing broadcaster_id to empty CCL array, CCL fetch rejection bubbles to caller, legacy blockedCategories preserved); `KickRandomService.whitelist.test.js` (3 tests: setter, default null, legacy preserved); `RandomStreamRotationService.whitelist-fanout.test.js` (2 tests: setter delegates to both inner services, does not throw when inner services lack the setter). Full `findRandomStreamer` end-to-end with a Twitch token and live API is not exercised — the legacy `KickRandomService.test.js` already pins the broader filter pipeline. **Phase 2/3 boundary**: this PR closes the rotation surface; the third (drift enforcement — catching a whitelisted streamer who switches game mid-broadcast) lands in PR-W4 as a new `WhitelistEnforcer` service polling the active relay every `drift_check_seconds` (default 60).

- **`BuffNotifier` collapses 28 buff/inventory emit sites across 3 events into one chokepoint (PR 3.3).** Third PR of Phase 3 — the structurally messiest of the three because the emits were split across **four layers**: services (`BuffDebuffService` ×4, `ItemUseService` ×4, `DrawingService` ×1, `ThrowingService` ×1 — total 10), socket handlers (`BuffHandler` ×11, `StreamHandler` ×2 — total 13), inline route handlers (`routes/items.js` ×3), and `server/index.js` (×2 — `streamer-buffs-update` clears on viewbot/legacy-viewbot stops). The Phase 3 plan called this out as "the mix is the structural issue" — owning emit logic from inside a route handler bypasses the service layer's invariants. (`server/routes/buffs.js` does NOT contain any buff-cluster emits — that claim in the original Phase 3 briefing was wrong.) New [`server/services/BuffNotifier.js`](server/services/BuffNotifier.js) replaces all 28 sites with calls to one of three methods: `streamerBuffsUpdate({ buffs, toSocket? })` for `streamer-buffs-update` — broadcast via `io.emit` OR per-socket via `socket.emit` (the per-query response variant in `BuffHandler.on('get-streamer-buffs')`); `inventoryUpdated({ toSocketId, action, itemId, quantity, remainingQuantity? })` for `inventory-updated` — always targeted via `io.to(socketId).emit`; `buffError({ toSocket, error })` for `buff-error` — always per-calling-socket. **Action-string pinning**: `BuffNotifier.INVENTORY_ACTIONS` is a Set of the 6 distinct `action` values produced by the 9 `inventory-updated` callsites (`purchase`, `sell`, `grant`, `use`, `draw`, `throw`); strict-equality size check in tests forces deliberate baseline updates for future additions, and per-action `test.each` catches deletions. Same pattern as `StreamNotifier.REASONS` from PR 3.1. The other two events have no discriminator fields (`{ buffs }` and `{ error }` only) so no pinning needed. **Construction**: `new BuffNotifier(io)` — single dep, no other state. Wired in [`server/bootstrap/services.js`](server/bootstrap/services.js) before `buffDebuffService` so the latter can take it via its existing 5th-arg options bag (alongside `itemRepository`); `expectedKeys` bumps 37 → 38. The 4 internal `this.io.emit('streamer-buffs-update', …)` sites in `BuffDebuffService` now check `if (this.buffNotifier) buffNotifier.streamerBuffsUpdate(…) else this.io.emit(…)` — the fallback preserves behaviour when the notifier isn't wired (test fixtures, etc.), same pattern as PR 3.1's `LiveKitService` / `WebRTCViewBotRotation` fallbacks. **Threading**: `StreamHandler` and `BuffHandler` get the notifier in their existing `deps` bags (passed from `registerStreamHandler` / `registerBuffHandler` callsites in `server/index.js`); the 2 server/index.js emit sites read from the module-scope destructure alongside `streamNotifier` and `viewerCountNotifier`; `app.set('buffNotifier', buffNotifier)` exposes it to route handlers (route side: `routes/items.js` adds `const buffNotifier = req.app.get('buffNotifier')` to each of the 3 inventory-updated callsites + threads it into the `services` / method-arg bag passed to `itemUseService.useItem`, `drawingService.startDrawing`, `throwingService.startThrow`). **Method-arg services** (`ItemUseService.useItem`, `DrawingService.startDrawing`, `ThrowingService.startThrow`) destructure `buffNotifier` from their existing call-time options bag — passed in by `routes/items.js` alongside `io` and `sessionService`. **Bootstrap test** (`server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js`): mock + identity-pin `BuffNotifier` ctor `(io)`; identity-pin the buffDebuffService 5th-arg options bag to assert `{ buffNotifier: <factory's buffNotifier> }`; bump `expectedKeys` to 38. **Tests** (`server/tests/services/BuffNotifier.test.js` — 31 new tests): ctor throws on missing io; `INVENTORY_ACTIONS` baseline + strict-size pin; `streamerBuffsUpdate` broadcast vs per-socket variant; broadcast accepts empty array (the stream-end clear); `toSocket` key never leaks into the wire payload; suppress + warn on non-array buffs; `inventoryUpdated` targets via `io.to(socketId).emit`, omits `remainingQuantity` when absent, includes it when present, all 6 baseline actions accepted without warn, unknown action warns + emits, missing `toSocketId` or `action` suppresses + warns; `buffError` per-socket emit, suppress + warn on missing `toSocket` / empty string / non-string error. Bootstrap suite +2 net tests (new buffNotifier ctor identity + buffDebuffService 5th-arg identity, alongside a 4→5 args-count update on the existing buffDebuffService test). Full server-side suite passes. **Behaviour preservation**: wire format byte-equivalent for every callsite. Same event names, same payload shapes, same target scopes (broadcast / targeted / per-socket).
