Single intentional payload change: the per-query `streamer-buffs-update` response in `BuffHandler.get-streamer-buffs` was previously `socket.emit('streamer-buffs-update', { buffs })`; the chokepoint preserves the per-socket scope when `toSocket` is set, so the emit still goes to the same socket with the same payload shape. **buffError suppression breadcrumb (post-review fix)**: the new validator suppresses + warns on missing `toSocket` / empty / non-string `error` (strict improvement over the old code's `socket.emit('buff-error', { error: undefined })` from re-thrown non-Error values), but originally only `console.warn`'d the validator condition — losing the underlying exception. Post-review patch adds `console.error('⚠️ BUFF_NOTIFIER: original error:', error)` inside the suppression path so the operator still has a server-log breadcrumb when the wire emit is dropped. **Live-exposure note**: the route-side fallback path in `routes/items.js` previously emitted `io.to(socketId).emit('inventory-updated', …)` directly when `io && sessionService` were both present; the new code requires `io && sessionService && buffNotifier` — strictly tighter, but `buffNotifier` is always present once the bootstrap factory has run (the `app.set` runs synchronously at module load before `httpServer.listen` is called inside `startServer()`), so in practice the guard's behaviour is unchanged. **Scope deferred**: (a) the action surface for `inventory-updated` could expand to include `gift` or `expire` as future inventory operations land; the pin will surface those at test time. (b) `buff-error` doesn't pin its error-message surface — error messages are free-form by design (`error.message` from caught exceptions) and pinning the set would be brittle; the validation is "non-empty string" only. (c) ADR-0009 extended with a third "Subsequent applications" entry covering this PR. **Next**: PR 3.4 — `viewBotIntervals` state unification at `server/index.js:859-883` (relocate module-scope Map into a ViewBot service instance). Structurally different work (state relocation, not socket-emit chokepointing).
- **URL-relay whitelist submission gate (PR-W2, Phase 1 of ADR-0010).** Activates the `WhitelistService` scaffolding from PR-W1 against direct URL submissions. New `ViewBotURLService.setWhitelistService(svc)` setter follows the existing `setStreamService`/`setLiveKitService`/`setStreamNotifier` pattern. Two new private helpers: `_extractLoginFromUrl(url, platform)` delegates to `URLStreamExtractorService.extractIdentifier()` and lowercases the result so it matches `WhitelistService`'s canonical-form streamer keys; `_checkWhitelistGate(url, validation)` is the gate itself — returns `{allowed: true, reason: 'service_unset'}` when no service is wired (so Phase 0 behavior is preserved on hosts that haven't shipped the wire-up yet), `{allowed: true, reason: 'platform_not_gated'}` for non-Twitch/non-Kick platforms (YouTube, Facebook, Dailymotion, etc. — they're not in the whitelist's per-platform tables), and otherwise delegates to `WhitelistService.checkAllowed({platform, login, currentGameName: null, ...})`. Gate fires inside `startURLStream` immediately after `validateURL` succeeds and before the existing-stream stop block — earliest point at which platform + login are known, latest point before any side effects (no FFmpeg, no LiveKit ingress, no DB writes yet). Rejection returns `{success: false, error: 'Content policy: <reason>', urlId, gateThatBlocked: <gate>}`. The route handler in `server/routes/url-stream.js` is updated to forward `gateThatBlocked` alongside `error` in the 400 body (previously dropped) so the admin UI in PR-W5 can surface which gate (`mature_flag` / `ccl_gate` / `blacklist_streamer` / `blacklist_category` / `whitelist_miss`) rejected the submission. The `_startingStream` mutex is released by the existing `finally` clause so rejection doesn't leave the service in a "starting" state. The `currentGameName` is passed as `null` deliberately — at validation time we don't have the current Twitch/Kick category yet; `whitelist` mode callers will fall through to the streamer allowlist alone on this path. A post-extraction re-check that has the category in hand is deferred to PR-W3 (Phase 2) where it can share the API call that the rotation service is already making. Wired in `server/index.js` on both the MediaSoup branch and LiveKit branch immediately after their respective `setSocketIO`/`setStreamNotifier` blocks; both branches use the same `app.locals.whitelistService` instance constructed in PR-W1. The wire-up is guarded by `if (whitelistService)`, and the PR-W1 bootstrap is amended to null out the local on init failure (previously the constructed-but-uninitialized object remained truthy, so the setter ran and the first `checkAllowed` call threw a cryptic "cache not initialized" instead of the intended Phase-0 pass-through). 12 new tests in `server/tests/services/ViewBotURLService.whitelist-gate.test.js` cover: setter stores the reference; `_extractLoginFromUrl` lowercases Twitch + Kick and returns null on platform mismatch / unparseable / empty input; `_checkWhitelistGate` passes through when service is unset, passes through for non-gated platforms (and does NOT call the stub), delegates to the service for Twitch + Kick with correctly-shaped `{platform, login, currentGameName: null}` snapshot, handles missing validation gracefully, handles URL with unrecognized platform tag. The full `startURLStream` end-to-end is NOT mocked — it orchestrates streamlink, FFmpeg, MediaSoup/LiveKit, the active-streams map, and the real-streamer protection check; testing all of that for one new branch is heavier than the branch is worth. Live smoke test on the running host (operator step) covers the integration. 302/302 overall (+12 new). **Phase 1/2 boundary**: this PR introduces the gate but does NOT yet remove the hardcoded `blockedCategories: ['ASMR', 'Pools, Hot Tubs, and Beaches']` on `RandomStreamRotationService.js:106`; rotation still uses the legacy blocklist. That cutover lands in PR-W3 (Phase 2) once `TwitchRandomService` / `KickRandomService` consult `WhitelistService.filterCandidates()` directly.

- **URL-relay whitelist scaffolding (PR-W1, Phase 0 of ADR-0010).** New `WhitelistService` (`server/services/WhitelistService.js`) is the future single source of truth for the URL-relay content filter — three modes per platform (`off` / `blacklist` / `whitelist`) with optional fallback category + evergreen channel. Three new SQLite tables in `server/database/url-relay-whitelist-schema.sql`: `url_relay_filter_config` (one row per platform: mode + fallback fields), `url_relay_filter_entries` (allow/block streamer logins or category names, unique on `(platform, entry_type, value, list)`), `url_relay_filter_audit` (append-only log of mode changes, entry adds/removes, drift events, fallback engagements). Seed loader populates the tables on first init from `server/data/seeds/url-relay-whitelist.seed.json` — 35 Twitch streamers (Bob Ross 24/7 + Monstercat FM + Chillhop as evergreens) + 20 safe categories, 8 Kick streamers + 13 categories, with risk flags and notes per entry. `WhitelistService.checkAllowed({platform, login, currentGameName, isMature, ccls, hasMatureContent})` returns `{allowed, reason, gateThatBlocked}` and runs CCL/mature-flag gates (Twitch `SexualThemes`/`ViolentGraphic`/`DrugsIntoxication`, Kick `has_mature_content`) **regardless of mode** — those are platform-supplied signals, defense-in-depth against an admin allowlisting something whose labels change later. `filterCandidates(platform, candidates)` is the bulk-filter hook for rotation, `chooseFallback(platform)` returns the fallback configuration for the orchestrator, mutations (`setMode`/`addEntry`/`removeEntry`/`markReviewed`) emit `change` events and write audit rows with `before_json` / `after_json`. In-memory cache invalidates on mutation; stale-cache refresh is non-blocking so a slow disk doesn't block policy checks. Service is wired in `server/index.js` immediately after `SimpleViewBotRotation.setStreamService(streamService)` (the existing branch-shared hoist) and exposed on `app.locals.whitelistService` + `global.whitelistService` per the existing pattern. **Phase 0 only — no caller consults the service yet.** `ViewBotURLService` gate, `TwitchRandomService`/`KickRandomService` candidate filter, and `WhitelistEnforcer` drift checker land in PR-W2–W4. If `URL_RELAY_REQUIRE_WHITELIST_SERVICE=true` is set (planned for Phase 5/PR-W6), initialize failure is fatal; without that flag it's a logged warning so partial rollout stays safe. 30 new tests in `server/tests/WhitelistService.test.js` (in-memory SQLite, no network) cover: schema apply + idempotent re-init; CCL gates fire in `off` mode (`is_mature`, `SexualThemes`, `has_mature_content`); blacklist streamer + category blocks; whitelist allow by streamer OR by category; case-insensitive login match; CCL precedence over whitelist allow; `filterCandidates` end-to-end; `chooseFallback` returns evergreen list; every mutation writes an audit row with the right shape; cache invalidates within a single `checkAllowed` cycle after `setMode`; validation rejects unknown platforms/modes/empty value; seed loads the expected `bobross` evergreen and `mustafa_go` Kick allow entry. 288/288 overall (+30 new). **Schema parser fix**: the inherited split-on-`;` SQL parser (mirrored from `URLStreamDatabaseService._initializeSchema`) was filtering out CREATE statements that had leading `-- comment` lines because `s.startsWith('--')` was true after split-trim; the new implementation strips line comments per-line before checking emptiness, which is the actual robust behavior every other schema file in this repo was relying on by accident. **Documentation**: ADR-0010 (`docs/architecture/adr/0010-url-relay-whitelist-mode.md`, accepted), implementation plan (`docs/architecture/plans/url-relay-whitelist-mode.md`, 6 phases mapped to 6 PRs), operations runbook (`docs/operations/runbooks/url-relay-whitelist.md` — add/remove entries, fallback diagnostics, 90-day re-review query, force-stop incident response). **Known follow-up scope**: the parallel hardcoded `blockedCategories: ['ASMR', 'Pools, Hot Tubs, and Beaches']` on `RandomStreamRotationService.js:106` (and the duplicated filter inside `TwitchRandomService.findRandomStreamer:253` + `KickRandomService.findRandomStreamer:170`) are LEFT IN PLACE this PR; PR-W3 (Phase 2) deletes them after the rotation service starts consulting `WhitelistService` instead.

- **`ViewerCountNotifier` collapses 13 `viewer-count-update` emit sites into one chokepoint (PR 3.2).** Second PR of Phase 3, following the same chokepoint pattern as PR 3.1's `StreamNotifier` but with smaller blast radius and a slightly different shape. The 13 pre-existing emit sites were all **literally identical**: `io.emit('viewer-count-update', sessionService.getUniqueViewerCount())`. No payload variations, no `extras`, no per-site fields — the only thing varying was the file/line. New [`server/services/ViewerCountNotifier.js`](server/services/ViewerCountNotifier.js) owns both the emit AND the count derivation; callers now just write `viewerCountNotifier.broadcast()` and the notifier reads `sessionService.getUniqueViewerCount()` internally. The headline benefit beyond deduplication: the previous pattern forced every callsite to remember the right helper — `sessionService.getUniqueViewerCount()` (canonical unique-IP count) vs. `streamService.getViewerCount()` (raw socket-id count, multi-tab counts twice) was always one autocomplete away from a wrong-helper bug; with the chokepoint owning the lookup, that wrong choice is no longer available at the callsite. **Construction**: `new ViewerCountNotifier(io, sessionService)` — both args required (constructor throws otherwise). Wired in [`server/bootstrap/services.js`](server/bootstrap/services.js) immediately after `streamNotifier`; `expectedKeys` bumps 36 → 37. **Threading**: `StreamHandler` (3 sites at `:163`, `:709`, `:803`), `MediaSoupHandler` (2 sites at `:355`, `:385`), and `server/index.js` (8 sites — `:1945`, `:1979`, `:2023`, `:2059`, `:2087`, `:2793`, `:4908`, `:5127`) all get the notifier via their existing `deps` bag / module-scope destructure; no new construction order constraints because all 13 sites already had access to both `io` and `sessionService`. **Behaviour preservation**: wire format byte-equivalent — same event name `'viewer-count-update'`, same payload (single integer = `sessionService.getUniqueViewerCount()`'s return value), same per-emit freshness contract (the test pins "re-reads count on each broadcast" so a future `setInterval`-driven cache that staleness-shifts emits won't slip in silently). Zero is passed through deliberately (a "skip if zero" optimisation would create stuck-counter bugs on full-viewer-departure). **Tests** (`server/tests/services/ViewerCountNotifier.test.js` — 6 new tests): ctor throws on missing io OR missing sessionService; broadcast() reads the helper once and emits with the value; back-to-back broadcasts re-read (no caching); zero is emitted, not skipped. Bootstrap test (`server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js`) updated to mock + identity-pin `ViewerCountNotifier` ctor `(io, sessionService)` and bump `expectedKeys` to 37. 476/476 (was 469; +6 new + 1 bootstrap identity). **Scope deferred**: a future PR could expose an event-driven model where `sessionService` emits "viewer-count-changed" and the notifier subscribes — that would eliminate the remaining "remember to call broadcast()" coupling at the 13 callsites. Postponed because it's a bigger contract change (sessionService would need an EventEmitter base) and the chokepoint pattern is enough to unblock the next steps. **Next**: PR 3.3 (BuffService.update() chokepoint for streamer-buffs-update / inventory-updated / buff-error, 28 sites split between BuffDebuffService and inline route handlers).

- **`StreamNotifier` collapses 17 `stream-ended` emit sites into one chokepoint (PR 3.1).** First PR of Phase 3 ("state unification + typed socket facade"). The fragmentation hit-list in [`docs/architecture/socket-events-actual.md`](docs/architecture/socket-events-actual.md) names `stream-ended` as the headline target. Counted precisely: **17 emit sites across 8 files** — 16 `io.emit('stream-ended', …)` calls plus 1 `socket.broadcast.emit('stream-ended', …)` for the takeover variant in `StreamHandler.js:414` (which deliberately EXCLUDES the new streamer's own socket so its UI doesn't process its own stream as "ended"). New [`server/services/StreamNotifier.js`](server/services/StreamNotifier.js) is a thin façade — one method `streamEnded({ reason, excludeSocket, ...extras })` that funnels through a single `io.emit` (or `excludeSocket.broadcast.emit` when the takeover semantic is requested). Constructed in [`server/bootstrap/services.js`](server/bootstrap/services.js) with `(io)` as its only dep. The 17 callsites are converted: `server/sockets/StreamHandler.js:414` (takeover, via `excludeSocket`), `:792` (`user_stopped_streaming`); `server/sockets/ViewBotHandler.js:385` (`stop_stream_request`); 7 sites in `server/index.js` (admin/test/disconnect/ban paths — reasons `viewbot_stopped`, `viewbot_legacy_stopped`, `test_stream_stopped`, `admin_clear`, `admin_disconnect`, `streamer_banned`, `streamer_disconnected`); `server/services/ViewBotURLService.js:1236` (dynamic `url_stream_${inner}`), `:1448` (`url_stream_stopped`); `server/services/LiveKitService.js:659` (`webrtc_disconnect`); `server/services/ViewBotRotationService.js:286` (`rotation` — also drops the `global.io` access, which was the ugliest of the 17 sites); `server/services/RandomStreamRotationService.js:873` (`random_rotation_starting`), `:962` (`random_rotation_stopped`); `server/services/WebRTCViewBotRotation.js:206` — previously emitted **with no `reason` field**, so it silently fell through every client `useStreamState.ts:318` branch into the catch-all "normal stream end" path even mid-rotation; now tagged `webrtc_viewbot_stopped` and added to `REASONS`. **Threading**: `StreamHandler` and `ViewBotHandler` take it in their existing `deps` bag (passed from the `registerStreamHandler`/`registerViewBotHandler` callsites at `server/index.js:4742, 4806`). For the four services historically wired via setter or `global.io` (`ViewBotURLService`, `RandomStreamRotationService`, `LiveKitService`, `ViewBotRotationService`), a parallel `setStreamNotifier(notifier)` setter is added — preserves the existing post-construction wiring pattern. `WebRTCViewBotRotation` accepts the notifier as a 3rd ctor arg; `UnifiedViewBotRotation` (the sole caller) threads it through. `LiveKitService` is constructed inside `WebRTCAdapter` before the bootstrap factory runs, so its setter is wired post-construction in `server/index.js` immediately after services are built. **Reason-string surface pinning**: `StreamNotifier.REASONS` is a Set containing the 20 reason strings produced by the 17 baseline sites (the 16 distinct reasons plus the 4-way fan-out of `url_stream_${reason}` from `_handleStreamEnd`'s inner values `source_ended` / `http_error` / `reconnect_failed` / `error`). At runtime, an unknown reason still emits — typo doesn't silently swallow the event — but logs a structured `console.warn` so monitoring catches surface drift. A missing reason DOES suppress the emit (malformed payload reaching the client is worse than no event: the client's reason-discrimination branches all fall through to "normal stream end" on absent reason). **Tests** (`server/tests/services/StreamNotifier.test.js` — 32 new tests): constructor requires `io`; `REASONS` contains every Phase 3 baseline reason (one `test.each` per reason — both deletion AND addition without baseline update fail loud, because the strict-equality size check at the end of the `REASONS` describe block forces a baseline edit on any extension); known-reason emit produces correct payload with all extras passed through; unknown reason emits + warns; missing/no-args call suppresses + warns; `excludeSocket` routes through `socket.broadcast.emit` and strips the control field from the wire payload. Bootstrap test (`server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js`) updated to mock + identity-pin `StreamNotifier` and bump `expectedKeys` from 35 → 36 (one new identity test added). **Behaviour preservation** — the wire format is byte-equivalent: same event name, same payload shape for every reason; the `excludeSocket` branch preserves the `socket.broadcast.emit` semantic bit-for-bit. The single payload *addition* is the `reason: 'webrtc_viewbot_stopped'` field on the WebRTCViewBotRotation emit (previously absent) — clients that ignore the field see no change. **MediaSoup-branch suppression (post-review fix)** — the original MediaSoup branch at `server/index.js:5212-5215` (pre-PR) did NOT call `viewBotURLService.setSocketIO(io)`, only the LiveKit branch did. With `this.io` undefined, the two URL-stream emits at `ViewBotURLService.js:1236, 1448` were suppressed by `if (this.io)` in MediaSoup-mode production. The reviewer flagged that an earlier draft of this PR called `setStreamNotifier(streamNotifier)` on the MediaSoup branch — which would have silently activated those two previously-dormant emits. Fixed by deliberately omitting the setter on the MediaSoup branch (commented inline at the same site); the `if (this.streamNotifier)` guard now mirrors the original `if (this.io)` suppression. **Scope deferred to follow-up PRs**: (a) `streamGeneration` counter on `stream-ended` payloads — PR 2.5's counter applies to `stream-status` only; threading it onto `stream-ended` is a one-line addition inside the notifier paired with a client-side drop-by-counter, postponed to keep this PR scoped. (b) Collapsing `setStreamNotifier` setters into proper ctor args once Phase 4's `server/index.js` decomposition lets the construction order put the notifier ahead of `ViewBotURLService` etc. (c) PR 3.2 (same pattern for `viewer-count-update` — 13 sites), PR 3.3 (`BuffService.update()` chokepoint for `streamer-buffs-update` / `inventory-updated` / `buff-error` — 28 sites across `BuffDebuffService` and inline route handlers in `server/routes/items.js` + `server/routes/buffs.js`). New ADR [ADR-0009](docs/architecture/adr/0009-stream-notifier-chokepoint.md) records the decision and the receivers' reason-discrimination contract at `client/src/hooks/useStreamState.ts:318` (`takeover`, `random_rotation_*`, `url_stream_*` prefix, `webrtc_disconnect`).

### Fixed
- **Random-stream rotation settings persist when changed from the admin UI.** `RandomStreamRotationService.updateSettings()` (`server/services/RandomStreamRotationService.js:1952`) merged new values into `this.settings` and mirrored them onto the inner Twitch/Kick services, but never called `_saveState()` — only `start()` (:712) and `stop()` (:917) wrote `server/data/random-rotation-state.json`. So any change made via `PUT /api/random-stream/settings` (the admin panel) was lost on the next `pm2 restart`: the constructor's `_loadState()` read the file (which still held whatever value was current the last time someone toggled the rotation) and silently reverted the change. Concrete repro: set `minViewers=499` in the UI, observe `👁️ Viewer range set: 499 – 999999` in the log, restart, find `minViewers` back at the previously-persisted value (and the UI now also shows that older value). Fix is a single `this._saveState()` call at the end of `updateSettings()` so every UI write is durable. `_saveState()` already wraps in try/catch, so a transient disk error is logged but doesn't break the in-memory update path. New tests in `server/tests/services/RandomStreamRotationService.test.js` (2 tests): `updateSettings({minViewers: 499, maxViewers: 123456})` writes both fields into the on-disk state file; a fresh service instance loaded after a separate `updateSettings({minViewers: 777})` picks up `777` from disk without `start()` being called.
- **Recording cleanup no longer races B2 upload (PR 2.6).** Closes the documented hazard in `docs/architecture/background-work.md` "Notable hazards". `ContinuousRecordingService.cleanupOldRecordings()` (the body at :1378, fired by the 60-second interval at :1368) used to unconditionally `fs.rmSync` any `session_<timestamp>` directory older than `retentionMinutes` (= 10 min stock — `bootstrap/services.js:210`). `RecordingUploadScheduler.localBufferHours` waits 2 h after `end_time` before queueing the upload (`RecordingUploadScheduler.js:15`), and the upload's success path is the only thing that sets `b2_file_id` (:178). If the cleanup ever matched a session whose upload hadn't yet completed, it would nuke the local files 110 min before the upload fired; the upload then fails at :147 with "Local recording not found", retries every 30 min against a missing path, and the row sits at `status = 'completed'` / `b2_file_id = NULL` forever — recording permanently lost. **Live-exposure note**: the current production session-id generator at :818 produces `recording_<YYYY-MM-DD>` (date-based; one session per day), which does NOT match the cleanup regex `/session_(\d+)/` or the `.startsWith('session_')` guard — so in today's running system the cleanup loop is effectively a no-op and the race hasn't been actively destroying recordings. The fix is preemptive: the existing `extractSessionIdFromEgress` path at :940-942 hints that the per-session naming format can re-converge, and the loop-as-written is one config flip or one refactor away from the live failure mode. **Fix**: at the top of `cleanupOldRecordings()`, preload the set of session_ids that have NOT yet been uploaded (`SELECT session_id FROM recording_sessions WHERE b2_file_id IS NULL` — same predicate the upload scheduler queries at `RecordingUploadScheduler.js:52`), and skip those directories in the loop. Covers both `status='completed'` (pending) and `status='processing'` (in flight) since both have `b2_file_id IS NULL` until the upload sets it. The single-file `room_<ts>.mp4` / `.json` branch is left untouched: grep confirms no current code path produces matching filenames (egress writes `playlist_<ts>.m3u8` and `seg_<ts>_<idx>.ts` inside session directories, never `room_*` at the output-dir root), so the legacy cleanup is harmless dead code with no `recording_sessions` row to gate against. Cleanup is now async (the DB lookup needs await); the `setInterval` callback at :1368 fires-and-forgets the promise, which is the correct shape for a periodic cleanup. **Fail-closed**: if the DB query itself throws (e.g. `SQLITE_BUSY` under heavy write contention), the cleanup aborts the tick without deleting anything and the next tick retries — better to delay cleanup than to race-delete an unconfirmed upload's source. 7 new tests in `server/tests/services/ContinuousRecordingService.cleanup-race.test.js`: (1) headline — pending session_id stays on disk, (2) uploaded session_id is deleted, (3) mixed-batch discrimination (4 sessions, 2 of each), (4) retention cutoff still respected for uploaded sessions, (5) currently-active session is skipped, (6) orphan directory (no DB row) falls through to deletion (intentional — alternative would be a slow-motion disk-fill bug), (7) fail-closed on DB error. DB and `fs` operations are mocked at the module-require level (same pattern as PR 2.1's `AccountService.points-race.test.js`); no fake timers because the production race is between two scheduled intervals, not microtask interleaving inside one method. 206/206 (was 199; +7). **Known follow-up scope**: (a) the parallel `RecordingCleanupScheduler.js` (B2/DB row deletion) has the same gap and needs its own gate against `b2_file_name IS NULL`; (b) the upload scheduler's `loadPendingUploads` (:50-54) queries only `status='completed'` — a server crash mid-upload leaves rows orphaned at `status='processing' AND b2_file_id IS NULL`, which the cleanup now also (correctly) skips, but with no escape hatch they sit on disk forever; (c) currently no metric/alarm when `skippedPendingUpload > 0` for many consecutive ticks (a real B2 outage would silently fill disk). These each warrant a separate PR.
- **Kick random-stream picker honours `minViewers` again.** `server/services/kick-api-helper.py` now requests `https://kick.com/stream/livestreams/<lang>?…&sort=desc` — without `sort=desc`, that endpoint returns `viewer_count: 0` for every entry, so the helper was feeding the picker a list of fake-zero streams. `KickRandomService.findRandomStreamer` had been papering over this with a `if (minViewers > 1 && viewers < minViewers) return false;` guard that turned the viewer-count filter off at the default `minViewers: 1`; the moment an operator raised the threshold (e.g. 1 → 499) every Kick stream was filtered out and rotation recovery logged `⚠️ No suitable Kick streams found after filtering`. With real counts now coming back, the filter collapses to the obvious `viewers < minViewers || viewers > maxViewers` form. With `sort=desc`, page N covers a contiguous viewer-count band (page 1: ~6k–46k, page 3: ~3k–4.7k, page 5: ~1.6k–2k, page 10: ~700–830, page 20: ~330–345), so the existing random-page-1-through-5 sweep still surfaces a healthy range without hitting the long tail. Test coverage in `server/tests/services/KickRandomService.test.js` pins: streams below `minViewers` are dropped when `minViewers > 1`; zero-viewer streams are dropped at `minViewers === 1`; streams above `maxViewers` are dropped; an all-too-low list returns `null`.
- **URL-stream relay for Twitch no longer fails when popular streams are picked.** `server/services/URLStreamExtractorService.js` `getStreamURL()` now resolves Twitch URLs to a direct HLS m3u8 via `yt-dlp -g` and returns `{pipeMode: false, isHLS: true}`, so FFmpeg consumes the playlist directly (same code path Kick already uses). Previously Twitch fell into the streamlink pipe, and streamlink 6.6.2's `plugins/twitch.py` hardcodes `headless=False` when acquiring its client-integrity token — which means it launches Chromium with a real window and polls `http://127.0.0.1:<port>/json/version`. On this headless host there is no `DISPLAY`, Chromium dies with "Missing X server or $DISPLAY", and streamlink exits with `error: Unable to open URL: …/json/version`, which bubbled up as repeated `FFmpeg exited early with code 183` in the rotation logs. The integrity-token requirement is enforced more aggressively on high-viewer Twitch channels, so raising `minViewers` (e.g. 1 → 499) made the failure mode constant instead of intermittent. Test coverage in `server/tests/services/URLStreamExtractorService.test.js` pins: yt-dlp is invoked for Twitch and the result is `tool: 'yt-dlp', pipeMode: false, isHLS: true`; YouTube/Kick/Facebook continue to use streamlink pipe mode; direct `.m3u8` URLs still bypass both extractors unchanged.

### Added
- **Client adopts `streamGeneration` + deletion of the 10-second takeover lock (PR 2.5b — pair to PR 2.5).** Server-side seam from PR 2.5 (`StreamService.streamGeneration` counter, bumped on every `setStreamer` / `clearStreamer`, included in every `stream-status` payload via `getStreamStatus()`) is now consumed on the client, and the wall-clock-window lock that PR 2.5 was structurally replacing is deleted. New `client/src/hooks/useStreamGenerationGuard.ts` (custom hook) tracks the highest-seen counter on a `useRef` (initial −1 so the server's first emit at 0 is accepted), and exposes a memoized `acceptStreamStatus(incoming)` predicate that returns `false` (and the caller drops the payload) when `incoming < lastSeen`. Equal counters are accepted (same generation, fresh viewer-count / display-name resolution). Payloads with no `streamGeneration` field — older servers, or partial emit sites that don't yet thread the counter — are accepted unconditionally (back-compat: can't reason about ordering without the counter, safer to apply than to silently drop). The guard also subscribes to the socket's `connect` event and resets its high-water mark to −1 there: a server restart rewinds `StreamService.streamGeneration` to 0, and without the reset the client would lock itself out of every subsequent `stream-status` forever. `App.tsx`'s `stream-status` listener is rewritten: the 10-second `takeoverTargetRef` / `takeoverTimestampRef` lock (lines 272-323 pre-PR), including both the "ignore stale during transition" branch and the "clear lock on match" branch, is replaced by a single `if (!acceptStreamStatus(status.streamGeneration)) return;` guard at the top of the handler. The post-guard body preserves the existing `streamerDisplayName` and rotation-timer fall-through merge so display continuity through transitions is unchanged. `useStreamState` is cleaned up to match: the `takeoverTargetRef` and `takeoverTimestampRef` declarations (`useStreamState.ts:161-162`), interface entries (138-139), all set sites (`stream-ended` takeover branch :316-318, `stream-takeover` :669-670), all clear sites (`stream-started` :281-283, post-transition `setTimeout` :698), and return entries (:745-746) are deleted; the hook's header comment is updated to reflect the new ordering source. `StreamStatus` gains an optional `streamGeneration?: number` field for type safety. The `GameStreamService` symmetry deferred in PR 2.5 is also closed: `streamService` is threaded into the ctor as a 4th positional arg (`server/bootstrap/services.js:236`), and both `startGameStream` and `stopGameStream` emits call `streamService.bumpStreamGeneration()` (new method on `StreamService` — explicit bump for callers that emit stream-status outside the `setStreamer`/`clearStreamer` path; returns the new counter) and include it in their custom payload via spread. The bootstrap test at `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js:410` is updated to assert `_args.length === 4` and `_args[3] === streamService`. **Tests**: 9 new client-side tests in `client/src/hooks/__tests__/useStreamGenerationGuard.test.tsx` covering: first-emit accept, equal-counter accept, strictly-higher advance, strictly-lower drop (the headline), back-compat for missing counter, socket-connect reset (server-restart case), connect-listener unbind on unmount (no leak), stable callback reference across renders (so the App.tsx `useEffect` dep doesn't churn), null-socket tolerance. 3 new server-side tests in `server/tests/services/GameStreamService.streamGeneration.test.js` covering: `startGameStream` bump + payload inclusion, `stopGameStream` bump + payload inclusion, omitted field when `streamService` is absent (back-compat). 1 new test in `server/tests/StreamService.test.js` for `bumpStreamGeneration()` itself. Server: 199/199 (was 195). Client hooks suite: 32/32 (was 23). The pre-existing client test failures in `App.test.tsx`, `MediasoupClient.test.ts`, `WebRTCViewer.test.tsx`, etc. exist on `main` and are not introduced by this PR. **Scope considered but not done in this PR**: the `stream-started` / `stream-ended` / `stream-takeover` payloads in `useStreamState.ts` also drive `setStreamStatus`, and they don't currently carry a `streamGeneration` field — so they sit outside the guard. The headline ordering hazard is the `stream-status` channel (the canonical "current state" message), which is fixed; threading the counter onto the notification-style events is a follow-up if a real-world out-of-order arrival on those channels is observed.
- **`StreamService.streamGeneration` monotonic counter on stream-status emits (server-side seam for PR 2.5).** Per the WebRTC red-team finding, the takeoverTargetRef 10-second lock at `client/src/App.tsx:272-323` is hiding cross-channel ordering between `stream-status` events: the lock papers over stale stream-status events arriving after a takeover. The structurally correct fix is a monotonic generation counter threaded through every stream-status emit so the client can drop out-of-order arrivals by counter. This PR adds the server-side half: `StreamService.streamGeneration` (init 0), incremented in `setStreamer()` and `clearStreamer()` (every stream-identity change), exposed via `getStreamGeneration()` and included in `getStreamStatus()` return. Since the three `stream-status` emit sites in `server/sockets/StreamHandler.js` (lines 104, 518, 628) all build their payload from `streamService.getStreamStatus()` and the `enrichStreamStatus` helper does `{...status}`, the new field rides through automatically with no emit-site changes. Viewer add/remove deliberately does NOT bump the counter — only stream-identity changes do — so the client's drop-by-counter check fires only on stream-state messages, not on viewer-count-only updates that arrived with the same stream context. The factory wiring is unchanged (StreamService takes no deps). 5 new tests in `server/tests/StreamService.test.js` (17/17, up from 12); existing shape `toEqual` test updated to include the new field. 195/195 overall (was 190). **Scope deferred to PR 2.5b**: the client-side drop-by-counter logic at `App.tsx:272-323` + the matching site in `useStreamState.ts` and the deletion of `takeoverTargetRef` / `takeoverTimestampRef` (declarations at `useStreamState.ts:161-162`, return at :745, all set/clear sites at :281-283, :316, :669, :698, plus App.tsx consumer destructure at :189 and dep array at :424). **Also deferred**: `GameStreamService` emits at `services/game/GameStreamService.js:52,93` build their own payload and don't currently include the counter — its game-mode stream uses a constant streamerId (`GAME_STREAM_ID`) so ordering pressure is lower, but PR 2.5b should add the counter for symmetry (which requires threading streamService into the GameStreamService ctor; bootstrap test update needed).
- **Bootstrap fail-fast guard for the service-factory DAG.** Third PR of Phase 2. The existing 33 tests in `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js` each pin one service's ctor args by identity — catches *wrong* wiring. Three new tests catch *missing* wiring: with the full `buildDeps()` bag, no positional ctor arg on any returned service should be `undefined`. The iteration walks every entry in the returned `services` (and `bag`) object, skips entries without `_args` and `null` ViewBot branch slots, then reports a list of `serviceName#argIndex` offenders. With the current factory, the offender list is `[]` — meaning future PRs that add a new service to `createServices` with `new X(deps.zservice)` but forget to add `zservice` to the destructure, or extend an existing service's ctor without threading the new dep, will fail with a useful name-and-index list instead of routes blowing up later when the undefined gets dereferenced at runtime. The check is `!== undefined` (not `!= null`) so deliberate `null` choices — `viewBotClientService` passing `null` as serverUrl for the env-var fallback, the unused LiveKit/MediaSoup branch leaving its `viewBot*Service` null on the bag, `livekitService=null` on the MediaSoup branch — pass through untouched. One guard for the main factory, two for `createViewBotServices` (MediaSoup branch + LiveKit branch, since each path hits a different `new` site). 36/36 in the suite (was 33), 190/190 overall.
- **TakeoverService concurrent-claim coverage.** Second PR of Phase 2. Four new tests under `server/tests/TakeoverService.test.js` close the gap between the existing 15 sequential-happy-path tests and the actual concurrent claim flow at `server/sockets/StreamHandler.js`. (1) `Promise.all` of two `canTakeOver()` calls with no `recordTakeover` between them returns `allowed=true` for both — pins down that TakeoverService is intentionally non-reserving so a future refactor doesn't silently start serializing here and mask the caller-layer gap PR 2.5 actually fixes with a monotonic `streamGeneration` counter on stream-status emits. (2) After `recordTakeover()`, three concurrent `canTakeOver()` calls all return `denied`/`global_cooldown`/`cooldownRemaining>0` — proves there is no stale-read window inside `canTakeOver`; will fail if anyone defers the in-memory `lastStreamStartTime` write past an `await`. (3) Per-identifier cooldown isolation: `setIpCooldown('alice', 'stream_taken_over')` does not block Bob's claim, but Alice herself sees `individual_cooldown` with `cooldownRemaining ≤ 60`. (4) Boundary test of the `(now - lastStreamStartTime) < globalCooldownMs` comparison: `lastStreamStartTime` 5 s ago → denied, 31 s ago → allowed. Tests target `globalCooldownSeconds`/`individualCooldownSeconds` directly (the live properties `canTakeOver` reads) rather than `setCooldownSeconds()` (the legacy field, which the existing "no-arg constructor leaves cooldownSeconds unset" test already pins). 19/19 in the suite, 187/187 overall.
- **Failing test documents the points-balance lost-update race.** First PR of Phase 2. New `server/tests/services/AccountService.points-race.test.js` proves the long-standing read-compute-write defect in `AccountService.addPoints` / `subtractPoints`: each method does `await getUserStats` → JS arithmetic → `UPDATE user_stats SET points_balance = ?` with the absolute new value, so two concurrent callers both read the same balance, both compute, both write — second write overwrites the first. The headline test fires 20 concurrent `addPoints(userId, 5, …)` calls and asserts the final balance is **strictly less than** the expected 100; it passes today (bug is live) and will fail when Phase 5 lands the atomic `UPDATE user_stats SET points_balance = points_balance + ? … RETURNING points_balance` fix — at which point the same diff flips the assertion to `toBe(100)`. A control test using sequential awaits asserts `toBe(100)` to prove the bug is the race itself, not the arithmetic. `subtractPoints` gets the same treatment. DB layer is mocked with an in-memory map + `Promise.resolve()` microtask yields between read and write; that's enough to expose the race in Node's single-threaded model and faithfully mirrors what real sqlite3 (which yields on I/O) does today. All 183 existing tests still pass.
- **`BotEventBus` decouples ChatBot ↔ MovieBot.** Third step of Phase 1. New `server/services/BotEventBus.js` (a thin `EventEmitter` wrapper with a `stop()` lifecycle hook) is constructed once in the factory and injected into both `ChatBotService` (constructor arg `{ botEventBus, getMoviePromptTemplate }`) and `MovieBotService` (5th positional arg). ChatBot now emits `chat-message` events on the bus instead of calling `movieBotService.addChatMessage(...)` directly; MovieBot subscribes in its existing `setupChatListener()` (handler captured on `this._onBusChatMessage` so a future `stop()` can `removeListener` cleanly). The post-construction setter `chatBotService.setMovieBotService(movieBotService)` was deleted from both the factory and the class — its only purpose was wiring the now-unnecessary cross-reference. The one other cross-service read (`createTemporaryBot` reads `movieBotService.config.moviePromptTemplate` — admin-editable, normally populated from the DB) is preserved via a factory-built closure (`getMoviePromptTemplate`) that lazily resolves `movieBotService.config.moviePromptTemplate` at call time. Forward-declared with `let movieBotService` so the closure captures by reference; the construction-time circular dep is broken without losing the runtime config read. `MovieBot → ChatBot` direction is unchanged: that direction is request/response (`generateMovieComment`, `getMovieBotEnabledBots`, `llmService` config) and contorting it through a bus would be ceremony. Also fixed in the same PR: PR 1.2 changed `createServices`/`createViewBotServices` to return `{ services, stoppables }` but didn't update `server/tests/bootstrap/services.test.js`; 20+ test callsites are migrated to `const { services: s } = createServices(...)`, the deleted `setMovieBotService` test is replaced with bus-wiring tests that assert both services hold the same bus instance and that `emit('chat-message')` reaches subscribers, and `services.test.js` `expectedKeys` array adds `'botEventBus'` (35 keys, was 34). All 33 tests pass.
- **Graceful-shutdown iteration over a `stoppables` registry.** Second step of Phase 1: `server/bootstrap/services.js`'s `createServices()` and `createViewBotServices()` now return `{ services, stoppables }`. `stoppables` is a list of services that actually expose `stop()` today (the four bot/effect services with leaked anonymous intervals — `visualFxService`, `chatBotService`, `movieBotService`, `transcriptionService`, plus `viewBotLiveKitService` — are deferred to later PRs that add real `stop()` rather than no-op fallbacks). `server/index.js` aggregates them: core stoppables from the factory + livekit (when on the LiveKit branch) + viewbot stoppables + two more inline-constructed services (`viewBotManager`, `portMonitor`). livekit is pushed *before* the viewbot stoppables so reverse-iteration stops viewbot-consumers before the underlying livekit client. The graceful-shutdown work is extracted into a single `shutdown(signal)` function that **both** `SIGINT` and `SIGTERM` call directly — the previous `process.emit('SIGINT')` from SIGTERM was fire-and-forget and never awaited the async handler, which made systemd / Docker shutdowns silently skip the cleanup work. Each `svc.stop()` runs as an async IIFE (catches sync throws) against a per-iteration cancelable timeout (no leaked unhandled rejections on fast successes). The existing inline cleanup block stays in place as belt-and-braces — a follow-up PR prunes entries that overlap with stoppables once the iterator is proven in production. `cleanupMediaProcesses()` (the `uncaughtException` emergency `pkill` path) is unchanged.
- **Uniform `async stop()` lifecycle method on 12 services.** First step of Phase 1 of the refactor (background-work lifecycle discipline). Each service in [`docs/architecture/background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) "Owned" table now exposes an `async stop()` method. Sets up the next PR (factory returns a `stoppables` array; SIGTERM iterates) to dispatch through one method name across the whole service graph.
  - Ten services received a delegating alias to an existing teardown method (`ResourceMonitor`→`stopMonitoring`, `AudioOptimizationService`→`stopMonitoring`, `PortMonitorService`→`stopMonitoring`, `TimeTrackingService`→`stopPeriodicCleanup`, `LiveKitService`→`stopStreamerHealthCheck`, `BuffDebuffService`→`shutdown`, `CanvasFxService`→`shutdown`, `ContinuousRecordingService`→`shutdown`, `ViewBotManager`→`cleanup`, `ViewbotService`→`cleanup`, `ViewBotClientService`→`cleanup`).
  - Two services received fresh bodies: `StreamBotService.stop()` calls both `stopPeriodicMessages` and `stopAutoSummon`.
  - **Fixed two pre-existing leaks while wiring the entry points**: `BuffDebuffService.startCacheCleanup()` was storing the cache-cleanup interval handle anonymously, so `shutdown()` only cleared one of its two intervals — handle now stored as `this.cacheCleanupInterval` and cleared in `shutdown()`. `TimeTrackingService.stopPeriodicCleanup()` referenced `this.realTimeUpdateIntervals.entries()` but the attribute initialized in the constructor is named `this.updateIntervals` — that meant per-user interval cleanup was silently throwing on every call. Renamed to the actual attribute name.
  - **Scope caveat for PR 1.2**: three of the twelve services (`ViewBotManager`, `PortMonitorService`, `LiveKitService`) are constructed *outside* `bootstrap/services.js` today — `ViewBotManager` in `server/index.js:5461` and `WebRTCViewBotRotation.js:51`; `PortMonitorService` in `server/index.js:5498`; `LiveKitService` in `WebRTCAdapter.js` / `WebRTCAdapterV2.js`. PR 1.2's `stoppables` iterator needs to collect these alongside the factory-built bag.
  - **`ViewBotClientService.cleanup()` pre-existing footgun** (called transitively via the new `stop()` alias on SIGTERM): `pkill -f "puppeteer.*chrome"` is unscoped and would kill Puppeteer processes belonging to other projects on the same host. Not introduced by this PR; flagged for tightening as a Phase 1 follow-up (track launched browser PIDs in `activeBots`, kill those specifically).
- **Inventory artifacts under `docs/architecture/`.** Three new reference files captured at the start of the refactor:
  - [`schema-actual.sql`](docs/architecture/schema-actual.sql) — live `.schema` dump from the production 2 GB+ DB; baseline for the Phase 5 migration framework.
  - [`background-work.md`](docs/architecture/background-work.md) — every `setInterval` / `setTimeout` / child-process site with lifecycle status (handle-on-instance vs leaked), grouped by severity. Crucial for the Phase 2 lifecycle work.
  - [`socket-events-actual.md`](docs/architecture/socket-events-actual.md) — mechanical site-level surface of socket events, complementing the feature-grouped `realtime-events.md`. Names the Phase 3 hotspots (e.g. `stream-ended` emitted from 16 sites across 9 files).
- **Structured logging (pino).** New `server/bootstrap/logger.js` exports a shared pino instance: JSON-to-stdout in production (consumable by log aggregators) and `pino-pretty` colored output in development. `LOG_LEVEL` env var overrides the level; defaults are `info` in production, `debug` in development. Converted the noisiest startup sites: `server/index.js` env-check banner, `server/database/database.js` connect + PRAGMA logs, `server/database/applyPragmas.js` WAL-fallback warning, `server/routes/bug-reports.js` connection errors. The rest of the codebase still uses `console.*` and migrates opportunistically — this PR establishes the pattern without sweeping every file.
- **Fail-fast env validation at startup.** New `server/bootstrap/env.js` aggregates checks for the four secrets `.env.example` marks REQUIRED (`JWT_SECRET`, `SESSION_SECRET`, `TURN_SECRET`, `TURNSTILE_SECRET_KEY`) — both presence and a minimum-length floor where it applies — and throws a single error listing every missing/malformed var. Wired into `server/index.js` immediately after `dotenv.config()` and before any other `require()` that imports a file calling `requireEnv()`. Operators now see all env problems in one error instead of the previous "fix one, restart, see next miss, repeat" loop with `requireEnv()`. Existing `requireEnv()` callsites stay as a secondary safety net for any required var added to a route file but not yet added to `bootstrap/env.js`'s schema. `ADMIN_KEY` is deliberately not in the schema — it's documented as a legacy key without a length requirement; its existing `requireEnv` enforces presence.

### Removed
- **Legacy `user_stats.points` column dropped.** The migration to `points_balance` as the authoritative column (originally executed by `server/migrations/migrate-points-system.js`) has been complete for some time, and a grep across the codebase confirmed the `points` column was no longer read on any write or read path. Removed from the `CREATE TABLE` definition in `server/database/database.js`; the prior `ALTER TABLE user_stats ADD COLUMN points` migration block was replaced with an idempotent `ALTER TABLE user_stats DROP COLUMN points` (guarded by `"no such column"` for second-run safety). The `/api/auth/me` endpoint that serves `stats.points` to the client already overrode that field with `points_balance` (`routes/auth.js:285–288`), so the API contract is unchanged — `UserProfile.tsx` continues to display the authoritative balance. The standalone `migrate-points-system.js` historical script gained an at-start guard that detects the column-gone state and exits cleanly (preserved for forensic value but no longer re-runnable). `docs/architecture/data-model.md` updated to remove the legacy column from the documented schema.

### Changed
- **SQLite tuned for the 2 GB+ live DB.** New `server/database/applyPragmas.js` helper applies the project-wide PRAGMA set on every handle that opens `onestreamer.db`: `journal_mode=WAL` (with verification — silent fallback no longer leaves `synchronous=NORMAL` on a rollback journal, a power-loss corruption hazard), `synchronous=NORMAL` (conditional on WAL being active), `foreign_keys=ON`, `busy_timeout=5000`, plus large-read tunings (`temp_store=MEMORY`, `mmap_size=256 MB`, `cache_size=64 MB`) on the main handle. Before this change: live DB was on `delete` journal + `synchronous=FULL`, and the two auxiliary handles (`routes/bug-reports.js`, `services/URLStreamDatabaseService.js`) opened with no PRAGMAs at all — so writes from those handles were silently running with `foreign_keys=OFF` and `busy_timeout=0`, a pre-existing correctness regression that WAL would have made more visible (`SQLITE_BUSY` on collision). The pre-existing `sqlite3 ... ".backup"` in `docs/operations/backup-restore.md` is already WAL-safe; the inline comment there explicitly anticipated this. Takes effect on the next `pm2 restart onestreamer-server`.
- **Viewbot URL-stream encoder defaults retuned for lower CPU.** `ViewBotURLService` `adaptiveConfig.mode` default flipped from `'balanced'` to `'performance'` (maps to x264 `ultrafast` + 0.7× bitrate multiplier in `AdaptiveEncodingSettings`). The fixed-fallback path (which fires only on probe failure) was aligned: `superfast`/4000k/4500k/6000k → `ultrafast`/2000k/2500k/4000k. Adaptive remains the hot path. Observed: per-bot ffmpeg CPU dropped from ~90% to ~67% of a single core on a Kick HLS source at 720p30.
- **`onestreamer-client` PM2 entry removed** from `config/ecosystem.config.js`. The entry ran `react-scripts start` (CRA dev server) in "production" and was crash-looping (59 restarts in PM2). nginx already serves the built SPA from `/var/www/html` and never proxied to `127.0.0.1:3443`. Recovers ~1.2 GB RAM. Rollback: restore the entry and `pm2 start config/ecosystem.config.js --only onestreamer-client`.
- **CLAUDE.md** and **docs/architecture/overview.md** inline references to "LiveKit dormant" updated to point at [ADR-0008](docs/architecture/adr/0008-revive-livekit-for-url-streams-and-recording.md). The ADR landed but these inline mentions were missed.

### Added
- **`LIVEKIT_INGRESS_BYPASS_TRANSCODING` env var (default off)** in `ViewBotLiveKitService.createIngress`. When `true`, calls `createIngress` with `bypassTranscoding: true` and no `encodingOptions`, allowing LiveKit ingress to pass upstream H.264/AAC through unchanged (skips ~60% CPU of re-transcoding per active ingress). The team's prior "RTMP requires transcoding for WebRTC conversion, can't bypass" comment is preserved as context; flag exists so the claim can be re-validated on the current `livekit-server-sdk` version. **Requires device-QA (desktop Chrome + mobile Safari) before flipping in production** — mismatched SDP/keyframe interval can cause subscriber-side black streams.
- **`VIEWBOT_STREAM_COPY` env var (default off)** in `ViewBotURLService._createFFmpegRTMPProcess`. When `true` and the input is a direct URL (most IVS/Kick/Twitch HLS sources are H.264 + AAC already), uses `-c:v copy -c:a copy -bsf:v h264_mp4toannexb` instead of x264 re-encoding (~70% CPU off the viewbot ffmpeg). **Same QA requirement**; silent failure modes exist if a platform changes its encoder.

### Fixed
- **Admin Connections tab no longer hangs.** The `/admin/connections` handler in `server/index.js` tried to instantiate `new AccountService()`, but that class is never imported in the file — only the bootstrap-built `accountService` instance (destructured at module scope). The synchronous `ReferenceError` was thrown inside an async handler, which Express 4 leaves un-responded; clients hung until their own timeout. Removed the shadow; the outer-scope `accountService` is reused.
- **Admin Recording Review tab no longer hangs.** The `/admin/review/timeline` handler ran `SELECT * FROM recording_stream_segments` with no time filter (28,931 rows) and then did **one or two follow-up DB queries per segment** for display-name lookups. Response could exceed 20 MB and many seconds. Added a `?days=N` window filter (defaults to 30) and batched the per-segment lookups into a single `WHERE source_url IN (…)` + a single channel-ID `LIKE` per IVS channel + a single `streaming_logs` `WHERE streamer_id IN (…)`. Same data shape returned; timeline at `days=30` now responds in ~0.9 s with 3.3 MB.
- **URL-stream relay (Twitch/Kick) produces video again.** Operational fix; see ADR-0008 below. Verified end-to-end: FFmpeg → RTMP → `livekit-ingress` → LiveKit room → transcription / recording / MovieBot replies.

### Changed
- **LiveKit revived as the active WebRTC backend.** See [ADR-0008](docs/architecture/adr/0008-revive-livekit-for-url-streams-and-recording.md). Supersedes ADR-0002 (LiveKit dormant) and pauses ADR-0007's staged cleanup. URL-stream relay (Twitch/Kick), continuous recording (LiveKit Egress), and MovieBot transcription all depend on LiveKit being live; ADR-0002's "dormant" framing did not match the running system. The shipped LiveKit triad (livekit-server systemd unit + livekit-ingress + livekit-egress containers) is now load-bearing; rollback procedure documented in the ADR.
- **`config/livekit-config.example.yaml`** updated with: mandatory `redis:` section (without which `createIngress` fails), and `bind_addresses` containing both `127.0.0.1` and `::1` (the shipped nginx vhost proxies `/livekit/*` to `[::1]:7882`, so IPv4-only binds return 502). Documentation comment block rewritten to match ADR-0008 instead of ADR-0002.

### Added
- New runbook [`docs/operations/runbooks/livekit-ingress-not-connected.md`](docs/operations/runbooks/livekit-ingress-not-connected.md) covering the most distinctive failure modes encountered during the May 2026 LiveKit revival: missing `redis:` section, IPv4-only bind, stopped ingress/egress containers, stale Redis registry, and downed Redis itself.
- New [ADR-0008](docs/architecture/adr/0008-revive-livekit-for-url-streams-and-recording.md) documenting the LiveKit revival, supersession of ADR-0002/0007, and rollback procedure.

### Removed
- **All references to a phantom "~333 ms A/V sync offset"** across `README.md`, `docs/architecture/streaming-stack.md` (warning banner and limits-table row), `docs/features/streaming-and-takeover.md` (warning banner), `docs/getting-started/first-stream.md` (test step), and `CHANGELOG.md` (Verified entry). The ~333 ms claim was not borne out in practice — viewers don't observe a perceptible offset; the original `AV_SYNC_IMPLEMENTATION_COMPLETE.md` (now in `/docs/archive/av-sync/`) was inherited as documentation without re-verification. The archive directory itself is preserved for forensic value.

## [Documentation overhaul 2026-05-23]

### Added
- **Documentation overhaul.** Comprehensive `/docs/` tree organized by audience (getting-started, operations, features, architecture, integrations, api, contributing, security, archive). 70 markdown files covering the full system: feature flows, architecture, ADRs, runbooks, integration references, API endpoints, socket events, contributing conventions, and security policies.
- New root README — feature tour, quick-start, Mermaid system diagram, documentation map, tech stack, honest status notes.
- 6 Architecture Decision Records (ADRs) documenting major design choices: ADRs for the use of ADRs, MediaSoup-as-primary / LiveKit-dormant rationale, the Sept-2025 LiveKit dual-stack rollback, chat-as-separate-microservice rationale, Backblaze B2 over direct AWS S3, and whisper.cpp over cloud STT.
- 7 Mermaid diagrams: system architecture, streaming-stack data flow (×3), data-model ER, deployment topology, stream-takeover sequence, plus 7 auth-flow sequence diagrams in `/docs/security/auth-flows.md`.
- Five operations runbooks: stream-stuck, livekit-disconnect, recording-upload-failed, viewbot-fleet-misbehaving, secret-rotation.
- `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `SECURITY.md`, this changelog, `CODEOWNERS`.
- `.github/` templates: issue templates (bug, feature), pull request template (with doc-update checkbox), CI workflow, Dependabot config.

### Changed
- 22 evergreen `.md` files migrated from repo root into `/docs/` (e.g. `ADMIN_PANEL.md` → `docs/features/admin-panel.md`).
- Repo root cleaned up: only `README.md`, `CONTRIBUTING.md`, `SECURITY.md`, `CHANGELOG.md`, `LICENSE`, `CLAUDE.md` allowed going forward.

### Archived (not removed — preserved for forensic value)
- 44 historical `.md` files moved to `/docs/archive/` under topical subdirectories (livekit, transcription, viewbot-fixes, av-sync, audio, points, soundboards, plans, browser, optimization, rollbacks, investigations, test-notes). Each carries a redirect banner pointing at the current state.

### Removed
- `client/README.md` (CRA boilerplate; superseded by the dev guide).
- Empty `server/docs/` directory.

### Verified (not changed, but ground-truthed)
- Transcription pipeline: `whisper.cpp` native binary is live. `openai-whisper` is a phantom dependency.
- ~~Primary streaming backend: MediaSoup. LiveKit is dormant infrastructure.~~ (Superseded by ADR-0008 — see Unreleased / Changed.)
- Points balance: `user_stats.points_balance` is authoritative (refactor was executed).
- Clips system: substantially implemented; live endpoint returns valid status.
- Account deletion: end-to-end wired with 24h confirm token + 15-day grace + 8-table hard purge.
- Strapi blog: server-side OG-meta injection only; React app oblivious.

## [0.1.0] - YYYY-MM-DD

Initial tagged release marker. Project predates structured versioning — `0.1.0` is a starting point for future release-tagging discipline rather than a complete description of what's in this version. See `git log` for the actual development history.
